هـ.
قوله: (فعلى هذا الخ) أقول : هذا مما يدل على أن مجرد طأطأة الرأس لا تكون ركوعاً وإلا لسموه ركوعاً واقتصروا على ذكر الإيماء للسجود فلا بد في الركوع من انحناء كما مر وإلا فهو إيماء قول المصنف : أومأ قاعداً قال في النهر : هذا أولى من قول بعضهم صلى قاعداً إذ يفترض عليه أن يقوم للقراءة فإذا جاء أوان الركوع والسجود أو ما قاعداً ا قلت : ومقتضاه افتراض التحريمة قائماً أيضاً ولم أر ما ذكره في شيء من الكتب التي عندي من فتاوى وشروح وغيرها، بل كلهم متفقون على سقوط ركنية القيام وأن شرعيته للتوصل إلى السجود على أن القعود قيام من وجه، ولذا جوزوا اقتداء الراكع الساجد بالقاعد. وممن عبر بقوله صلى قاعداً يومئ إيماء القدوري في المختصر وصاحب الهداية في كتابه الهداية وكتابه مختارات النوازل وهي عبارة الكرخي أيضاً كما في
لا تجوز صلاته لأن الإيماء للسجود جالساً أقرب إلى حقيقة السجود ا هـ. وأومأ بالهمز كذا في السراج الوهاج قوله : (ولو مرض في صلاته يتم بما قدر يعني قاعداً يركع ويسجد أو مومئاً إن تعذر أو مستلقياً إن لم يقدر لأنه بناء الأدنى على الأعلى فصار كالاقتداء وهذا هو المشهور. وعن أبي يوسف أنه إذا صار إلى حالة الإيماء يستقبل الصلاة لأن تحريمته انعقدت موجبة للركوع والسجود فلا تجوز ،بدونهما، ووجه المشهور أنه إذا بنى كان بعض الصلاة كاملاً وبعضها ناقصاً وإذا استقبل كانت كلها ناقصة فلأن يؤدي بعضها كاملاً أولى وهو الصحيح قوله : (ولو) صلى قاعداً يركع ويسجد فصح بني ولو كان مومياً لا) أي لو كان يصلي بالإيماء فصح لا يبني لأنه لا يجوز اقتداء الراكع بالمومئ فكذا البناء، ويجوز اقتداء القائم بالقاعد الذي يركع ويسجد خلافاً لمحمد كما سبق. قيد بكونه صلى بالإيماء لأنه لو كان افتتحها بالإيماء ثم قدر قبل أن يركع ويسجد بالإيماء جاز له أن يتمها لأنه لم يؤد ركناً بالإيماء وإنما هو مجرد تحريمة فلا يكون بناء القوي على الضعيف وأشار إلى أنه لو كان يومئ مضطجعاً ثم قدر على القعود ولم يقدر على الركوع والسجود فإنه يستأنف وهو المختار لأن حالة القعود أقوى فلا يجوز بناؤه على الضعيف.
قوله : ( وللمتطوع أن يتكئ على شيء إن أعيا) أي تعب لأنه عذر أطلق في الشيء فشمل العصا والحائط. وأشار إلى أن له أن يقعد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما لا يجوز له القعود إلا إذا عجز لما مر من قبل وقيد بقوله إن أعيا لأن الاتكاء مكروه بغير عذر لأنه إساءة في الأدب وفيه اختلاف المشايخ والصحيح كراهته من غير عذر وعدم كراهة القعود من غير عذر عنده قوله : (ولو صلى في فلك قاعداً بلا عذر صح) يعني صلى فرضاً قاعداً بلا عذر صحت عند أبي حنيفة وقد أساء كما في البدائع . وقالا : لا يجزئه إلا من علة لأن القيام مقدور عليه فلا يترك، وله أن الغالب فيها دوران الرأس وهو كالمحقق الآن أن القيام أفضل لأنه أبعد عن شبهة الخلاف والخروج أفضل إن أمكنه لأنه أمكن لقلبه والخلاف في غير المربوطة والمربوطة كالشط هو الصحيح . كذا في الهداية وهو مقيد بالمربوطة بالشط ، أما إذا كانت مربوطة في لجة البحر فالأصح إن كان الريح يحركها شديداً فهي كالسائرة وإلا فكالواقفة. ثم ظاهر الهداية والنهاية والاختيار جواز الصلاة في المربوطة في الشط مطلقاً. وفي الايضاح : فإن كانت موقوفة في ا الشط وهي على قرار الأرض
السراج، بل يلزم من كلامه أيضاً أن لا يسقط الركوع عنه إذ عجز عن السجود فقط لأنه يمكنه أداؤه قائماً كالقراءة مع أنه يسقط عنه كما مر عن البدائع. وبعد هذا فإن كان ما ذكره منقولاً فهو مقبول، وإن كان قاله قياساً على ما إذا قدر على بعض القيام حيث يلزمه وتلزمه القراءة فيه فالفرق جلي لا يخفى فليراجع قوله : (وأشار إلى أنه الخ) قال في النهر في هذه الإشارة نظر. قلت: يمكن تصحيحها بتقييد قوله ولو كان مومياً بالحال السابقة أي ولو كان يصلي قاعداً مومياً فتدبره قوله : (فإن
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Sick Person's Prayer. His heart and his eyebrow, and if bowing and prostration are impossible but standing is not, he gestures while sitting. If he falls ill during his prayer, he completes what he can. If he prays sitting, bowing and prostrating, then recovers, he builds (on what he did); but if he was gesturing, he does not. For the voluntary (prayer), he may lean on something if tired. The sick person is not obligated to count rak'ats or prostrations due to drowsiness that overcomes him. If he performs them with the prompting of another, it should suffice. His saying: (He did not gesture with his eye, heart, and eyebrow. Zufar said: He gestures with his eyebrow, if unable then with his eyes, if unable then with his heart. Al-Shafi'i said: With his eyes and heart. Al-Hasan said: With his eyebrows and heart, and he repeats if he recovers. The correct (view) of our school is based on the hadith of 'Imran and Ibn 'Umar: 'If he cannot gesture with his head, then Allah is more worthy of accepting his excuse.' And because the obligation of prostration is connected to the head, not the eye, heart, or eyebrow, so it is not transferred to them like the hand, and by analogy with fasting and Hajj where they are not transferred to the heart when unable. In the Fatwas of Qadikhan: The sick person, if unable to gesture, moves his head. From Abu Hanifa that he said: His prayer is valid. And Sheikh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: It is not valid because no action occurred from him. So on this basis, the reality of gesture is lowering the head. His saying: (If bowing and prostration are impossible but standing is not, he gestures while sitting) because the standing pillar is a means to prostration due to its ultimate glorification. If prostration does not follow, it is not a pillar, so he has a choice. The best is to gesture while sitting because it is more similar to prostration. The funeral prayer is not an exception because the standing is not waived there due to the waiving of prostration, since the funeral prayer is not a real prayer but a supplication. In al-Mujtaba: If he gestures for prostration while standing, it suffices him, and this is better and more analogical, just as if he gestured for bowing while sitting it is not valid according to the most correct view. And the apparent (position) of the school is the permissibility of gesturing for both while standing and sitting, as is not hidden. Al-Walwaliji mentioned in his Fatwas: A man with a wound – if he prays with gesture while standing his wound does not flow, but if he bows and prostrates his wound flows – he prays standing and gestures for bowing, then sits and gestures for prostration so that the prayer is performed with purity. If he does not do that and prays standing, gesturing like that, it is an ima (gesture). Qadikhan says that it implies that what is less than the majority, he is obligated to make it up if he is able, even by gesture. If he does not make it up, he is obligated to bequeath it. That is what the author researched, and there is nothing in their words that contradicts that. Rather it is... His saying: (Regarding 'on this basis' etc.) I say: This indicates that mere lowering of the head is not bowing, otherwise they would have called it bowing and confined themselves to mentioning gesture for prostration. So bowing requires bending as mentioned, otherwise it is gesture. The author's saying: 'He gestured while sitting' – al-Nahr said: This is better than someone saying 'He prays sitting' because it is obligatory for him to stand for recitation. When the time for bowing and prostration comes, he gestures while sitting. I say: Its implication is the assumption of the opening takbir while standing as well. I have not seen what he mentioned in any of the books I have from fatwas and commentaries and others. Rather, they all agree on the dropping of the obligation of standing and that its legislation is a means to prostration, and that sitting is a kind of standing in some respects. Therefore, they allowed the follower who bows and prostrates to follow the one who sits. Among those who expressed 'he prays sitting, gesturing' are al-Quduri in al-Mukhtasar and the author of al-Hidayah in his book al-Hidayah and his book Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, and it is also the expression of al-Karkhi as in... His prayer is not valid because gesturing for prostration while sitting is closer to the reality of prostration. And he gestured with a hamzah, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His saying: (If he falls ill during his prayer, he completes what he can) meaning sitting, bowing and prostrating, or gesturing if unable, or lying down if unable, because it is building the weaker on the stronger, so it becomes like following. This is the well-known view. From Abu Yusuf that when he reaches the state of gesture, he starts the prayer anew because his opening takbir was made binding for bowing and prostration, so it is not permissible without them. The basis of the well-known view is that if he builds, part of the prayer is complete and part deficient. If he starts anew, it is all deficient. So performing part completely is better, and that is correct. His saying: (If he prays sitting, bowing and prostrating, then recovers, he builds; but if he was gesturing, he does not) meaning if he was praying with gesture and recovers, he does not build because it is not permissible for someone who bows and prostrates to follow a gesturer, so likewise for building. It is permissible for a standing person to follow a sitting person who bows and prostrates, contrary to Muhammad as mentioned. It is conditioned that he was praying with gesture because if he opened with gesture and then became able before he performed any gesture for bowing and prostration, he is permitted to complete the prayer because he did not perform any pillar with gesture, only the opening takbir, so it is not building the strong on the weak. It indicates that if he was gesturing while lying down and then became able to sit but not to bow and prostrate, he starts anew, which is the chosen view because the sitting state is stronger, so building on the weak is not allowed. His saying: (For the voluntary, he may lean on something if tired) meaning fatigued, because it is an excuse. 'Something' is unrestricted, including a staff and wall. It indicates that he may also sit according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he may not sit unless unable, as mentioned before. He conditioned it with 'if tired' because leaning is disliked without excuse due to bad etiquette. There is disagreement among the scholars; the correct view is that it is disliked without excuse and sitting without excuse is not disliked according to him. His saying: (If he prays in a ship sitting without excuse, it is valid) means he prays an obligatory prayer sitting without excuse; it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, though he has done wrong as in al-Bada'i. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It does not suffice except due to a reason because standing is within ability so it is not abandoned. He (Abu Hanifa) says: The predominant (condition) on it (the ship) is dizziness of the head, so it is like verified now. Standing is better because it is further from the shade of disagreement. To go out (of the ship) is better if possible because it is easier for his heart. The disagreement is concerning the ship that is not tied; the tied one is like the shore, that is the correct view. Thus in al-Hidayah, and it is restricted to the tied at the shore. But if it is tied in the midst of the sea, the most correct is that if the wind moves it strongly, it is like the moving one; otherwise it is like the stationary. Then the apparent (view) of al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Ikhtiyar is the permissibility of prayer in the tied (ship) at the shore absolutely. In al-Idah: If it is stopped at the shore and it is on the ground... Al-Siraj, rather it also follows from his statement that bowing is not waived for the one who is unable to prostrate only because he can perform it standing like recitation, yet it is waived from him as mentioned from al-Bada'i. After this, if what he mentioned is transmitted, it is accepted. If he said it by analogy with the case when he is able to part of the standing where it is obligatory and recitation is obligatory, then the difference is clear. So let it be reviewed. His saying: (And he indicated that... etc.) Al-Nahr said regarding this indication: There is a consideration. I say: It can be corrected by restricting his saying 'even if he was gesturing' to the previous state, i.e., even if he was praying sitting, gesturing. So reflect on it. His saying: (Then...)
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a detailed commentary on the chapter of the sick person's prayer from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It covers multiple rulings: the primary method of gesture (إيماء) when unable to bow and prostrate is by lowering the head (طأطأة الرأس), not by eyes, heart, or eyebrow. The proof is the hadith 'If he cannot gesture with his head, Allah is more worthy of his excuse.' The text then addresses the scenario where one can stand but not bow/prostrate: he gestures while sitting. Standing is only a means to prostration; if prostration is not possible, standing is no longer obligatory. The commentary also discusses building on a prayer when condition changes: if a sick person recovers during prayer, he may continue if he was sitting and performing actual bowing/prostration, but not if he was merely gesturing. For voluntary prayers, leaning on something or sitting without excuse is discussed with differences among the founders. Finally, praying in a ship while sitting without excuse is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but the two disciples require an excuse. The passage ends with a discussion on the definition of gesture and additional fatwas.

Key Terms
الاتكاء (al-ittikā'): Leaning; in prayer, leaning on a wall, staff, etc. Ruling: makruh without excuse.
فلك (fulk): Ship; the chapter on prayer on a ship includes rulings based on its stability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi ruling on praying an obligatory prayer sitting without excuse on a ship that is tied at the shore (calm waters)?
A) Valid according to all Hanafi imams
B) Invalid according to all Hanafi imams
C) Valid according to Abu Hanifa, but not accepted by the Sahibayn
D) Valid only if the worshipper feels dizzy

Key Takeaway
For voluntary prayer, leaning or sitting without excuse is disliked or makruh; for ship prayer, the ruling depends on the ship's stability and the individual's condition, with a difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Building the Weaker on the Stronger: Completing Prayer During Illness
Ruling on building upon previous prayer when illness occurs mid-prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding completing prayer when illness occurs mid-prayer and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Even if you fall ill mid-prayer, you may complete it in the easiest posture; restarting is wasteful.

What happens if you begin praying with full ability but suddenly become too weak to continue? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses this exact scenario, revealing a subtle disagreement within the Hanafi school itself. The key is the concept of bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la—building the weaker upon the stronger—which the majority accepts, while Abu Yusuf insists on restarting once nodding is required. Let's break down the reasoning and identify the reliable ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the issue
A person begins prayer with full ability (standing, bowing, prostrating) but falls ill mid-prayer and can only perform nodding (ima') for the remaining actions. The question: can he continue or must he restart?
The scenario involves a change in ability during the prayer itself.
2
State the mashhur view and its proof
The famous position is that he completes the prayer in the easiest posture he can manage. The rationale is building the weaker upon the stronger, analogous to following an imam where partial participation is valid.
The analogy is to iqtida' (following an imam) where you build upon the imam's actions.
3
State Abu Yusuf's view and its proof
Abu Yusuf holds that once the person reaches the nodding stage, the prayer must be started over. His proof: the opening takbir obligated full bowing and prostration; without them, the prayer is invalid.
Abu Yusuf emphasizes the initial obligation (takbir) as requiring full rukn performance.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The mashhur view responds that building preserves some completeness (some parts perfect, some imperfect), whereas restarting makes the entire prayer imperfect. Performing some parts completely is better.
The principle of preservation of completeness (ikmal) is preferred.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical outcome
The author declares the mashhur view as correct (sahih), and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa. The practical difference: Abu Yusuf requires i'ada (restart), while the mashhur view permits completion without i'ada.
The tarjih is based on the stronger evidence and leniency for the sick.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو مرض في صلاته يتم بما قدر يعني قاعداً يركع ويسجد أو مومئاً إن تعذر أو مستلقياً إن لم يقدر لأنه بناء الأدنى على الأعلى فصار كالاقتداء وهذا هو المشهور. وعن أبي يوسف أنه إذا صار إلى حالة الإيماء يستقبل الصلاة لأن تحريمته انعقدت موجبة للركوع والسجود فلا تجوز، بدونهما، ووجه المشهور أنه إذا بنى كان بعض الصلاة كاملاً وبعضها ناقصاً وإذا استقبل كانت كلها ناقصة فلأن يؤدي بعضها كاملاً أولى وهو الصحيح قوله : (ولو) صلى قاعداً يركع ويسجد فصح بني ولو كان مومياً لا) أي لو كان يصلي بالإيماء فصح لا يبني لأنه لا يجوز اقتداء الراكع بالمومئ فكذا البناء، ويجوز اقتداء القائم بالقاعد الذي يركع ويسجد خلافاً لمحمد كما سبق. قيد بكونه صلى بالإيماء لأنه لو كان افتتحها بالإيماء ثم قدر قبل أن يركع ويسجد بالإيماء جاز له أن يتمها لأنه لم يؤد ركناً بالإيماء وإنما هو مجرد تحريمة فلا يكون بناء القوي على الضعيف وأشار إلى أنه لو كان يومئ مضطجعاً ثم قدر على القعود ولم يقدر على الركوع والسجود فإنه يستأنف وهو المختار لأن حالة القعود أقوى فلا يجوز بناؤه على الضعيف.
His saying: (If he falls ill during his prayer, he completes it to the extent possible) meaning: sitting while bowing and prostrating, or nodding if that is not possible, or lying on his back if he is unable. This is because it is a building of the lesser upon the greater, so it becomes like following (an imam). This is the famous position. From Abu Yusuf: when he reaches the state of nodding, he must start the prayer over, because his opening takbir was concluded requiring bowing and prostration, so it is not valid without them. The basis of the famous position: if he builds, some parts of his prayer are complete and some incomplete; if he starts over, all of it is incomplete. So performing some parts completely is better, and that is correct. His saying: (If he prays sitting while bowing and prostrating, then recovers, he builds; but if he was nodding, he does not build) i.e., if he was praying by nodding and recovers, he does not build upon it, because it is impermissible for one who bows to follow one who nods, and likewise for building. It is permissible for one who stands to follow one who sits and bows/prostrates, contrary to Muhammad as previously mentioned. He restricted it to having prayed by nodding, because if he had started with nodding and then recovered before performing any bowing or prostration by nodding, he is allowed to complete it, because he did not perform any integral by nodding; it was merely the opening takbir, so there is no building of the strong upon the weak. And he indicated that if he was nodding while lying down and then became able to sit but not to bow and prostrate, then he must restart, and that is the chosen view, because the sitting state is stronger, so it is not permissible to build the stronger upon the weaker.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh discusses the ruling for someone who falls ill during an obligatory prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the famous (mashhur) position that the person should complete the prayer to the extent possible, whether sitting, nodding, or lying down, because it is like building a weaker part upon a stronger part, similar to following an imam. Abu Yusuf disagrees: once the person reaches nodding, he must restart because the opening takbir obligated full bowing and prostration. The mashhur view is preferred because it preserves some completeness. The text also distinguishes between starting with nodding and then recovering before performing any rukn by nodding (then he may continue), versus recovering after having nodded (then he must restart). If one was nodding lying down and then becomes able to sit but not bow/prostrate, he must restart, as sitting is stronger.

Key Terms
بناء الأدنى على الأعلى (bina' al-adna 'ala al-a'la): Performing the weaker part of prayer (e.g., nodding) after having performed a stronger part (standing, bowing), akin to following an imam.
إيماء (ima'): Nodding with the head for bowing and prostration when unable to perform them physically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mashhur view, if someone falls ill during prayer and can only nod, should he:
A) Restart the prayer from the beginning
B) Complete the prayer with nodding
C) Wait until recovery and then continue
D) Perform qada later

Key Takeaway
When illness strikes mid-prayer, the mashhur Hanafi view allows building the weaker part upon the stronger, thus completing the prayer rather than restarting.

Leaning and Sitting in Voluntary Prayer
Ruling on leaning and sitting in nafl prayer with excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on leaning and sitting during nafl prayer and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Leaning in nafl prayer is allowed only with excuse; sitting is allowed without excuse according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn require inability.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rules for the mutatawwi' who becomes tired. The key rulings hinge on the presence or absence of an excuse, and there is an intra-madhhab difference regarding sitting without excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine whether the mutatawwi' is leaning on something or sitting. Note that leaning is allowed only when tired (excused).
2
State the condition for permissibility
Leaning is permissible only with an excuse (tiredness). Without excuse, it is makruh. Sitting is permissible without excuse according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.
The difference stems from whether sitting is considered a deviation from the norm of standing.
3
Acknowledge the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa permits sitting without excuse in nafl, while the Sahibayn require the worshipper to be unable to stand. This is a legitimate difference within the school.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that sitting without excuse is disliked, as per the later scholars.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
If a person is tired, leaning is fine. If not tired, leaning is makruh. Sitting without excuse: Abu Hanifa says valid but not disliked, but the later view holds it makruh.
The text says 'وعدم كراهة القعود من غير عذر عنده' meaning it is not disliked according to him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وللمتطوع أن يتكئ على شيء إن أعيا) أي تعب لأنه عذر أطلق في الشيء فشمل العصا والحائط. وأشار إلى أن له أن يقعد أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما لا يجوز له القعود إلا إذا عجز لما مر من قبل وقيد بقوله إن أعيا لأن الاتكاء مكروه بغير عذر لأنه إساءة في الأدب وفيه اختلاف المشايخ والصحيح كراهته من غير عذر وعدم كراهة القعود من غير عذر عنده قوله : (ولو صلى في فلك قاعداً بلا عذر صح) يعني صلى فرضاً قاعداً بلا عذر صحت عند أبي حنيفة وقد أساء كما في البدائع . وقالا : لا يجزئه إلا من علة لأن القيام مقدور عليه فلا يترك، وله أن الغالب فيها دوران الرأس وهو كالمحقق الآن أن القيام أفضل لأنه أبعد عن شبهة الخلاف والخروج أفضل إن أمكنه لأنه أمكن لقلبه والخلاف في غير المربوطة والمربوطة كالشط هو الصحيح . كذا في الهداية وهو مقيد بالمربوطة بالشط ، أما إذا كانت مربوطة في لجة البحر فالأصح إن كان الريح يحركها شديداً فهي كالسائرة وإلا فكالواقفة.
His saying: (And for the voluntary worshipper, he may lean on something if he becomes tired) i.e., exhausted, because it is an excuse. He made it general regarding the thing, so it includes a stick and a wall. And he indicated that he may also sit according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), sitting is not permissible except if he is unable, as previously. And he restricted it with 'if he becomes tired' because leaning is disliked without an excuse, because it is bad manners. There is difference among the mashayikh; the correct view is that it is disliked without excuse, and sitting without excuse is not disliked according to him. His saying: (And if he prays in a boat sitting without excuse, it is valid) means he prays obligatory prayer sitting without excuse; it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, though he has done wrong, as in al-Bada'i'. The two (Sahibayn) say: it does not suffice him except due to a cause, because standing is within his ability so it should not be abandoned. And he (Abu Hanifa) argued that dizziness usually occurs in it (the boat), and it is as if now established that standing is better because it is further from the shadow of disagreement, and exiting (the boat) is better if possible because it is more calming for the heart. The disagreement is regarding the unmored (boat); the moored (boat) is like the bank, that is correct. Thus in al-Hidayah, and it is restricted to the one moored at the bank. However, if it is moored in the open sea, the more correct view is that if the wind moves it strongly, it is like a moving boat; otherwise it is like a stationary one.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First, for voluntary prayers, the worshipper may lean on something if tired; this is an excuse. If not tired, leaning is disliked. According to Abu Hanifa, he may also sit without excuse, but the Sahibayn require inability. Second, regarding praying obligatory prayer sitting in a boat without excuse: Abu Hanifa considers it valid but sinful; the Sahibayn require a valid excuse (like dizziness). Abu Hanifa's reasoning: dizziness is common in boats, so it is effectively an excuse. The dispute applies only to unmored boats; for a boat moored at the bank, it is like land. For boats moored in the open sea, the ruling depends on movement.

Key Terms
اتكاء (ittika'): Leaning on an object for support during prayer.
المتطوع (al-mutatawwi'): One performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a voluntary worshipper sitting without excuse according to the Sahibayn?
A) Permissible, not disliked
B) Not permissible unless unable
C) Valid but sinful
D) Invalid

Key Takeaway
Leaning in nafl requires an excuse; sitting in nafl is subject to ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn, with the mufta bihi being dislike without excuse.

Praying Obligatory Prayer Sitting in a Boat Without Excuse
Ruling on sitting in fard prayer in a boat without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on sitting during obligatory prayer in a boat and evaluate the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa validates sitting in a boat due to common dizziness; Sahibayn require an actual excuse.

This passage addresses a unique scenario: praying obligatory prayer sitting in a boat without a medical excuse. The ruling involves an important principle about the effect of the environment on the ability to stand, and the distinction between moored and unmored boats.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage refers to a person praying fard (obligatory) prayer sitting in a boat without a physical excuse (like illness).
The boat is not moored; the ruling for moored boats is different.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer is valid but sinful (asaa'a), because he considers that dizziness is common in boats and thus it is as if there is an excuse.
Abu Hanifa's reasoning: 'al-ghalib fiha dawaran al-ra's' – dizziness is prevalent.
3
State Sahibayn's ruling
The Sahibayn say the prayer is not valid unless there is a genuine cause (illness). Standing is possible, so it should not be abandoned.
They require inability to stand, not mere inconvenience.
4
Understand the moored/unmored distinction
The disagreement applies only to unmored (moving) boats. If the boat is moored at the bank, it is like praying on land – standing is required. If moored in the open sea, the ruling depends on movement: if strongly moved by wind, it is like a moving boat; otherwise, it is like stationary.
This is a detailed mas'ala showing the precision of Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note the preferred view
The text indicates that standing is better to avoid the shadow of disagreement. Exiting the boat to pray on land is even better if possible.
The mufta bihi is that sitting without excuse is not sufficient, following the Sahibayn for caution.

Praying Obligatory Salah Sitting in a Boat Without Excuse: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting in obligatory prayer aboard a boat without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on praying obligatory salah sitting in a boat without excuse and apply the distinctions between moored and unmored boats.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa allows sitting without excuse; Sahibayn require an excuse; dispute only for unmored boats.

Imagine you are on a boat that is gently moving. You need to pray the obligatory salah but feel slightly dizzy when standing. Can you pray sitting? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer: Abu Hanifa allows it (though with dislike), while his two main disciples require a valid excuse. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the key condition—whether the boat is moored or moving—that determines the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Understand that the passage deals with praying obligatory salah sitting in a boat without a legitimate excuse. Note Abu Hanifa's view: valid but sinful (sahih ma'a al-karahah), and the Sahibayn's view: invalid unless there is a cause.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; both sides are recorded in the school.
2
State Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that dizziness is common on boats, so sitting is effectively justified even without a specific excuse. This makes the prayer valid, though he acknowledges it is better to stand or exit.
The argument relies on the prevalence of dizziness (ghalabat dawar al-ra's).
3
State the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that standing is possible, so it cannot be abandoned without a valid excuse. They consider the prayer invalid if no cause exists.
Their position is based on the general principle that an obligatory act (qiyam) cannot be omitted without excuse.
4
Analyse the hanafi response and limitation
The text then qualifies the dispute: it only applies to unmored boats (ghayr al-marbutah). For a boat moored at the bank or settled on the ground, it is like land, and standing is required. This resolution narrows the practical scope of the difference.
Also, if the boat is moored in open sea and moved strongly by wind, it is considered like a moving boat.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and practical application
If someone prays sitting without excuse on an unmored boat, Abu Hanifa's view leads to validity (though the person is sinful), while the Sahibayn require repetition. The mufta bihi (operative view) may lean toward the Sahibayn for caution.
The passage also discusses following an imam in another boat and facing qibla, but the core dispute is the central legal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو صلى في فلك قاعداً بلا عذر صح) يعني صلى فرضاً قاعداً بلا عذر صحت عند أبي حنيفة وقد أساء كما في البدائع . وقالا : لا يجزئه إلا من علة لأن القيام مقدور عليه فلا يترك، وله أن الغالب فيها دوران الرأس وهو كالمحقق الآن أن القيام أفضل لأنه أبعد عن شبهة الخلاف والخروج أفضل إن أمكنه لأنه أمكن لقلبه والخلاف في غير المربوطة والمربوطة كالشط هو الصحيح . كذا في الهداية وهو مقيد بالمربوطة بالشط ، أما إذا كانت مربوطة في لجة البحر فالأصح إن كان الريح يحركها شديداً فهي كالسائرة وإلا فكالواقفة. ثم ظاهر الهداية والنهاية والاختيار جواز الصلاة في المربوطة في الشط مطلقاً. وفي الايضاح : فإن كانت موقوفة في الشط وهي على قرار الأرض فصلي قائماً جاز لأنها إذا استقرت على الأرض فحكمها حكم الأرض، فإن كانت مربوطة ويمكنه الخروج لم تجز الصلاة فيها لأنها إذا لم تستقر فهي كالدابة بخلاف ما إذا استقرت فإنها حينئذ كالسرير. واختاره في المحيط والبدائع. وفي الخلاصة : وأجمعوا أنه لو كان بحالة يدور رأسه لو قام تجوز الصلاة فيها قاعداً وأراد بالصلاة قاعداً أن تكون بركوع وسجود لأنها لو كانت بالإيماء لا تجوز اتفاقاً لأنه لا عذر وأطلقها فشمل ما إذا كان منفرداً أو بجماعة فلو اقتدى به رجل في سفينة أخرى، فإن كانت السفينتان مقرونتين جاز لأنهما بالاقتران صارتا كشيء واحد، وإن كانتا منفصلتين لم يجز لأن تخلل ما بينهما بمنزلة النهر وذلك يمنع صحة الاقتداء. وإن كان الإمام في سفينة والمقتدون على الجد والسفينة واقفة. فإن كان بينه وبينهم طريق أو مقدار نهر عظيم لم يصح اقتداؤهم به لأن الطريق ومثل هذا النهر يمنعان صحة الاقتداء. ومن وقف على أطلال السفينة يقتدي بالإمام في السفينة صح اقتداؤه إلا أن يكون أمام الإمام لأن السفينة كالبيت واقتداء الواقف على السطح بمن هو في البيت صحيح إذا لم يكن أمام الإمام، ولا يخفى عليه حاله كذا ههنا. كذا في البدائع . وقيد بترك القيام لأنه لو ترك استقبال وجهه إلى القبلة وهو قادر عليه لا يجزئه في قولهم جميعاً فعليهم أن يستقبلوا بوجههم القبلة كلما دارت السفينة يحول وجهه إليها. كذا في الأسبيجابي.
His saying: (And if he prays in a boat sitting without excuse, it is valid) means he prays an obligatory prayer sitting without excuse; it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, and he has done wrong, as in al-Bada'i'. The two (Sahibayn) say: it does not suffice him except due to a cause, because standing is within his ability so it should not be abandoned. And he (Abu Hanifa) argued that dizziness usually occurs in it, and it is as if now it is established that standing is better because it is further from the shadow of disagreement, and exiting (the boat) is better if possible because it is more calming for the heart. The disagreement is regarding the unmored (boat); the moored is like the bank, that is correct. Thus in al-Hidayah, and it is restricted to the one moored at the bank. However, if it is moored in the open sea, the more correct view is that if the wind moves it strongly, it is like a moving boat; otherwise it is like a stationary one. Then apparent from al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Ikhtiyar is the permissibility of praying in a boat moored at the bank absolutely. In al-Idah: if it is stopped at the bank and it is on the ground, then praying standing is permissible because if it is settled on the ground, its ruling is that of the ground. If it is moored and he can exit, prayer is not permissible in it because if it is not settled, it is like an animal, unlike when it is settled, for then it is like a bed. And al-Muhit and al-Bada'i' chose this. In al-Khulasah: they all agreed that if he is in a state where his head would spin if he stood, then it is permissible to pray sitting, and by 'praying sitting' they mean with bowing and prostration, because if it were by nodding, it would not be permissible by agreement, as there is no excuse. And he made it general, including whether he is alone or in congregation. So if a man follows him in another boat: if the two boats are joined, it is permissible because they become like one thing; if they are separate, it is not permissible because the space between them is like a river which prevents the validity of following. And if the imam is in a boat and the followers are on the bank (jid) and the boat is stationary: if there is between him and them a road or the distance of a large river, following them is not valid because the road and such river prevent the validity of following. And one who stands on the ruins of a boat following an imam in the boat, his following is valid unless he is in front of the imam, because the boat is like a house, and following of one standing on the roof to one inside the house is valid if he is not in front of the imam and his condition is not hidden from him. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And he restricted it to leaving standing, because if he leaves facing the qibla while being able to do so, it does not suffice him in all their views. So they must face the qibla with their faces every time the boat turns, turning his face towards it. Thus in al-Ispijabi.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This lengthy passage continues the discussion of praying in a boat. The core ruling: according to Abu Hanifa, praying obligatory prayer sitting without excuse is valid but sinful (makruh tanzihi). The Sahibayn require a valid excuse such as dizziness. The dispute only applies to unmored boats; for a boat moored at the bank, it is like land. If moored in open sea, the ruling depends on movement. The text then discusses following an imam in another boat: permissible if the boats are joined, otherwise not. If the imam is on a boat and followers on the bank, it is valid only if there is no road or large river between them. Also, one can follow from the ruins of a boat similar to following from a roof. Finally, facing the qibla is essential; if the boat turns, they must turn their faces.

Key Terms
فلك (falk): Ship or boat.
مربوطة (marbutah): A boat moored to the shore or anchored.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, praying the obligatory prayer sitting in a boat without excuse is:
A) Valid but disliked
B) Invalid unless there is a reason
C) Better than standing
D) Permissible unconditionally

Key Takeaway
The validity of praying obligatory salah sitting in a boat without excuse is disputed within the Hanafi school; Abu Hanifa allows it (with karahah), while the Sahibayn require an excuse, and the dispute only applies to unmored boats.

Qada for Insanity or Fainting: The Five-Prayer Limit
Ruling with istihsan and comparison to sleep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for prayers missed during insanity/fainting and explain the istihsan reasoning that overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Insanity/fainting for ≤5 prayers requires qada; beyond that, hardship exempts.

What happens to missed prayers when a person is insane or unconscious for days? The Hanafi school balances obligation and hardship: a short period (up to five prayers) must be made up, but a longer period does not. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than strict qiyas, and this lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling from the matn: 'Who becomes insane or unconscious for five prayers, he makes them up; if more, no.' Note the threshold: five prayers (roughly 24 hours).
The ruling is clear from the text: up to five prayers wajib, beyond not.
2
Understand the qiyas that would apply
The qiyas (analogy) would be: if unconsciousness covers a complete prayer time, no qada is needed because the person was genuinely unable (عاجز). But the Hanafi school does not adopt this absolute qiyas.
Qiyas would exempt all missed prayers entirely.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
The text says 'This is istihsan.' The basis: if the period is short, few prayers are missed – making them up is easy. If the period is long, many prayers accumulate, causing hardship (حرج). Istihsan avoids that hardship by limiting qada to five prayers.
Istihsan is a stronger argument because it considers practical hardship.
4
Compare with sleep
The text contrasts insanity/unconsciousness with sleep: sleep does not exempt qada even if longer than a day, because sleep does not normally extend that long, so hardship is less. This reinforces the rationale.
The distinction is based on typical duration and resulting hardship.
5
Note the exception for intention
The text mentions that obligation remains in the dhimmah even during insanity. For example, one who intended to fast and then became insane does not have to make up that day – because the intention already existed, and insanity during the act does not invalidate the reward.
This shows that insanity only affects the condition of intention for new obligations, not existing ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن جن أو أغمي عليه خمس صلوات قضى ولو أكثر لا) وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن لا قضاء عليه إذا استوعب الإغماء وقت صلاة كاملة لتحقق العجز. وجه الاستحسان أن المدة إذا طالت كثرت الفوائت فيحرج في الأداء وإذا قصرت قلت : فلا خرج والكثير أن يزيد على يوم وليلة لأنه يدخل في حد التكرار والجنون كالإغماء على الصحيح. وفي تحرير الأصول: الجنون ينافي شرط العبادات وهي النية فلا تجب مع للحرج وما لا يمتد طارئاً جعل كالنوم من حيث إنه عارض يمنع فهم الخطاب زال قبل الامتداد ولأنه لا ينفي أصل الوجوب إذ هو : بالذمة له حتى ورث وملك وكان أهلاً وهي للثواب كأن نوى صوم الغد فجن فيه ممسكاً كله فلا يقضي لو أفاق بعده ا هـ . بالجنون والإغماء لأن النوم لا يسقط مطلقاً حتى لو نام أكثر من يوم وليلة يقضي لأن النوم مما لا يمتد يوماً وليلة غالباً فلا يحرج في القضاء بخلاف الإغماء لأن مما يمتد عادة. وقيده
His saying: (And whoever becomes insane or unconscious for five prayers, he makes them up; if more, he does not). This is istihsan, and the qiyas is that he does not make up if unconsciousness covers a complete prayer time, because actual inability. The basis of istihsan: if the duration is long, the missed prayers increase, leading to hardship in performance; if short, they are few, so no hardship. The large amount is more than a day and night, because it enters the limit of repetition. Insanity is like unconsciousness according to the correct view. In Tahrir al-Usul: Insanity negates the condition of worship, which is intention, so they are not obligatory due to hardship. What does not extend temporarily is made like sleep in that it is a temporary barrier preventing understanding of the address, ceasing before extension. And because it does not negate the basis of obligation, for the obligation remains in the dhimmah, so he inherits and owns and is eligible, and it is for reward. For example, if he intended to fast tomorrow and then became insane while abstaining the whole day, he does not make it up if he regains consciousness after. This (the ruling) is for insanity and unconsciousness, because sleep does not exempt absolutely; even if he sleeps more than a day and night, he makes up, because sleep does not typically extend a day and night, so there is no hardship in making up, unlike unconsciousness, because it typically extends. And it is restricted by...
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on making up prayers missed due to insanity or unconsciousness. According to istihsan (preference), if the period covers five prayers or less (i.e., up to approximately 24 hours), the prayers must be made up. If it covers more than that, no qada is required. The qiyas would be that no qada is required at all if a complete prayer time is covered, because one is unable. But istihsan avoids hardship: if the period is long, making up many prayers would cause hardship. The text compares with sleep: sleep does not exempt one from making up missed prayers, even if longer than a day, because sleep does not typically extend that long and thus hardship is less. Insanity and unconsciousness typically extend longer, so the exemption applies. The text also cites Tahrir al-Usul regarding intention being a condition and how insanity negates it, but obligation remains in the dhimmah.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas for a stronger reason (e.g., removing hardship).
الجنون (al-junun): Insanity that negates legal capacity (taklif) for worship requiring intention.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on shared illa.
الحرج (al-haraj): Hardship or difficulty that the Shari'ah aims to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a person who remains unconscious for three days must make up how many prayers?
A) All 15 prayers
B) The first 5 prayers only
C) None
D) The first 24 hours worth (5 prayers) plus any prayers missed before unconsciousness

Key Takeaway
For insanity or unconsciousness, missed prayers are wajib only up to the first five (≈24 hours); beyond that, no qada is required, based on istihsan to avoid hardship.

Prayer in a Ship and Following the Imam
Rulings on prayer in a ship and following the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on prayer in a ship, including conditions for sitting, following an imam, and facing the qibla.

Core Idea
Prayer in a ship is valid when stable; following an imam requires connection; always face the qibla when the ship turns.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings of prayer in a ship. It clarifies when one may sit, the conditions for following an imam in another ship or from the shore, and the obligation to face the qibla even as the ship moves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The text states that praying in a ship sitting without an excuse is valid. Determine what this implies about the legal nature of the ship.
The default is that prayer should be performed standing, but sitting is excused due to the context.
2
Analyze the condition of stability
The text distinguishes between a ship that is stable (like land) and one that is tied but unstable (like an animal). Understand how stability affects validity.
If the ship is tied and one can exit, prayer is invalid because it is like a moving animal.
3
Examine the exception for dizziness
The scholars agree that if standing causes dizziness, sitting with full ruku' and sujud is allowed, even without a valid excuse otherwise.
This exception covers both individual and congregational prayer.
4
Evaluate the rules for following an imam
When following an imam in another ship, the ships must be connected. When on shore, there must be no road or large river between the imam and followers.
The analogy to a house and roof is used for the case of standing on the ruins of a ship.
5
Apply the qibla requirement
The text emphasizes that one must face the qibla; if the ship turns, one must turn his face accordingly.
Failure to do so while able invalidates the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة المريض
يتكيء على شيء إن أعيا ولو صلى في فلك قاعداً بلا عذر صح
فصلي قائماً جاز لأنها إذا استقرت على الأرض فحكمها حكم الأرض، فإن كانت مربوطة ويمكنه الخروج لم تجز الصلاة فيها لأنها إذا لم تستقر فهي كالدابة بخلاف ما إذا استقرت فإنها حينئذ كالسرير. واختاره في المحيط والبدائع. وفي الخلاصة : وأجمعوا أنه لو كان بحالة يدور رأسه لو قام تجوز الصلاة فيها قاعداً وأراد بالصلاة قاعداً أن تكون بركوع وسجود لأنها لو كانت بالإيماء لا تجوز اتفاقاً لأنه لا عذر وأطلقها فشمل ما إذا كان منفرداً أو بجماعة فلو اقتدى به رجل في سفينة أخرى، فإن كانت السفينتان مقرونتين جاز لأنهما بالاقتران صارتا كشيء واحد، وإن كانتا منفصلتين لم يجز لأن تخلل ما بينهما بمنزلة النهر وذلك يمنع صحة الاقتداء. وإن كان الإمام في سفينة والمقتدون على الجد والسفينة واقفة. فإن كان بينه وبينهم طريق أو مقدار نهر عظيم لم يصح اقتداؤهم به لأن الطريق ومثل هذا النهر يمنعان صحة الاقتداء. ومن وقف على أطلال السفينة يقتدي بالإمام في السفينة صح اقتداؤه إلا أن يكون أمام الإمام لأن السفينة كالبيت واقتداء الواقف على السطح بمن هو في البيت صحيح إذا لم يكن أمام الإمام، ولا يخفى عليه حاله كذا ههنا. كذا في البدائع . وقيد بترك القيام لأنه لو ترك استقبال وجهه إلى القبلة وهو قادر عليه لا يجزئه في قولهم جميعاً فعليهم أن يستقبلوا بوجههم القبلة كلما دارت السفينة يحول وجهه إليها. كذا في الأسبيجابي .
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Sick Person's Prayer. He may lean on something if he becomes tired, and if he prays in a ship sitting without an excuse, it is valid. He should pray standing if possible, because when it (the ship) is stable on land, its ruling is the ruling of land. If it is tied and he can exit, prayer in it is not valid because when it is not stable, it is like an animal; contrary to when it is stable, for then it is like a bed. This is chosen in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i'. In al-Khulasa: And they agreed that if he is in a condition that his head spins if he stands, it is permissible to pray in it sitting. By 'praying sitting' is intended with bowing and prostration, because if it were with gestures, it is not permissible by agreement, because there is no excuse. And it (the statement) is general, so it includes whether he is alone or in a congregation. If a man follows him (the imam) in another ship, and the two ships are connected, it is permissible because by being connected they become like one thing. If they are separate, it is not permissible because what lies between them is like a river, and that prevents the validity of following. If the imam is in a ship and the followers are on the shore and the ship is stationary, and between him and them is a road or the distance of a great river, their following him is not valid because the road and such a river prevent the validity of following. Whoever stands on the ruins of a ship following the imam in the ship, his following is valid unless he is in front of the imam, because the ship is like a house, and the following of one standing on the roof (following) someone in the house is valid if he is not in front of the imam and his state is not hidden from him. Similarly here. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And it is restricted by leaving standing, because if he leaves facing his face to the qibla while able to do so, it does not suffice him in all their statements. So they must face their faces to the qibla; whenever the ship turns, he turns his face towards it. Thus in al-Asbijabi.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings regarding prayer in a ship from the chapter on the sick person's prayer. The author first states the matn: a sick person may lean on something if fatigued, and praying in a ship sitting without an excuse is valid. The commentary explains that if the ship is stationary on land, it is treated as land, so standing is better. If the ship is tied to land and one can exit, prayer inside is invalid because it is mobile like an animal. But if it is anchored and stable, it is like a bed and prayer is valid. The scholars agreed that if standing causes dizziness, one may pray sitting with full ruku' and sujud, not just gestures, even without a valid excuse. This includes both individual and congregational prayer. Regarding following an imam in another ship: if the two ships are connected (e.g., tied together), it is valid because they form one unit; if separated by water, it is like a river and invalid. If the imam is on a stationary ship and the followers are on the shore, their following is valid only if there is no road or large river between them; otherwise, it is invalid. One standing on the ruins of a ship can follow the imam inside the ship unless he is in front of the imam, analogously to a person on a roof following someone inside a house. The ruling requires facing the qibla; if the ship turns, one must turn his face to the qibla. This is a continuous discussion of various conditions.

Key Terms
فلك (fulk): A ship or boat on water
اقتداء (iqtida'): The act of following an imam in congregational prayer
الجد (al-jadd): The bank or shore of a river

Key Takeaway
Prayer in a ship is valid under specific stability conditions; following an imam requires physical connection or absence of major obstacles; facing the qibla is obligatory at all times.

Making Up Missed Prayers Due to Insanity or Unconsciousness: Hanafi Ruling and Internal Disputes
Intra-Hanafi dispute with istihsan reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up prayers missed due to insanity or unconsciousness, explain the istihsan reasoning that limits the obligation to five or fewer prayers, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the threshold and treatment of original versus accidental insanity.

Core Idea
The obligation to make up missed prayers is waived if the period exceeds five prayers, based on istihsan to avoid hardship.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a classic Hanafi problem: what happens to missed prayers when a person is incapacitated by insanity or unconsciousness? The matn states a clear rule—make up five or fewer, but not more—and the commentary unpacks the reasoning (istihsan overriding qiyas) and the internal disagreements among the three imams. As you work through this lesson, you will learn not only the settled ruling but also the legal principles that shape the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn ruling and its immediate exception
Locate the statement: 'Whoever becomes insane or unconscious for five prayers must make them up; if more, no.' This is the core ruling. Note that it applies to both insanity and unconsciousness.
The 'five prayers' are measured as missed prayer times, not necessarily consecutive.
2
Understand the istihsan reasoning that justifies the ruling
The commentator explains that strict analogy (qiyas) would require no makeup at all because the person was completely unable. But istihsan (juridical preference) creates a distinction: a short period (≤5 prayers) involves little hardship, so makeup is required; a long period would cause excessive hardship, so it is waived.
This is a classic example of istihsan overriding qiyas to avoid hardship (haraj).
3
Analyze the internal dispute on the threshold for 'more than five'
The text presents two views on what constitutes 'more': Muhammad and one narration of Abu Hanifa say it means six or more prayers; Abu Yusuf says it means more than a day and night (by hours). Trace the practical consequence: if someone becomes unconscious before noon and recovers the next day after noon, Abu Yusuf would not require makeup (since more than 24 hours), while Muhammad would require it if he recovers before Zuhr time ends.
The text declares Muhammad's view as 'al-ashah' (most correct).
4
Distinguish the treatment of original vs. accidental insanity
Muhammad treats both original insanity (since birth, reaching puberty insane) and accidental insanity equally: if the period is long, makeup is waived; if short, required. Abu Yusuf treats original insanity like childhood: no makeup at all, even for a short period, because the person was never addressed by the commands.
Abu Hanifa's view on original insanity is not explicitly stated here; the commentary focuses on the other two.
5
Examine the effect of the cause of the condition
The passage notes that if the condition was caused by a sin (e.g., alcohol), makeup is always required, even if lengthy, by consensus. If caused by a permissible means (e.g., medicinal henbane), Abu Hanifa still requires makeup (since the original text refers only to 'heavenly afflictions'), while Muhammad waives it if it extends. This shows that the ruling can vary based on the cause.
This is a key principle: an excuse arising from disobedience does not lighten the obligation.

الخ) أقول : هذا الكلام هنا غير محرر لأنه بعد ما ذكره من التعليل لا ورود لما ذكر أصلاً. نعم يرد ظاهراً ما إذا كان بسبب فزع من سبع أو خوف من عدو لأنه يتوهم فيه أنه لم يحصل بآفة سماوية فلا يكون مما ورد فيه النص، فيجاب بالمنع لأن سببه القريب ضعف القلب وهو مرض ليس من صنع العباد، فالأحسن في التعبير ما ذكره الشارح الزيلعي حيث ذكر أولاً ما إذا زال عقله بالخمر أو بالبنج وعلل لهما، ثم ذكره مسألة الفزع والخوف وعلل لها فكان ذكرها أخيراً بمنزلة جواب عن سؤال مقدر وهو ترتيب حسن قوله : فعند أبي يوسف لا يجب القضاء قاله الرملي. أقول : وبه يعلم أن الوتر لا يجب ا.هـ. والظاهر أن قوله لا يجب محرف عن لا يحسب بالسين قبل الموحدة أي لا يعد
من الست .
The extended one absolutely. His statement: (And whoever becomes insane or unconscious for five prayers must make them up; if more, no.) This is istihsan, while qiyas is that he does not have to make up if unconsciousness covers a complete prayer time, due to actual inability. The reasoning for istihsan is: if the period is long, many prayers are missed, causing hardship in performing them; if short, few are missed, so no hardship. And 'much' means more than a day and night, because it enters the limit of repetition. Insanity is like unconsciousness according to the correct view. In Tahrir al-Usul: Insanity contradicts the condition of acts of worship, which is intention, so it is not obligatory due to hardship. And what does not extend as an incidental occurrence is treated like sleep in that it is an obstacle that prevents understanding of address, ceasing before extension; and because it does not negate the original obligation, as it is incumbent on the liability until he inherits and owns and was qualified, and it is for reward—like if one intends to fast tomorrow and then becomes insane while fasting the whole day, he does not have to make it up if he recovers afterwards—End. Regarding insanity and unconsciousness, because sleep does not drop the obligation absolutely; even if one sleeps more than a day and night, he must make up because sleep usually does not extend a day and night, so no hardship in making up, unlike unconsciousness because it normally extends. And it is restricted... (interrupted) ... 'Qayyada bi-tark al-qiyam' (He restricted by leaving standing) - corrected: 'kanat marbutatan wa yumkinuhu al-khuruj lam tujaz al-salat fiha' (if it is tied and he can exit, prayer in it is not valid) and accordingly, prayer should not be valid in it if it is moving with possibility of exiting to land; people are heedless of this issue. Thus in Sharh al-Munya. His statement: ('ala al-jadd) said al-Ramli: al-jadd is the bank of the river. End. Pronounced with kasr al-jim as in Ibn Amir Hajj 'ala al-Munya. His statement: (la tajib ma'a al-mumtad minhu mutlaqan) i.e., whether it is original or incidental after puberty. His statement: (illa annahu: yuraddu 'alayhi) (except that it is objected to him) regarding continuous unconsciousness, because if he becomes conscious during it, then it is considered: if his consciousness has a known time, like his illness is relieved at dawn for example, so he becomes conscious briefly then returns to unconsciousness, this consciousness is considered and nullifies the previous ruling of unconsciousness if it was less than a day and night; and if his consciousness has no known time but he suddenly becomes conscious and speaks like a healthy person then falls unconscious, this consciousness is not considered. It is absolute in unconsciousness and insanity, so it includes if it is due to fear from a wild animal or fear of an enemy; then makeup is not obligatory if it extends, by consensus, because the fear is due to weakness of the heart which is an illness. However, an objection arises if his mind is lost due to alcohol or unconsciousness due to drinking henbane or medicine; then indeed makeup is not waived in the first case even if lengthy, by agreement, because it came about through disobedience, so it does not cause leniency; hence his divorce is valid. It is also not waived in the second case according to Abu Hanifa, because the text (nass) came regarding unconsciousness caused by a heavenly affliction, so it does not apply to unconsciousness caused by human action, because if the excuse comes from a direction other than the one who has the right, it does not drop the right. Muhammad said: makeup is waived if it becomes many, because it came about through what is permissible. Thus in al-Muhit. And it includes if the insanity is original, like when one reaches puberty insane and then recovers; this is the saying of Muhammad, so to him, incidental and original are the same regarding waiving of makeup if many and not if few. Abu Yusuf said: original is like childhood, so no makeup absolutely. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And it is restricted to prayer in equating insanity to unconsciousness because there is a difference in fasting: if he becomes unconscious before Ramadan until the whole Ramadan passes then recovers, he must make up the Ramadan fast; if he becomes insane before Ramadan and recovers after Ramadan passes, he does not have to make up the fast, as will be explained by Allah's will. The apparent meaning of his speech is that the majority is in terms of prayers; the majority of five prayers is six or more, which is the saying of Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifa, and this is the most correct. According to Abu Yusuf, also a narration from him, the consideration is for increase in terms of hours; its benefit appears if one becomes unconscious before noon and recovers the next day after noon; according to Abu Yusuf, makeup is not obligatory; according to Muhammad, it is obligatory if he recovers before the time of Zuhr exits. And Allah Most High knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and destination.

(Etc.) I say: This discussion here is not precise because after what he mentioned of reasoning, there is no objection to what was mentioned at all. Yes, an objection apparently arises if it is due to fear from a wild animal or fear of an enemy, because it might be suspected that it did not occur through a heavenly affliction, thus not covered by the text. The answer is a denial, because its proximate cause is weakness of the heart, which is an illness, not from human action. The best expression is what the commentator al-Zayla'i mentioned: he first mentioned the case of loss of mind due to alcohol or henbane and gave the reasoning for both, then mentioned the case of fear and fright and gave the reasoning, so mentioning it last serves as an answer to an implicit question, which is a good order. His statement: 'According to Abu Yusuf, makeup is not obligatory' said al-Ramli. I say: And from this it is known that witr is not obligatory. End. And apparently the phrase 'la yajib' is corrupted from 'la yuhsab' with sin before ba', i.e., not counted among the six.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on making up missed prayers due to insanity or unconsciousness. The matn states that if one misses five prayers, he must make them up; if more, not. The commentator explains that this is istihsan (preference), whereas qiyas would require no makeup even for fewer, due to complete inability. The reasoning for istihsan is to avoid hardship: a short period (≤5 prayers) involves little difficulty, so makeup is required; a longer period (more than a day and night) would cause hardship in making up so many prayers, hence it is waived. The commentary then details various points: original vs accidental insanity; the effect of consciousness in between; the cause of the condition (sinful vs permissible); and disputes between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf. For example, if the condition is caused by consumption of alcohol (sinful), makeup is always required. If caused by permissible medicine, Abu Hanifa still requires makeup (because the text refers only to heavenly afflictions), while Muhammad waives it if the period extends. Regarding original insanity (from birth to puberty), Abu Yusuf treats it like childhood—no makeup ever—while Muhammad treats it like accidental insanity. The commentator also clarifies that the measure for 'more than five prayers' is the number of prayers (six or more) according to Muhammad and one narration from Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf considers the total time (more than a day and night). A marginal note criticizes the presentation as imprecise and suggests a better order from al-Zayla'i. The lesson includes the key proof mechanisms: istihsan vs qiyas, and reference to ijma on certain points.

Key Terms
جنون (junun): Insanity, loss of rational faculty. In this context, it refers to a state that negates the capacity for intention (niyyah), thereby excusing from prayer obligations.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness, complete loss of senses. It is treated like insanity for prayer makeup, but differs in fasting rulings.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference, departing from strict analogy (qiyas) to avoid hardship or to achieve a more equitable result. Here, istihsan is the basis for limiting makeup to five prayers.
قضاء (qada'): Making up missed acts of worship after their prescribed time. In this lesson, it refers to performing missed prayers later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view in the Hanafi school, if a person becomes unconscious and misses exactly six prayers, which prayers must be made up?
A) All six prayers must be made up.
B) The first five prayers must be made up; the sixth is waived.
C) None of the prayers must be made up because the total exceeds five.
D) Only the last prayer must be made up; the first five are waived.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school waives the obligation to make up prayers missed due to insanity or unconsciousness if the missed period exceeds five prayer times, based on istihsan to avoid hardship, with the threshold defined as six or more prayers (Muhammad's view) being the most correct position.

Qada' for Fainting and Madness: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Cause and Duration
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada' for unconsciousness and insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which qada' of salah is waived for fainting or madness according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the cause, duration, and definition of majority.

Core Idea
Qada' is not required if fainting or madness exceeds a day and night from a heavenly affliction; human-caused loss of reason may still require it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a detailed intra-Hanafi examination of when missed prayers must be made up by someone who faints or becomes insane. The general rule is that qada' is waived if the condition lasts more than a full day and night and is caused by a divine affliction. However, significant differences emerge among the founding imams regarding the cause (sin vs. permissible action), the type of madness (original vs. acquired), and how to determine whether the period is 'the majority' (by number of prayers or by hours). Understanding these nuances is essential for correct fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine the default rule for qada' when one faints or goes mad due to a heavenly affliction (e.g., illness, fear from a beast).
The default is that if the state exceeds a full day and night, qada' is not required by consensus.
2
Distinguish the cause
Analyze how the cause of unconsciousness/madness affects the ruling: heavenly affliction vs. sin (alcohol) vs. permissible action (bang/drug).
Abu Hanifa holds that only heavenly affliction waives qada'; Muhammad extends it to permissible actions if prolonged.
3
Compare positions on madness
Examine the difference between original (asli) and acquired (arid) madness in the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
Muhammad treats both equally based on duration; Abu Yusuf treats original like childhood – no qada' at all.
4
Analyze the definition of majority (akthariyyah)
Understand the two criteria for determining 'majority': by number of prayers (6 or more) vs. by hours (exceeding 24 hours).
The mufta bihi is the criterion of prayers (Muhammad's view), but Abu Yusuf uses hours, leading to practical differences.
5
Apply the ruling to an intermittent case
Consider a scenario where the person regains consciousness briefly. How does that affect the calculation of the total period?
If consciousness occurs at a known time, it resets the clock; if sudden and brief, it is disregarded.

بدوام الإغماء لأنه إذا كان يفيق فيها فإنه ينظر، فإن كان لإفاقته وقت معلوم مثل أن يخف عنه المرض عند الصبح مثلاً فيفيق قليلاً ثم يعاوده فيغمى عليه تعتبر هذه الإفاقة فيبطل ما قبلها من حكم الإغماء إذا كان لا يسقط الحق. وقال محمد : يسقط القضاء إذا كثر لأنه إنما حصل بما هو مباح. كذا في المحيط. وشمل ما إذا كان الجنون أصلياً كما إذا بلغ مجنوناً وزال وهو قول محمد، فالعارض والأصلي عنده سواء في سقوط القضاء إذا كثر وعدمه إذا قل. وقال أبو يوسف: الأصلي كالصبا فلا قضاء مطلقاً. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وقيد بالصلاة في تسوية الجنون بالإغماء لأن بينهما فرقاً في الصوم فإنه إذا أغمي عليه قبل شهر رمضان حتى مضى رمضان كله ثم أفاق فإنه يلزمه قضاء شهر رمضان، فلو جن قبل رمضان وأفاق بعد ما مضي شهر رمضان لا يلزمه قضاء الصوم كما سيأتي بيانه إن شاء الله تعالى. وظاهر كلامه أن الأكثرية من حيث الصلوات فإن الأكثر من خمس صلوات ست فأكثر وهو قول محمد ورواية عن أبي حنيفة وهو الأصح، وعند أبي يوسف وهو رواية عنه أيضاً العبرة للزيادة من حيث الساعات وفائدته تظهر فيما إذا أغمي عليه قبل الزوال فأفاق من الغد بعد الزوال، فعند أبي يوسف لا يجب القضاء، وعند محمد يجب إذا أفاق قبل خروج وقت الظهر والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب، وإليه المرجع والمآب. الخ) أقول : هذا الكلام هنا غير محرر لأنه بعد ما ذكره من التعليل لا ورود لما ذكر أصلاً. نعم يرد ظاهراً ما إذا كان بسبب فزع من سبع أو خوف من عدو لأنه يتوهم فيه أنه لم يحصل بآفة سماوية فلا يكون مما ورد فيه النص، فيجاب بالمنع لأن سببه القريب ضعف القلب وهو مرض ليس من صنع العباد، فالأحسن في With continuous fainting, because if he regains consciousness during it, then it is considered: if his regaining consciousness has a known time, such as the illness easing at dawn, so he becomes conscious briefly then it returns and he faints again – this consciousness is considered, and it invalidates the previous ruling of fainting if it was less than a day and night. And if his consciousness does not have a known time, but he regains consciousness suddenly and speaks like the healthy, then faints again, this consciousness is disregarded. This applies to fainting and madness, so it includes if it was due to fright from a beast or fear of an enemy; then qada' is not obligatory if it continues, by consensus, because fear causes weak heart which is a disease. However, an exception occurs if he lost his mind due to alcohol or fainted due to drinking bang or medicine: in the first case, qada' is not waived even if prolonged, by agreement, because it occurred through sin, so it does not cause leniency; hence his divorce takes effect. And in the second case also, it is not waived according to Abu Hanifa, because the text came regarding fainting from a heavenly affliction, so it does not apply to fainting from human action, because if the excuse comes from a direction other than the one who has the right, the right is not waived. Muhammad said: qada' is waived if it is frequent, because it occurred through what is permissible. Thus in al-Muhit. And it includes if the madness is original, such as if he reached puberty insane and then recovered – this is the view of Muhammad; according to him, temporary and original are equal in waiving qada' if frequent and not if little. Abu Yusuf said: original is like childhood, so absolutely no qada'. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. He restricted it to prayer in equating madness with fainting because there is a difference in fasting: if one faints before Ramadan until all of Ramadan passes then regains consciousness, he must make up the month of Ramadan; but if he becomes insane before Ramadan and regains consciousness after Ramadan passed, he does not have to make up the fast, as will be explained. The apparent meaning of his words is that the majority is in terms of prayers: the majority over five prayers is six or more; this is Muhammad's view and a narration from Abu Hanifa, and it is the most correct. According to Abu Yusuf, also a narration from him, the criterion is the increase in terms of hours; its benefit appears in the case of one who fainted before noon and regained consciousness the next day after noon – according to Abu Yusuf qada' is not obligatory, according to Muhammad it is obligatory if he regained consciousness before the departure of the zuhr time (the next day). And Allah knows best. (Etc.) I say: This discussion here is not well-established, because after the reasoning he mentioned, there is no mention of it originally. Yes, it appears as an objection in the case of fright from a beast or fear of an enemy, because one might think it did not occur from a heavenly affliction and thus not included in the text. It is answered by denial because its proximate cause is weak heart, which is a disease, not from human action. The best expression is what al-Zaylai mentioned: he first mentioned the case of loss of mind due to alcohol or bang and reasoned for them, then mentioned the case of fright and fear and reasoned for it; so mentioning it later serves as an answer to an implied question – a good arrangement. He said: (According to Abu Yusuf qada' is not obligatory) al-Ramli said it. I say: And from this it is known that witr is not obligatory. End. And it appears that his words 'not obligatory' are corrupted from 'not counted' (sin before ba) meaning it is not counted among the six.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the obligation of qada' for missed prayers due to unconsciousness (ighma') or insanity (junun). The main ruling: if the state of unconsciousness or madness exceeds a full day and night (24 hours) and is caused by a 'heavenly affliction' (e.g., illness, fear from a beast), then qada' is not required. However, if the cause is a sin (like alcohol) or a human action (like taking bang/drug), the ruling differs. The author first discusses intermittent fainting: if the person regains consciousness at a known time (e.g., dawn) and then faints again, that consciousness invalidates the previous period of fainting, but only if the total fainting before that was less than a day and night. If he regains consciousness suddenly without a known time, it is disregarded. Then he extends the same ruling to fainting from fear, which is considered a disease. The exception: if the cause is alcohol (sin) or bang (permissible according to Muhammad), Abu Hanifa says qada' is not waived for bang either, because the textual proof (hadith) only applies to divine afflictions, not human actions. Muhammad disagrees, saying qada' is waived if the fainting is prolonged, because bang is permissible. For original insanity (asli), Muhammad treats it like acquired insanity (arid) regarding qada' based on duration, while Abu Yusuf compares it to childhood — no qada' at all. The passage also notes that for fasting, the ruling differs: fainting for a whole month requires qada', but insanity does not. Finally, the dispute over determining 'majority' (akthariyyah): Muhammad and one narration from Abu Hanifa say majority is by the number of prayers (6 or more), while Abu Yusuf says by hours. The author of the commentary (Ibn Nujaym) critiques the previous commentator (possibly al-Zaylai) for not properly ordering the discussion, then corrects it by presenting al-Zaylai's better arrangement: first alcohol/bang, then fear/fright. He also notes that according to Abu Yusuf, qada' is not obligatory in the example given, but Muhammad disagrees. The end suggests a textual corruption: 'لا يجب' should be 'لا يحسب' (not counted).

Key Terms
إغماء (ighma'): Loss of consciousness; fainting that prevents perception and awareness.
جنون (junun): Madness; a mental disorder that supplants reason.
آفة سماوية (afah samawiyyah): A heavenly affliction; a calamity from Allah, not human action, such as disease or fear from a beast.
الأكثرية (al-akthariyyah): The majority; here it refers to whether the period of unconsciousness is considered 'long' by the number of prayers (6 or more) or by hours (exceeding a day and night in hours).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person faints due to a permissible medicine (e.g., a prescribed sedative) for more than a day and night, which of the following statements is correct?
A) Qada' is waived because it exceeds a day and night, regardless of cause.
B) Qada' is not waived according to Abu Hanifa, but is waived according to Muhammad al-Shaybani.
C) Qada' is always waived for any substance that is not a sin.
D) Qada' is not waived under any circumstance for any substance.

Key Takeaway
The waiver of qada' for unconsciousness or madness in Hanafi fiqh depends critically on the cause (heavenly affliction vs. human action) and on the duration exceeding a day and night, with internal disagreement on how to measure 'majority' and treat original madness.

Defining Sujud al-Tilawah: Conditions, Pillars, and Rulings
Opens the chapter on Sujud al-Tilawah, explaining its placement and basic rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sujud al-Tilawah, state its wajib nature, list its conditions and pillars, and distinguish between the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding its completion.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Tilawah is a wajib prostration with conditions like salah except the opening takbir, and its pillar is placing the forehead.

This lesson opens the chapter on Sujud al-Tilawah (Prostration of Recitation). The author explains its placement in the text and then defines its ruling, conditions, and what invalidates it. You will learn that sujud al-tilawah is obligatory upon reciting or hearing specific verses, and it shares most conditions with prayer except the opening takbir. The lesson also introduces an important intra-Hanafi dispute about when the prostration is considered complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause and ruling
The passage states that sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon recitation or hearing. The cause is the recitation (and hearing), and the ruling is wajib, not fard, because its evidence is not qat'i.
The author notes that 'tilawah' covers both recitation and hearing, as recitation implies hearing.
2
List the conditions and pillar
The text says conditions are like salah except the opening takbir (tahrimah). The pillar (rukn) is placing the forehead on the ground, or gesturing if unable.
The opening takbir is excluded because it is meant to unify different actions, but sujud al-tilawah is a single prostration.
3
Apply istihsan for riding during travel
Qiyas would require full prostration on the ground, but istihsan allows gesturing on a ride during travel due to frequent occurrence and hardship, similar to supererogatory acts.
This concession does not apply to obligatory (fard) prayers or vowed prayers.
4
Analyze the dispute on invalidation
Muhammad holds that the prostration is complete only upon raising the head, so an invalidator before raising voids it. Abu Yusuf holds that placement alone completes it, so an invalidator after placement does not void it. The text presents both without explicit tarjih, but the cautious view (Muhammad's) is commonly followed.
The practical consequence: if one speaks after placing the forehead but before raising, according to Abu Yusuf it is valid, according to Muhammad it must be repeated.

Source Text
