باب سجود التلاوة كان من حق هذا الباب أن يقترن بسجود السهو لأن كلاً منهما سجدة لكن لما كان صلاة المريض بعارض سماوي كالسهو وألحقتها المناسبة به فتأخر سجود التلاوة ضرورة، وهو من قبيل إضافة الحكم إلى سببه. وإنما لم يقل سجود التلاوة والسماع بياناً للسببين لأن السماع سبب أيضاً لما أن التلاوة لما كانت سبباً للسماع أيضاً كان ذكرها مشتملاً على السماع من وجه فاكتفي به . وفي إضافة السجود إلى التلاوة إشارة إلى أنه إذا كتبها أو تهجاها لا يجب عليه سجود ولا تفسد الصلاة بالهجاء لأنه موجود في القرآن وشرائطها شرائط الصلاة إلا التحريمة لأنها لتوحيد الأفعال المختلفة ولم يوجد وركنها وضع الجبهة على الأرض أو ما يقوم مقامه من الركوع كما سيأتي، أو من الإيماء للمريض أو كان راكباً على الدابة في السفر وتلاها أو سمعها والقياس أن لا يجزئه الإيماء على الراحلة لأنها واجبة فلا يجوز أداؤها على الراحلة من غير عذر لكنهم استحسنوه لأن التلاوة أمر دائم بمنزلة التطوع فكان في اشتراط حرج بخلاف الفرض والمنذور. وما وجب من السجدة على الأرض لا يجوز على الدابة، وما وجب على الدابة يجوز على الأرض لأن ما وجب على الأرض وجبت تامة فلا تسقط بالإيماء، ولو تلاها على الدابة فنزل ثم ركب فأداها بالإيماء جاز. ويفسدها ما يفسد من الحدث العمد والكلام والقهقهة وعليه إعادتها كما لو وجدت في سجدة الصلاة، وقيل هذا على قول محمد لأن العبرة عنده لتمام الركن وهو الرفع ولم يحصل بعده، فأما عند أبي يوسف فقد حصل قبل هذه العوارض والعبرة عنده للوضع فينبغي أن لا يفسدها. وفي النزول له الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة : قوله: (لكن لما كان الخ قال الرملي ووجه آخر وهو أن سجود التلاوة قد يكون في الصلاة وقد يكون خارجها بخلاف صلاة المريض فإنها نفس الصلاة وأحكامها واردة على نفس الماهية فيها، وكذا سجود السهو يؤدي فيها لا خارجها تأمل قوله : (لأن السماع سبب أيضاً) قال في النهر : هذا مما لا حاجة إليه على رأي المصنف فقد رجح في الكافي أن السبب إنما هو التلاوة وأن السماع في حق السامع إنما هو شرط فقط، نعم ذهب صاحب الهداية إلى أن السماع سبب أيضاً فاعتذر عنه شراحها بما مر ا هـ. وما في الكافي صححه في المحيط كما في التتارخانية وصححه في الظهيرية أيضاً قوله : (إلا) التحريمة قال في النهر وينبغي أن يزاد وإلا نية التعيين البحر الرائق ج ٢ م ١٤
Chapter of the Prostration of Recitation. It was fitting for this chapter to be joined with the chapter of the Prostration of Forgetfulness, because each is a prostration. However, because the prayer of the sick is due to a heavenly accident like forgetfulness, and appropriateness attached it to that, the Prostration of Recitation was delayed out of necessity; and this is of the type of adding the ruling to its cause. He did not say 'prostration of recitation and hearing' to explain both causes, because hearing is also a cause; since recitation is also a cause for hearing, its mention includes hearing in a way, so it suffices. And in adding 'prostration' to 'recitation' there is an indication that if he writes it or spells it out, prostration is not obligatory upon him, and the prayer is not invalidated by spelling because it is present in the Qur'an. Its conditions are the conditions of prayer except the opening takbir (tahrimah), because that is for unifying different actions, and it is not found here. Its pillar is placing the forehead on the ground or what takes its place from bowing (ruku'), as will come, or from gesturing (ima') for the sick, or if one is riding an animal in travel and recites or hears it. The analogy (qiyas) is that gesturing on the riding animal should not be sufficient, because it is obligatory (wajib), so it is not permissible to perform it on a riding animal without an excuse. But they practiced istihsan (juristic preference) because recitation is a continuous matter like supererogatory acts, so requiring (the ground) would cause hardship, unlike obligatory (fard) and vowed prayers. That which becomes obligatory (wajib) of the prostration on the ground is not permissible on the animal, and that which becomes obligatory on the animal is permissible on the ground, because that which became obligatory on the ground was required fully, so it is not waived by gesturing. And if he recites it on the animal, then dismounts, then mounts again and performs it by gesturing, it is permissible. It is invalidated by what invalidates (prayer) from intentional hadath (breaking wudu), speech, and loud laughter; he must repeat it just as if it occurred in the prostration of prayer. It is said this is according to Muhammad's view, because the criterion (fi) is the completion of the pillar (rukn), which is the raising, and it had not occurred after; while according to Abu Yusuf, it had occurred before these impediments, and his criterion is the placement, so it should not invalidate it. And in the gloss: (His words: 'but because... etc.') al-Ramli said: Another aspect is that the prostration of recitation can be in prayer and outside it, unlike the prayer of the sick, which is itself prayer and its rulings apply to the same essence; similarly, the prostration of forgetfulness is performed within it, not outside it. Contemplate. His words: ('because hearing is also a cause') al-Nahr said: This is unnecessary according to the author's view, because he preferred in al-Kafi that the cause is only recitation, and hearing for the listener is only a condition. However, the author of al-Hidayah held that hearing is also a cause, and his commentators excused it as mentioned. And what is in al-Kafi is corrected in al-Muhit as in al-Tatarkhaniyya, and also corrected in al-Zahiriyya. His words: ('except') the tahrimah. Al-Nahr said: One should add 'and the intention of specification (niyyah al-ta'yin).' Al-Bahr al-Raiq vol. 2 p. 14.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Sujud al-Tilawah (Prostration of Recitation). The author first explains why this chapter follows the chapter on the prayer of the sick: both involve a prostration, but the prostration of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw) is more closely related to prayer, so it was placed earlier; sujud al-tilawah is placed here due to a thematic connection. The author then defines the act: it is wajib upon reciting or hearing specific verses of the Qur'an. The name itself indicates that recitation is the cause; hearing is also a cause but is included in 'tilawah' because recitation implies hearing. If one merely writes or spells the verses, no prostration is required. The conditions (shurut) for sujud al-tilawah are the same as for prayer (taharah, facing qibla, etc.) except for the opening takbir (tahrimah) because that is meant to unify different actions, and here there is only one prostration. The pillar (rukn) is placing the forehead on the ground; if unable, one can gesture (ima') like a sick person, or even when riding a camel during travel. Qiyas would suggest that a wajib act cannot be performed by gesture on a ride without excuse, but the scholars practiced istihsan (juristic preference) because recitation of these verses is frequent like supererogatory prayers, and requiring dismounting would cause hardship. However, if the obligation arose while on the ground (e.g., starting to recite while not traveling), one must prostrate on the ground; if it arose while riding, one may gesture. The passage also discusses what invalidates the prostration: intentional hadath (nullifying wudu), speech, and loud laughter, and one must repeat it. There is a disagreement between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf: Muhammad considers the prostration complete only upon raising the head, so if an invalidator occurs before raising, it is invalid; Abu Yusuf considers the placement (putting the forehead down) as the criterion, so once placed, the prostration is complete and not invalidated by later events. The author then includes marginal notes: al-Ramli gives another reason for the chapter placement; al-Nahr comments on the cause of sujud al-tilawah (recitation vs. hearing) and adds that intention of specification (niyyah al-ta'yin) should also be mentioned as a condition.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific verses of the Qur'an; it is wajib in the Hanafi school.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar to begin prayer). Here it is noted that sujud al-tilawah does not require it, because it is not a full prayer with multiple actions.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing; a motion of the head or body to indicate prostration when unable to prostrate fully due to illness or riding.
الراحلة (al-rahilah): A riding animal (camel, horse) used for travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of Sujud al-Tilawah according to the text?
A) Taharah (purity)
B) Facing the qibla
C) Opening takbir (tahrimah)
D) Placing the forehead on the ground or gesturing

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Tilawah is a wajib prostration with conditions similar to salah except the opening takbir; it may be performed by gesture during travel due to istihsan, and there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the point of completion that affects its validity.

Conditions, Ruling, and Nullifiers of Sujud al-Tilawah
Explains conditions, istihsan for gesture, and nullifiers of Sujud al-Tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and pillar of Sujud al-Tilawah, explain the istihsan for performing it on a mount, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether an invalidating act nullifies it.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Tilawah is wajib; its conditions mirror prayer except takbir; gesture on a mount is valid by istihsan due to frequency and hardship.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the placement of the chapter on Sujud al-Tilawah, its essential conditions, the rukn, and the ruling for performing it while traveling. It also clarifies what actions invalidate the sujud and highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the timing of completion of the pillar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal ruling
The act is Sujud al-Tilawah. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory) due to the hadith 'Al-sajdatu 'ala man sami'aha' and other evidence, though not fard because the proof is zanni.
The passage does not explicitly state wujub but the Hanafi position is assumed; the conditions and nullifiers align with that.
2
List the conditions for validity
The conditions are the same as those for prayer: taharah, facing qibla, covering awrah, etc., except the opening takbir (tahrimah). The takbir is omitted because it is meant to unify multiple acts, whereas Sujud al-Tilawah is a single act.
The text states: 'شرائطها شرائط الصلاة إلا التحريمة' — its conditions are the conditions of prayer except the takbir.
3
Determine the pillar (rukn)
The pillar of Sujud al-Tilawah is placing the forehead on the ground or any equivalent (such as a gesture for the sick or a rider). The text emphasizes that the rukn is the placement (wad'), not the raising.
This becomes crucial in the later dispute about nullification.
4
Analyze the istihsan for performing on a mount
By strict analogy (qiyas), performing an obligatory sujud on a mount without excuse would not be valid. However, the scholars applied istihsan (juristic preference) because recitation is frequent and requiring dismount would cause undue hardship, akin to supererogatory acts. Therefore, a traveler may gesture on a mount.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here due to the principle of removing hardship.
5
Examine the nullifiers and the intra-Hanafi dispute
Actions that invalidate prayer (intentional hadath, speech, loud laughter) also invalidate Sujud al-Tilawah. A dispute arises: According to Imam Muhammad, the invalidating act nullifies the sujud if it occurs before raising the head, because the pillar is not complete until the raising. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the sujud is valid because the placement (the pillar) already occurred before the invalidating act.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is whether repetition is required. The mufta bihi is typically Muhammad's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة
كان من حق هذا الباب أن يقترن بسجود السهو لأن كلاً منهما سجدة لكن لما كان صلاة المريض بعارض سماوي كالسهو وألحقتها المناسبة به فتأخر سجود التلاوة ضرورة، وهو من قبيل إضافة الحكم إلى سببه. وإنما لم يقل سجود التلاوة والسماع بياناً للسببين لأن السماع سبب أيضاً لما أن التلاوة لما كانت سبباً للسماع أيضاً كان ذكرها مشتملاً على السماع من وجه فاكتفي به . وفي إضافة السجود إلى التلاوة إشارة إلى أنه إذا كتبها أو تهجاها لا يجب عليه سجود ولا تفسد الصلاة بالهجاء لأنه موجود في القرآن وشرائطها شرائط الصلاة إلا التحريمة لأنها لتوحيد الأفعال المختلفة ولم يوجد وركنها وضع الجبهة على الأرض أو ما يقوم مقامه من الركوع كما سيأتي، أو من الإيماء للمريض أو كان راكباً على الدابة في السفر وتلاها أو سمعها والقياس أن لا يجزئه الإيماء على الراحلة لأنها واجبة فلا يجوز أداؤها على الراحلة من غير عذر لكنهم استحسنوه لأن التلاوة أمر دائم بمنزلة التطوع فكان في اشتراط حرج بخلاف الفرض والمنذور. وما وجب من السجدة على الأرض لا يجوز على الدابة، وما وجب على الدابة يجوز على الأرض لأن ما وجب على الأرض وجبت تامة فلا تسقط بالإيماء، ولو تلاها على الدابة فنزل ثم ركب فأداها بالإيماء جاز. ويفسدها ما يفسد من الحدث العمد والكلام والقهقهة وعليه إعادتها كما لو وجدت في سجدة الصلاة، وقيل هذا على قول محمد لأن العبرة عنده لتمام الركن وهو الرفع ولم يحصل بعده، فأما عند أبي يوسف فقد حصل قبل هذه العوارض والعبرة عنده للوضع فينبغي أن لا يفسدها.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah. It was appropriate for this chapter to be placed alongside Sujud al-Sahw because each is a prostration, but since the prayer of the sick is due to a heavenly cause like forgetfulness, and appropriateness attached it to that, so Sujud al-Tilawah was delayed necessarily, and it is of the type of adding the ruling to its cause. He did not say 'Sujud al-Tilawah and hearing' to state the two causes because hearing is also a cause; since recitation is also a cause for hearing, mentioning it includes hearing in one aspect, so sufficed with it. Adding prostration to recitation indicates that if one writes it or spells it out, no prostration is required, and prayer is not invalidated by spelling because it exists in the Quran. Its conditions are those of prayer except the takbir because it is for unifying different actions and does not exist. Its pillar is placing the forehead on the ground or what stands in its place from bowing as will come, or by gesture for the sick, or if one is riding on an animal in travel and recites or hears it. By analogy, gesturing on the mount would not suffice because it is obligatory and cannot be performed on a mount without excuse, but they deemed it good (istihsan) because recitation is a constant act akin to supererogatory worship, so requiring (dismounting) would be hardship, unlike obligatory and vowed acts. What is obligatory of prostration on the ground is not permissible on the mount, but what is obligatory on the mount is permissible on the ground because what is obligatory on the ground is complete and cannot be dropped by gesture. If one recited while on the mount, then dismounted, then mounted and performed it by gesture, it is permissible. It is invalidated by what invalidates (prayer): intentional hadath, speech, and loud laughter, and one must repeat it as if it occurred in the prostration of prayer. It is said this is according to Muhammad's view because with him the consideration is for the completion of the pillar, which is raising (the head), and it had not occurred afterward. As for Abu Yusuf, it had occurred before these impediments, and with him the consideration is for placing (the head), so it should not invalidate it.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the placement of the chapter on Sujud al-Tilawah and its conditions. The author explains why this chapter is placed after Sujud al-Sahw: both are prostrations, but Sujud al-Sahw is more closely related to the prayer of the sick due to a common heavenly cause, so Sujud al-Tilawah is delayed. He clarifies that the cause for prostration is recitation, not necessarily hearing, though hearing is also a cause in some views. The conditions for performing Sujud al-Tilawah are the same as for prayer (taharah, facing qibla, covering awra, etc.) except for the opening takbir (tahrimah), because the takbir is meant to unify different actions and is not present here. The pillar (rukn) of this prostration is placing the forehead on the ground, or if unable, bowing, or gesturing for a sick person, or for a traveler on a mount. The text then discusses the ruling for performing sujud on a ride: by qiyas, it would not be valid to perform an obligatory act on a mount without excuse, but the scholars applied istihsan (juristic preference) because recitation occurs frequently and requiring dismounting would cause hardship, similar to supererogatory acts. However, if the sujud is obligatory in origin (e.g., prostration for a specific verse during prayer), it must be done on the ground. An interesting point: if a person recited on a mount, then dismounted, then remounted and performed sujud with gesture, it is permissible. The passage also covers what invalidates the sujud: intentional hadath (breaking wudu), speaking, and loud laughter (qahqaha) – all require repetition. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Muhammad, the sujud is invalidated because the pillar (raising the head after prostration) was not completed, whereas according to Abu Yusuf, the sujud is valid because the placing of the forehead (the actual prostration) occurred before the invalidating act.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): The prostration performed when reciting or hearing specific verses of the Quran, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates prayer; it is not required for sujud al-tilawah because it is meant to unify different actions and sujud al-tilawah is a single act.
الإيماء (al-īmā'): A gesture made by head or body instead of full prostration, permitted for the sick or the traveler on a mount for sujud al-tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Tilawah is a wajib act with conditions similar to prayer except takbir; its performance by gesture on a mount is permissible by istihsan, and an invalidating act before raising the head nullifies it per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah: Verses, Proof, and Timing
Lists the 14 sujud verses, proves obligation with hadith, and discusses timing of performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the 14 sujud verses according to the Hanafi school, explain why sujud al-tilawah is wajib not fard, and state the mufta bihi position that it may be performed on tarakhi (delay).

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib due to zanni evidence; the relied-upon view allows delayed performance.

Sujud al-tilawah is a distinct act of worship triggered by reciting or hearing certain Quranic verses. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling: which verses, why it is obligatory, and when it must be performed. We will work through the proofs from hadith and the reasoning that makes this ruling wajib rather than fard, and then navigate the internal Hanafi disagreement on timing.

Guided Path
1
List the 14 sujud verses
Identify the 14 surahs and verses as per the Hanafi count, noting that four are in the first half of the Quran and ten in the latter half. The list is taken from the Mushaf of 'Uthman.
Memorising this list is essential for application.
2
Analyse the proof of obligation
Examine the hadith 'السجدة على من سمعها' and the Satan narration. Note that the preposition 'على' indicates obligation (as in 'عليكم الصلاة'), and the Satan story reinforces merit and obligation. The hadith is ahad, making its transmission zanni.
The text defends the authenticity of this hadith against those who consider it a Companion statement.
3
Distinguish wajib from fard
Because the evidence (hadith and Quranic indications) is zanni in both thubut and dalala, the ruling is wajib, not fard. Fard requires qat'i evidence (mutawatir or Quran).
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: the level of obligation corresponds to the strength of the evidence.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
Abu Hanifa has two narrations: one for fawr (immediate), one for tarakhi (delay). Abu Yusuf holds fawr; Muhammad holds tarakhi. The text indicates the mufta bihi is tarakhi.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether delaying is sinful and whether a later prostration is ada' or qada'.
5
Determine the consequence of the mufta bihi
Under the tarakhi view, if one prostrates later, it counts as ada' (performance), not qada' (make-up), meaning no sin has occurred by delaying within a reasonable time.
This is based on the principle that an obligation without a specified time can be performed at any time before it becomes overdue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تجب بأربع عشرة آية أي تجب سجدة التلاوة بسبب تلاوة آية من أربع عشرة آية في أربع عشرة سورة وهي الأعراف في آخرها ،والرعد والنحل، وبني اسرائيل، من الحج والفرقان والنمل، وألم ،تنزيل ،وص وحم السجدة، والنجم، والانشقاق، والعلق . هكذا كتب في مصحف عثمان وهو المعتمد فهي أربع في الأول وعشر في النصف الآخر. وإنما كانت واجبة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «السجدة على من سمعها» (۱) «وعلى» للإلزام. ولما رواه مسلم عن أبي هريرة في الإيمان يرفعه «إذا قرأ ابن آدم السجدة اعتزل الشيطان يبكي يقول يا ويله أمر ابن آدم بالسجود فسجد فله الجنة، وأمرت بالسجود فامتنعت فلي النار ) (۱) والأصل أن الحكيم إذا حكى عن غير الحكيم ولم يعقبه بالإنكار كان دليل صحته. فهذا ظاهر في الوجوب مع أن آي السجدة تفيده أيضاً لأنها ثلاثة أقسام : قسم فيه الأمر الصريح به وقسم تضمن حكاية استنكاف الكفرة حيث وقسم فيه حكاية فعل الأنبياء السجود وكل من الامتثال والاقتداء ومخالفة الكفرة واجب إلا أن يدل دليل في معين على عدم لزومه لكن دلالتها فيه ظنية فكان الثابت الوجوب لا الفرض، والاتفاق على أن ثبوتها على المكلفين مقيد بالتلاوة لا مطلقاً . فلزم واجبة على التراخي إن لم تكن صلاتية لأن دلائل الوجوب مطلقة عن تعيين الوقت فيجب في كلاماً كذلك. ثم هي ففي القنية أنه لا يجب يعني تعيين أنها سجدة آية كذا قول المصنف : بأربع عشرة آية) قال في النهر : أي بسبب تلاوتها ويجوز أن تكون الباء بمعنى في أي في أربع عشرة آية وكأنه أولى إذ مقتضى الأولى توقف الوجوب على تلاوة الأربعة عشر ، وقوله في البحر أي تجب الخ» مما لا دليل في كلامه عليه قوله : لقوله عليه السلام السجدة على من سمعها قال في العناية : اعلم أن صاحب النهاية قال : جعل هذا اللفظ في سائر النسخ من المبسوطين والأسرار والمحيط وشرح الجامع الصغير من ألفاظ الصحابة لا من الحديث. وأقول : لم يكن المصنف ممن لم يطالع الكتب المذكورة فلولا أنه ثبت عنده كونه حديثاً لما نقله حديثاً فإنه رحمه الله تعالى أعظم ديانة ممن يتوهم به ذلك ا هـ . . قوله : (ثم هي واجبة على التراخي قال في العناية : فمن سجد كان أداء لا قضاء وذلك عند محمد ورواية عن أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف وفي رواية أبي حنيفة أن وجوبها على الفور ا هـ. ونقل في الدرر عن
It is obligatory due to fourteen verses, meaning the prostration of recitation is obligatory due to reciting a verse from fourteen verses in fourteen surahs: al-A'raf (at its end), al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, Bani Isra'il, al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, Alif Lam Tanzil, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-'Alaq. Thus it is written in the Mushaf of 'Uthman and it is the relied-upon; so there are four in the first half and ten in the latter half. It is only obligatory because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it,' and 'upon' (على) indicates obligation. Also because of what Muslim narrated from Abu Hurairah raising it to the Prophet: 'When the son of Adam recites the prostration, Satan withdraws weeping saying, 'Woe to me! The son of Adam was commanded to prostrate and he prostrated, so Paradise is for him; I was commanded to prostrate and I refused, so the Fire is for me.' And the principle is that when a wise person narrates from an unwise person and does not follow it with disapproval, it is evidence of its validity. So this is apparent in obligation, and also the verses of prostration indicate it because they are three types: one containing explicit command for it, one containing the narration of the disbelievers' refusal, and one containing the narration of the prophets' prostration. Each of compliance, following, and opposing the disbelievers is obligatory unless evidence indicates otherwise in a specific case, but their indication is zanni (probable), so what is established is obligation not fard. There is agreement that its being obligatory upon those held accountable is conditioned by recitation, not absolute. So it becomes obligatory on tarakhi (delayed performance) if it is not performed during prayer, because the evidences of obligation are unrestricted regarding time. Then it is said in al-Qunyah: it is not obligatory to specify that it is for a particular verse. The author's statement: 'due to fourteen verses' – al-Nahr says: due to reciting them, and it is possible that the 'ba' is in the meaning of 'in', i.e., in fourteen verses, and that is more appropriate, and his statement in al-Bahr: 'meaning it is obligatory' etc., has no evidence for it in his speech. His statement: 'Because of his saying, peace be upon him: the prostration is upon the one who hears it.' Al-'Inayah says: Know that the author of al-Nihayah said: This wording in the various copies of al-Mabsut, al-Asrar, al-Muhit, and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir is from the sayings of the Companions, not from hadith. And I say: The author is not one who has not reviewed the mentioned books; if it were not established with him as hadith, he would not have transmitted it as hadith, for he, may Allah have mercy on him, is greater in piety than those who think that of him. His statement: 'Then it is obligatory on tarakhi.' Al-'Inayah says: So whoever prostrates, it is performance (ada') not make-up (qada'), and that is according to Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifah, while according to Abu Yusuf and another narration from Abu Hanifah, its obligation is immediate (fawr). And it is transmitted in al-Durar from...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that establishes the obligation of sujud al-tilawah, listing the specific verses and providing the evidence. The text first states that sujud al-tilawah is obligatory due to reciting or hearing any of fourteen verses from fourteen surahs. It lists them: al-A'raf (verse 206), al-Ra'd (verse 15), al-Nahl (verse 49), Bani Isra'il (verse 107), al-Hajj (verse 18), al-Furqan (verse 60), al-Naml (verse 25), Alif Lam Tanzil (verse 15), Sad (verse 24), Ha Mim al-Sajdah (verse 37), al-Najm (verse 62), al-Inshiqaq (verse 21), and al-'Alaq (verse 19). It mentions that this list is from the Mushaf of Uthman and is the relied-upon count. There are four verses in the first half of the Quran and ten in the latter half. The proof of obligation is the hadith: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it' – the preposition 'upon' indicates obligation. Also, a hadith from Muslim describes Satan weeping because the son of Adam obeys and prostrates, while Satan refused. The principle is that when Allah, the Wise, narrates the action of Satan without condemning it, it implies approval, but here the hadith clearly encourages sujud. The text then explains why it is wajib, not fard: the verses that command or mention prostration are of three types: explicit command, narration of disbelievers' refusal, and narration of prophets' prostration. Obeying a command, following prophets, and opposing disbelievers are generally obligatory, but the indication of these verses is zanni (probable), not qat'i, so the ruling is wajib, not fard. Furthermore, the obligation is conditional upon recitation or hearing, not absolute. Then there is a discussion about the timing: according to Muhammad and one narration from Abu Hanifah, the obligation is on tarakhi (delayed, meaning one can perform it later), while Abu Yusuf and another narration from Abu Hanifah say it is on fawr (immediate). The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is on tarakhi, so if one prostrates later, it counts as ada' (performance), not qada' (make-up). The text also addresses a concern about the authenticity of the hadith 'al-sajdatu 'ala man sami'aha', affirming that the author (likely the commentator) considered it authentic.

Key Terms
آيات السجدة (āyāt al-sajdah): The 14 Quranic verses upon reciting or hearing which sujud al-tilawah becomes wajib.
الوجوب (al-wujūb): The legal obligation; here sujud al-tilawah is wajib, meaning it is obligatory but with evidence of zanni thubut and dalala, so its status is not as strong as fard.
التراخي (al-tarākhī): Delayed performance; the ruling that sujud al-tilawah need not be performed immediately after recitation, but can be done later as long as it is still within a reasonable time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib due to hearing or reciting any of 14 specific verses, and the relied-upon Hanafi view permits delayed performance (tarakhi).

Obligation of Sajdah al-Tilawah: Fourteen Verses and the Proofs
States the number and list of sajdah verses and proves obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of sajdah verses, identify the Hanafi ruling (wajib), and explain the proof structure that establishes it as wajib not fard.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib for fourteen verses based on hadith and Quranic indications, but the evidence is zanni, so it is wajib, not fard.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq specifies that it is wajib for fourteen verses from fourteen surahs, based on the Mushaf of 'Uthman. We will explore the proofs from hadith and the Quranic verses themselves, and understand why the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib (obligatory but less than fard) due to the speculative nature of the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the act is (sajdah al-tilawah) and its hukm (wajib). Note who is obligated: the reciter and the hearer.
2
Learn the list of verses
Memorize the fourteen surahs containing sajdah verses: al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, Bani Isra'il, al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, Alif Lam Mim Tanzil, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, al-'Alaq. Note that four are in the first half and ten in the second half.
This list is from the Mushaf of 'Uthman, which is the relied-upon source.
3
Examine the first proof (hadith)
Analyze the hadith 'al-sajdatu 'ala man sami'aha'. In Hanafi usul, the preposition 'ala indicates obligation (wujub). The hadith is ahad, so it establishes zanni evidence, making the ruling wajib not fard.
The translation: 'The sajdah is upon the one who hears it.'
4
Examine the second proof (hadith of Satan)
Understand the hadith from Muslim: Satan laments that Adam is commanded to prostrate and obeys, while Satan refuses. Allah narrates this without disapproval, which, by the principle that the Wise (Allah) would not relate something incorrect without objection, implies approval of the command to prostrate.
This reinforces the obligation.
5
Analyze the Quranic verses themselves
The sajdah verses fall into three categories: those with an explicit command to prostrate, those narrating the disbelievers' refusal, and those narrating the prophets' prostration. Compliance, emulation of prophets, and opposition to disbelievers are all wajib, so the sajdah is wajib. However, the indications are zanni in meaning, so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
6
Understand why wajib, not fard
The evidence (hadith and Quranic implications) is zanni (speculative) in transmission or meaning. Hanafi usul distinguishes: fard requires qat'i evidence (e.g., Quran, mutawatir hadith), while wajib is established by zanni evidence. Hence, sajdah al-tilawah is wajib.
This epistemological distinction is crucial.

Source Text

It is obligatory due to fourteen verses including the first of al-Hajj and Sad, upon one who recites, even if an imam, or hears, even if... in fourteen surahs: al-A'raf at its end, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, Bani Isra'il, from al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, Alif Lam Mim Tanzil, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, al-'Alaq. The son of Adam was commanded to prostrate and he prostrated, so he has Paradise; I was commanded to prostrate and I refused, so I have Hellfire.' And the principle is that when the Wise [i.e., Allah] relates about someone other than the wise and does not follow it with disapproval, that is evidence of its correctness. This is apparent in obligation, even though the verses of sajdah also indicate it, because they are three types: a type containing the explicit command for it, a type containing the narration of the disbelievers' disdain where, and a type containing the narration of the prophets' prostration; and each of compliance, following, and opposing the disbelievers is wajib, unless evidence indicates non-necessity in a specific case, but its indication therein is zanni, so what is established is wujub, not fard. And there is agreement that its establishment upon the obligated is tied to recitation, not absolutely. So it is obligatory with delay if it is not a prayer sajdah, because the evidences of obligation are absolute regarding time specification, so it must be performed in a part of time without specification, and it becomes specified by actually performing it, and the obligation becomes restricted at the end of his life in all expanded obligations.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah. It begins by stating that sajdah al-tilawah is wajib due to reciting or hearing fourteen specific verses from fourteen surahs, which are listed. The author notes that this list is taken from the Mushaf of 'Uthman, which is the relied-upon count. There are four verses in the first half of the Quran and ten in the second half. The passage then provides two proofs: the hadith 'al-sajdatu 'ala man sami'aha' (the sajdah is upon the one who hears it) where the preposition 'ala indicates obligation; and the hadith from Muslim about Satan's reaction to the sajdah, arguing that Allah's narration without disapproval constitutes approval, thus making it wajib. The author then analyzes the sajdah verses themselves: some contain an explicit command to prostrate, some narrate the disbelievers' refusal, and some narrate the prostration of prophets. Since compliance, emulation, and opposing the disbelievers are all wajib, the sajdah is wajib. However, because the evidence is zanni (speculative) in meaning, it establishes wujub (obligation) but not fard (necessity at the level of fard). There is consensus that it is conditional upon recitation or hearing. Finally, if not performed in prayer, it is wajib with delay (muwassa'), because the evidences do not specify a time, so it can be performed at any time until death, though it becomes restricted at the end of life. This is consistent with other expanded obligations.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration that is wajib upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran.
واجبة (wājibah): In this context, legally obligatory with a speculative evidence (zanni); less than fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the sajdah is only for the reciter, not the hearer
D) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib upon reciter and hearer for fourteen specific verses, and its obligation is proven by hadith and Quranic analysis, but the zanni nature of the evidence places it at the level of wajib, not fard.

Time and Eligibility for Sajdah al-Tilawah
Discusses timing and eligibility for sajdah al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of sajdah al-tilawah (immediate in prayer, delayed outside) and identify who is obligated, applying the conditions of eligibility for prayer.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib: outside prayer with delay, in prayer immediately; eligibility mirrors prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two key aspects of sajdah al-tilawah: when it must be performed and upon whom it is obligatory. The Hanafi school internally debates whether the obligation is immediate or allows delay outside prayer, while there is consensus that during prayer it must be done promptly. Additionally, the passage clarifies that the obligation falls on anyone who is eligible for prayer—Muslim, sane, mature, and free from menstruation/postpartum—and also on the hearer, with the exception of hearing from an insane person or an echo.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time dimension
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib. The passage first discusses whether its performance is restricted to an immediate time (faur) or can be delayed (tarakhi) without sin.
The act itself is obligatory; the dispute is about the time envelope.
2
Distinguish outside prayer vs inside prayer
For recitation outside prayer, the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that the obligation is delayed—one may prostrate later and it counts as ada'. For recitation during prayer, the obligation is immediate because it becomes part of the prayer's acts.
This distinction is crucial: the ruling changes based on context.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
Imam Muhammad and one narration from Abu Hanifa hold delay; Abu Yusuf and another narration from Abu Hanifa hold immediacy. The mufta bihi is delay outside prayer, as stated in al-Hidayah and al-Bahr.
This shows how multiple valid opinions exist; the school eventually adopts one for fatwa.
4
Apply eligibility conditions for obligation
The passage states that sajdah al-tilawah is obligatory on anyone who is eligible for the obligation of prayer: Muslim, sane, mature, free from menstruation/postpartum. This includes those in minor or major impurity.
Eligibility (ahliyyah) for prayer is the benchmark.
5
Identify exceptions and special cases
The sajdah is not obligatory on a disbeliever, child, insane person, menstruating woman, or woman in postpartum, even if they recite or hear. The hearer is obligated except if the reciter is insane (lack of meaningful recitation) or if hearing an echo.
These exceptions follow from the absence of eligibility or valid recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ثم هي واجبة على التراخي) قال في العناية: فمن سجد كان أداء لا قضاء وذلك عند محمد ورواية عن أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف وفي رواية أبي حنيفة أن وجوبها على الفور ا هـ. ونقل في الدرر عن الخانية أنها تفسد على ظاهر الجواب اتفاقاً إلا أنه لا وضوء عليه في القهقهة، وكذا محاذاة المرأة لا تفسدها كما في صلاة الجنازة، ولو نام فيها لا تنتقض طهارته كالصلبية على الصحيح وسيأتي بقية أحكامها. وأما المتلوة في الصلاة فإنها تجب على سبيل التضييق لقيام دليل التضييق وهو أنها وجبت بما هو من أفعال الصلاة وهو القراءة فالتحقت بأقوالها وصارت جزءاً من أجزائها، ولهذا قلنا: إذا تلا آية السجدة ولم يسجد ولم يركع حتى القراءة ثم ركع ونوى السجدة لم تجز، وكذا إذا نواها في السجدة الصلبية لأنها صارت ديناً والدين يقضي بماله لا بما عليه. وأما بيان من تجب عليه فكل من كان أهلاً لوجوب الصلاة عليه إما أداء أو قضاء فهو من أهل وجوب السجدة عليه ومن لا فلا، لأن السجدة جزء من أجزاء الصلاة فيشترط لوجوبها أهلية وجوب الصلاة من الإسلام والعقل والبلوغ والطهارة من الحيض والنفاس حتى لا تجب على كافر وصبي ومجنون وحائض ونفساء، قرؤا أو سمعوا. وتجب على المحدث والجنب، وكذا تجب على السامع بتلاوة هؤلاء إلا المجنون لعدم أهليته لانعدام التمييز كالسماع من الصدى.
His statement: 'Then it is wajib with delay.' Al-'Inayah said: So whoever prostrated, it is performance (ada') not make-up (qada'), and that is according to Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifah, and according to Abu Yusuf and another narration from Abu Hanifah, its obligation is immediate. End quote. And in al-Durar it is reported from al-Khaniyyah that it invalidates based on the manifest answer unanimously, except that there is no wudu' upon him due to laughter, and similarly a woman's alignment does not invalidate it as in the funeral prayer, and if he sleeps in it his purification is not broken like the obligatory [prayer] according to the correct view, and the rest of its rulings will come. As for what is recited in prayer, it is obligatory on an immediate basis due to the evidence of immediacy, which is that it became obligatory through something that is an act of prayer, namely recitation, so it attaches to its statements and becomes a part of its parts. For this reason we say: if one recites a sajdah verse and does not prostrate and does not bow until the recitation, then bows and intends the sajdah, it is not valid; and likewise if he intends it in the obligatory prostration because it becomes a debt, and a debt is paid with what is like it not with what is not. As for the explanation of who it is obligatory upon: everyone who is eligible for the obligation of prayer either in performance or make-up, he is from among the people upon whom the sajdah is obligatory, and whoever is not, then not, because the sajdah is a part of the parts of prayer, so for its obligation the eligibility for the obligation of prayer is required: Islam, sanity, maturity, purity from menstruation and postpartum bleeding. Thus it is not obligatory upon a disbeliever, child, insane person, menstruating woman, or woman in postpartum, whether they recite or hear. And it is obligatory upon one in minor impurity and in major impurity, and likewise it is obligatory upon the hearer due to the recitation of these, except the insane for lacking eligibility due to absence of discernment, like hearing from an echo. End quote from al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers two related issues: the time of obligation for sajdah al-tilawah and who is obligated. First, it discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the obligation is immediate (faur) or delayed (tarakhi). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani and one narration from Abu Hanifah, it is delayed, so if one prostrates later it counts as ada' (performance), not qada'. According to Abu Yusuf and another narration from Abu Hanifah, it is immediate. The relied-upon position is that outside prayer it is delayed, as implied by the earlier ruling. Then the passage clarifies that when recited in prayer, the sajdah is immediate (tadyiq) because it becomes part of the prayer, so delaying it until after the prayer is not allowed; if one delays and then bows or prostrates in the obligatory sajdah, it does not count. It becomes like a debt that must be paid in kind. Second, the passage explains who is obligated: anyone who is obligated for prayer (muslim, sane, mature, free from menstruation and postpartum) is obligated for sajdah al-tilawah. Thus it is not obligatory on a disbeliever, child, insane person, or woman in menses/postpartum. However, it is obligatory on a person in minor impurity (hadath) or major impurity (janabah). The hearer is also obligated, except if the reciter is insane because then the recitation is meaningless. This is based on the principle that sajdah al-tilawah is a part of prayer and shares its conditions of obligation.

Key Terms
التراخي (al-tarākhī): Delaying the performance of a wajib act beyond its immediate time without sin, as the obligation is broad (muwassa').
التضييق (al-taḍyīq): Immediacy; the obligation must be performed at the soonest opportunity; delaying incurs sin.
أهلية وجوب الصلاة (ahliyyat wujūb al-ṣalāh): The capacity to be obligated for prayer: being Muslim, sane, mature, and free from menstrual/postpartum bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When recited in prayer
B) When recited outside prayer
C) Always, regardless of context
D) Never, it is always immediate

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib: delayed outside prayer, immediate in prayer; eligibility equals that of prayer, and the hearer is obligated if the reciter is a sane Muslim.

Immediate Obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah in Prayer
Contrasting expanded obligation outside prayer with immediate obligation inside prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sujud al-tilawah in prayer is immediately obligatory and apply the qiyas of debt to explain why it cannot be compensated by ruku' or sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah in prayer becomes a debt that must be paid with its like — a separate sujud.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi distinction between expanded obligations (muwassa') and immediate obligations (muwayyaq). While most acts of worship can be performed any time within their window, the sujud al-tilawah recited during prayer becomes tightly bound to the prayer itself. The source text uses a powerful analogy: once delayed, the missed prostration becomes a debt that can only be repaid with its precise equivalent, not with a bow or another prostration. Understanding this principle will prevent common errors in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts
Recognize that sujud al-tilawah outside prayer is muwassa' (expanded), while inside prayer it becomes muwayyaq (immediate). The difference hinges on the act of recitation being part of prayer.
Consider the phrase 'وجبت بما هو من أفعال الصلاة' — it became obligatory through something that is an act of prayer.
2
Understand the Hanafi principle of tadyiq vs tus'ah
Most obligations (e.g., zakat, fasting) are muwassa' — you can delay them within their time. But sujud al-tilawah in prayer is an exception: its obligation tightens immediately upon recitation.
The text compares it to the last part of one's life, when even muwassa' obligations become immediate.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The sujud al-tilawah becomes part of the prayer's utterances (أقوالها) and thus part of its parts (أجزائها). Therefore it shares the immediacy of prayer acts.
The evidence is intrinsic: the recitation triggers an immediate response within the same act of worship.
4
Apply the qiyas of debt (dayn)
Once the sujud is delayed, it becomes a debt (dayn). A debt must be repaid with its exact like — not with ruku' or another prostration. This explains why substituting is invalid.
The text says: 'صار ديناً والدين يقضي بماله لا بما عليه' — it became a debt, and a debt is repaid with its like, not with something else.
5
Derive practical consequences
If one recites a sujud verse and then bows (ruku') intending that sujud, the bow does not fulfill the obligation. Similarly, intending it in the obligatory prostration of prayer is insufficient.
The only valid options: perform sujud immediately after recitation (before next action), or if delayed, perform it before the end of prayer (before salam) or qada after prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما طالت جزء من الوقت غير عين ويتعين ذلك بتعيينه فعلاً وإنما يتضيق عليه الوجوب في آخر عمره في سائر الواجبات الموسعة وأما المتلوة في الصلاة فإنها تجب على سبيل التضييق لقيام دليل التضييق وهو أنها وجبت بما هو من أفعال الصلاة وهو القراءة فالتحقت بأقوالها وصارت جزءاً من أجزائها، ولهذا قلنا: إذا تلا آية السجدة ولم يسجد ولم يركع حتى القراءة ثم ركع ونوى السجدة لم تجز، وكذا إذا نواها في السجدة الصلبية لأنها صارت ديناً والدين يقضي بماله لا بما عليه
Just as it [the obligation] lasts for a part of time without being specified, and it becomes specified by actually specifying it, but the obligation becomes restricted in the last part of one's life for all expanded obligations. As for the [verse] recited in prayer, it is obligatory on an immediate basis due to the evidence of immediacy, which is that it became obligatory through something that is an act of prayer, namely recitation, so it joins the utterances of prayer and becomes a part of its parts. That is why we said: If one recites a verse of prostration and does not prostrate and does not bow until the end of recitation, then bows and intends the prostration, it is not valid. Similarly, if he intends it in the obligatory prostration, because it became a debt, and a debt is paid with its like, not with something else.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the nature of obligation of sujud al-tilawah. It distinguishes between obligations outside prayer, which are expanded over time, and the sujud al-tilawah recited during prayer, which is immediate. The proof is that since the prostration becomes part of the prayer (by being linked to recitation), it is like a debt that must be fulfilled specifically. The example given: if one recites the ayah, does not prostrate, then later in ruku' intends that prostration, it is invalid because the intent was not for the prostration of recitation at its proper time. Similarly, intending it in the obligatory prostration of prayer is insufficient because it has become a distinct obligation (like a debt) that requires its own specific action.

Key Terms
تضييق (tadyiq): The state of being immediately obligatory without delay
توسعة (tus'ah): The state of being expandable over time within a fixed period

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah in prayer is an immediate obligation; once delayed, it becomes a debt that can only be fulfilled by a separate prostration, not by substitution.

Conditions for Obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah
Listing required qualifications for sujud al-tilawah to be obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions required for sujud al-tilawah to be obligatory and distinguish those that are not conditions.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is like a part of prayer; its obligation requires the same eligibility as prayer.

Sujud al-tilawah is a wajib act when one recites or hears an ayah of sajdah. But is it always obligatory? The Hanafi school teaches that the obligation depends on the person's eligibility for prayer. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains who must perform it and who is exempt, based on the general rule that sujud is a component of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage states that sujud al-tilawah is a part (juz') of salah, so its obligation depends on the same eligibility conditions as salah.
This principle is used to derive the specific conditions.
2
List the conditions for salah obligation
From the principle, the conditions are: Islam, sanity (aqil), adulthood (baligh), and freedom from menstruation and postpartum bleeding.
These are conditions for obligation, not for validity.
3
Apply to sujud al-tilawah
Anyone lacking these conditions is not obligated, regardless of reciting or hearing. This includes disbelievers, children, the insane, menstruating women, and postpartum women.
The passage explicitly lists these exemptions.
4
Note what is NOT a condition
Purity from minor (hadath) and major (janabah) impurity is NOT a condition for obligation. A person in such states is still obligated, though they should purify before performing the sujud.
This distinguishes obligation from validity.
5
Understand the hearing rule
Hearing a sajdah verse from an eligible person obligates sujud. However, hearing from an insane person is like hearing an echo (sada) and does not obligate, due to the lack of discrimination.
The insane person's recitation has no legal effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان من تجب عليه فكل من كان أهلاً لوجوب الصلاة عليه إما أداء أو قضاء فهو من أهل وجوب السجدة عليه ومن لا فلا، لأن السجدة جزء من أجزاء الصلاة فيشترط لوجوبها أهلية وجوب الصلاة من الإسلام والعقل والبلوغ والطهارة من الحيض والنفاس حتى لا تجب على كافر وصبي ومجنون وحائض ونفساء، قرؤا أو سمعوا. وتجب على المحدث والجنب، وكذا تجب على السامع بتلاوة هؤلاء إلا المجنون لعدم أهليته لانعدام التمييز كالسماع من الصدى. كذا في البدائع
As for the explanation of who it is obligatory upon: every person who is eligible for the obligation of prayer, whether in performance or as a makeup, is eligible for the obligation of sujud [al-tilawah]; and whoever is not, is not. Because the sujud is a part of the parts of prayer, so for its obligation eligibility for the obligation of prayer is required: Islam, sanity, puberty, and purity from menstruation and postpartum bleeding. So it is not obligatory upon a disbeliever, a boy, an insane person, a menstruating woman, or a woman in postpartum bleeding, whether they recite or hear. And it is obligatory upon a person with minor impurity (hadath) and a person in major impurity (junub). Likewise, it is obligatory upon the hearer of the recitation of these [exempted persons] except the insane, due to their lack of eligibility caused by lack of discrimination, like hearing an echo (sada). It is mentioned in al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding who is obligated to perform sujud al-tilawah. The key principle is that since sujud al-tilawah is a part of prayer, the same qualifications for prayer obligation apply. Therefore, the following conditions are required: being Muslim, sane, having reached puberty, and being free from menstruation and postpartum bleeding. Thus, sujud al-tilawah is not obligatory on a disbeliever, a child, an insane person, a menstruating woman, or a woman in postpartum bleeding, regardless of whether they recite or hear the ayah. However, it is obligatory on a person with minor impurity (hadath) or major impurity (junub), as these do not negate eligibility for prayer (they can still pray after purification). Also, a listener must perform it if they hear the recitation from someone who is eligible (or even from the exempted persons except the insane), because the insane person's recitation is like an echo (sada) and does not convey legal obligation.

Key Terms
أهلية وجوب الصلاة (ahliyyat wujub al-salah): Eligibility for the obligation of prayer, which includes being Muslim, sane, adult, and free from menstrual/postpartum blood.
صدى (sada): An echo or a sound that returns from a hollow place; hearing the recitation of an insane person is likened to hearing an echo.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of sujud al-tilawah?
A) Being Muslim
B) Being sane
C) Being in a state of purity from minor and major impurity
D) Being free from menstruation and postpartum bleeding

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is only obligatory upon one who meets the same eligibility conditions as prayer: Muslim, sane, adult, and free from menstrual/postpartum blood.

Dying Person's Will and the Dislike of Delaying Sujud
Ruling on dying person's will and karahah of delaying sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a dying person must make a will for missed sujud al-tilawah and identify when delaying sujud is makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Delaying sujud outside prayer is only mildly disliked; inside prayer it is more severe.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh work al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two rulings: first, regarding a person on their deathbed (muhtadar) and whether he must make a will (wasiyyah) for any missed sujud al-tilawah; second, the general ruling on delaying the performance of sujud al-tilawah. The text resolves a dispute among Hanafi authorities, preferring the view that the dying person is not obligated to make such a will and that delaying sujud outside prayer is only makruh tanzih (mildly disliked), not makruh tahrimi (forbidden).

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
Note that the text from al-Qunyah states that it is not obligatory (la yajib) for the dying person to make a will regarding sujud al-tilawah, but a contrary view (qila) says it is obligatory. Identify the preferred view.
The phrase 'لا يجب' indicates non-obligation, and 'قيل' signals a weaker opinion.
2
Understand the second ruling on delay
From al-Tajnis, a dispute is reported: some say delaying sujud is only disliked if the recitation occurred during prayer; others (al-Tahawi) say it is disliked absolutely. The text declares al-Tahawi's view as more correct (asahh).
Al-Tahawi is a major Hanafi authority; his view carries weight.
3
Classify the karahah
The passage explains that the dislike (karahah) for delaying sujud outside prayer is tanzihiyyah (mild). It deduces this from the fact that if it were tahrimiyyah, the obligation would be immediate (fawr), which is not the case outside prayer.
This is a dalil aqli – reasoning based on the absence of immediacy.
4
Apply the distinction
Note that for sujud inside prayer, the obligation is immediate – you must do it at once. Therefore, delaying inside prayer is more severe, possibly makruh tahrimi or even requiring sujud al-sahw. Outside prayer, delay is not sinful but contrary to the better practice.
The text does not specify the ruling for inside prayer beyond stating that some said it is disliked; the more severe nature is inferred from the reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية ولا يجب على المحتضر الإيصاء بسجدة التلاوة، وقيل يجب ولا تجب نية التعيين في السجدات .اهـ. وفي التجنيس وهل يكره تأخيرها عن وقت القراءة ذكر في بعض المواضع أنه إذا قرأها في الصلاة فتأخيرها مكروه، وإن قرأها خارج الصلاة لا يكره تأخيرها وذكر الطحاوى أن تأخيرها مكروه مطلقاً الأم وهو أصح اهـ. وهي كراهة تنزيهية في غير الصلاتية لأنها لو كانت تحريمية لكان وجوبها على الفور وليس كذلك
In al-Qunyah: It is not obligatory for the dying person to make a will (wasiyyah) regarding sujud al-tilawah. And it is said (qila): It is obligatory. And resolution [niyyah] of specification is not obligatory in the prostrations. End quote. And in al-Tajnīs: Is delaying it from the time of recitation disliked? It is mentioned in some places that if he recited it in prayer, delaying it is disliked; if he recited it outside prayer, delaying it is not disliked. And al-Tahawi mentioned that delaying it is disliked absolutely; the matter (al-am) and it is more correct. End quote. And it is a disliked-without-reproach (karahah tanzihiyyah) for outside-prayer [sujud], because if it were prohibited (tahrim), its obligation would be immediate, and it is not so.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First, regarding a person on their deathbed (muhtadar): there is a disagreement (qila) whether they must make a will regarding sujud al-tilawah they owe. The preferred view is that it is not obligatory, and also no specific intention (niyyah ta'yin) is required for these prostrations. Second, the ruling on delaying sujud al-tilawah: Al-Tahawi's view, which is considered more correct, is that delaying it is disliked (makruh) in all cases, regardless of whether the recitation was in prayer or not. However, outside prayer, this karahah is tanzihiyyah (close to permissible), not tahrimiyyah. The reasoning: if it were forbiddingly disliked, that would imply the obligation is immediate, which is not the case for sujud outside prayer.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): A disliked action that is not sinful but contrary to the preferred practice
المحتضر (al-muhtadar): A person who is on their deathbed

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the dying person making a will (wasiyyah) to perform missed sujud al-tilawah?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is not obligatory; one view says it is.
C) It must be done with a specific intention.
D) It is haram to make such a will.

Key Takeaway
Delaying sujud al-tilawah outside prayer is makruh tanzih, and the dying person is not obligated to make a will for missed sujud, though it is recommended.

Disputed Sajdah Verses: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on al-Hajj and al-Fussilat
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on which verses of sajdah are included

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the second sajdah in Surah al-Hajj and the sajdah in Surah al-Fussilat, and apply the principle of ihtiyat to prefer the later verse.

Core Idea
Disputed sujud verses are resolved by ihtiyat: the later verse is safer to avoid deficiency.

The Quran contains verses of prostration (sujud al-tilawah) upon recitation or hearing. However, the four schools disagree on exactly which verses require sujud. This lesson examines the Hanafi view on two specific disputed cases: the second sajdah in Surah al-Hajj and the sajdah in Surah al-Fussilat. We will see how the Hanafi school uses ihtiyat (precaution) to resolve differences among Companions and prefer one location over another.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on each disputed verse
Identify the Hanafi ruling: only the first sajdah in al-Hajj is a place of sujud; the second is not. In Fussilat, the sajdah is at verse 38 (وهم لا يسأمون).
2
Identify the opposing views
Imam al-Shafi'i includes a second sajdah in al-Hajj and places the Fussilat sajdah at verse 37 (إن كنتم إياه تعبدون). Imam Malik excludes all sujud in al-Mufassal.
The text also mentions that Shafi'i negates sujud in Surah Sad, which is not a Hanafi sajdah.
3
Trace the Companion evidence
For the Hanafi position: Ibn Abbas and Wa'il ibn Hujr on Fussilat. For Shafi'i: Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar. No specific Companion is cited for al-Hajj second sajdah.
4
Apply the principle of ihtiyat
Precaution: if the correct sajdah is at verse 37, delaying to verse 38 still fulfills the obligation. If it is at verse 38, performing it earlier would be before the obligation exists, causing deficiency. Therefore, the later verse is safer.
This reasoning shows 'deep understanding in fiqh' as the text states.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi listener should not prostrate if a reciter makes sujud at the second sajdah of al-Hajj or at verse 37 of Fussilat. Each follows his own school.
The text emphasizes that the listener is not a follower of the reciter in this matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (منها أولى الحج وص) ذكرهما للاختلاف فيهما فقد نفى الشافعي السجود في «ص» ولم يخص الأولى من «الحج» بل قال : إن الثانية منها أيضاً فهي عنده أيضاً أربع عشرة آية. ونفى مالك السجود في المفصل، وبيان الحجج معلوم في المطولات ولسنا إلا بصدد تحرير المذهب غالباً. وفي التجنيس التالي والسامع ينظر كل واحد منهما إلى اعتقاد نفسه كالسجدة الثانية في سورة الحج ليس بموضع السجود عندنا وعند الشافعي هو موضع السجدة لأن السامع ليس بتابع للتالي تحقيقاً حتى يلزمه العمل برأيه لأن لا شركة بينهما ا هـ . ثم في سورة حم السجدة عندنا السجدة عند قوله وهم لا يسأمون [فصلت: 38] وهو مذهب عبد الله بن عباس ووائل بن حجر، وعند الشافعي عند قوله إن كنتم إياه أئمتنا تعبدون [فصلت: 37] وهو مذهب علي ومروي عن ابن مسعود وابن عمر. ورجح الأول أخذاً بالاحتياط عند اختلاف مذاهب الصحابة فإن السجدة لو وجبت عند قوله «تعبدون» فالتأخير إلى قوله لا يسأمون» لا يضر ويخرج عن الواجب، ولو وجبت عند قوله لا يسأمون» لكانت السجدة المؤداة قبله حاصلة قبل وجوبها ووجود سبب وجوبها فيوجب في الصلاة لو كانت صلاتية ولا نقص فيما قلنا أصلاً، وهذا هو أمارة التبحر في الفقه . كذا في البدائع
His statement: 'from them are the first of al-Hajj and Sad' – he mentioned them due to disagreement concerning them. Al-Shafi'i negated sujud in 'Sad' and did not specify the first from 'al-Hajj'; rather, he said: the second from it also is [a sajdah], so according to him there are fourteen verses. And Malik negated sujud in al-Mufassal. The explanation of the proofs is known in lengthy works, and we are only concerned with establishing the school mostly. And in al-Tajnis: The reciter and the listener each looks to his own belief, like the second sajdah in Surah al-Hajj: According to us it is not a place of sajdah, while according to al-Shafi'i it is a place of sajdah. Because the listener is not a follower of the reciter in reality so that he would be bound to act by his opinion, since there is no partnership between them. End quote. Then in Surah Ha Mim as-Sajdah: According to us the sajdah is at His statement: 'and they do not get weary' [Fussilat 38], and this is the madhhab of Abdullah ibn Abbas and Wa'il ibn Hujr. According to al-Shafi'i it is at His statement: 'If you worship them' [Fussilat 37], and this is the madhhab of Ali and narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. The first is preferred by way of precaution (ihtiyat) when the madhahib of the Companions differ. For if the sajdah were obligatory at the verse 'you worship', then delaying it to the verse 'they do not get weary' does not harm and fulfills the obligation. And if it were obligatory at 'they do not get weary', then a sajdah performed before it would occur before the obligation and the existence of its cause, which would cause a deficiency in prayer if it were a prayer prostration, and there is no deficiency in what we said at all. This is a sign of deep understanding in fiqh. So in al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding which verses of the Quran require sujud al-tilawah. The Hanafi school, based on the matn, specifies certain verses, including the first sajdah in Surah al-Hajj and the sajdah in Surah Sad. The text mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i differs: he includes a sajdah in Surah Sad (the Hanafi position excludes it) and also considers the second sajdah in Surah al-Hajj as a prostration, making a total of fourteen. Imam Malik excludes all prostrations in al-Mufassal (the later short surahs). The Hanafi position on the second sajdah in al-Hajj is that it is not a place of sajdah, and a listener follows his own school not the reciter's. Then the text focuses on the sajdah in Surah Fussilat: Hanafis place it at verse 38 ('and they do not get weary'), following Ibn Abbas and Wa'il ibn Hujr; while Shafi'i places it at verse 37 ('if you worship them'), following Ali and others. The Hanafi argument prefers the first location using ihtiyat (precaution): if the correct location is the earlier verse, performing sujud at the later verse still fulfills the obligation (since it includes the earlier part of the recitation); but if the correct location is the later verse, performing sujud at the earlier verse would be before the obligation exists, causing a deficiency. Thus, to be safe, they delay to the later verse. This shows meticulous legal reasoning.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing certain Quranic verses
احتياط (ihtiyat): Legal precaution to ensure fulfillment of obligation when evidence is unclear

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the sajdah in Surah Fussilat (Ha Mim Sajdah)?
A) At verse 37 (إن كنتم إياه تعبدون)
B) At verse 38 (وهم لا يسأمون)
C) There is no sajdah in this surah
D) Both verses are places of sajdah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies ihtiyat to prefer the later verse in disputed sujud locations, avoiding deficiency.

The Three Causes of Sujud al-Tilawah
Explaining the three causes: recitation, hearing, and following an imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes of sujud al-tilawah and identify the conditions for obligation.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah becomes wajib by reciting, hearing, or following an imam — each is an independent cause.

Sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) is an act of worship that becomes obligatory under specific circumstances. This lesson identifies the three causes that trigger the obligation, based on the Hanafi school. Understanding these causes is essential for proper practice in prayer and when reciting the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes
The passage explicitly names three causes: tilawah (recitation by oneself), sama' (hearing recitation from another), and iqtida' (following an imam who recites). List each with a brief definition.
Note: 'tilawah' includes even if the reciter is deaf and does not hear his own recitation.
2
Understand the condition for obligation
The reciter or hearer must be eligible for prayer (Muslim, sane, adult, not in a state of major impurity or menstruation/postpartum). Without these, sujud is not obligatory.
This condition applies to all three causes.
3
Distinguish the cause for a follower
For a follower in congregational prayer, the cause is iqtida' (following the imam), not hearing. Even if the follower does not hear the imam's recitation (e.g., in a silent prayer), they must prostrate because they follow the imam.
This corrects a possible misinterpretation of the matn.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider: A deaf person recites an ayah of sajdah. Does sujud become wajib? Yes, because the cause is tilawah, not hearing.
This highlights that each cause operates independently.
5
Summarize the ruling
In summary, sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon anyone who recites an ayah of sajdah (even if deaf), anyone who hears such recitation (even unintentionally), and any follower whose imam recites such an ayah (even if the follower does not hear).
The passage also notes that the imam is obligated like anyone else, refuting any doubt about exemption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (على من تلا ولو إماماً أو سمع ولو غير قاصد أو مؤتماً لا بتلاوته) بيان لسببها أحد ثلاثة : التلاوة ولو لم يوجد السماع كتلاوة الأصم والسماع بتلاوة وغيره، والاقتداء بإمام تلاها وإن لم يسمع المأموم تبعاً لإمامه بأن قرأ الإمام سراً أو لم يكن حاضراً عند القراءة واقتدى به قبل أن يسجد لها، ولذا قالوا: إن الأبكم إذا رأى قوماً يسجدون لا يجب عليه السجود لأنه لم يقرأ ولم يسمع والمصنف جعل المؤتم معطوفاً على غير قاصد فأفاد أن المؤتم يلزمه بسماعه وليس كذلك، وإنما يلزمه باقتدائه وإن لم يسمع، فلو قال المصنف «أو اقتدى» معطوفاً على تلا» لكان أولى كما لا يخفي. فقد قال في المجتبى : الموجب لها أحد ثلاثة : التلاوة والسماع والائتمام وإنما قال ولو إماماً» لما أن المنقول في البدائع أنه يكره للإمام أن يتلو آية السجدة في صلاة يخافت فيها بالقراءة فإنه لا ينفك عن مكروه من ترك السجدة إن لم يسجد أو التلبيس على القوم إن سجد ا هـ. وكذا لا ينبغي أن لا يقرأها في الجمعة والعيدين لما ذكرنا كما في السراج الوهاج فربما يتوهم من ذلك عدم وجوبها على الإمام فصرح به نفياً المصنف له، وقد قدمنا شرائط الوجوب على التالي والسامع. وصحح في الكافي أن السبب المؤتم الخ قد يقال قصد المصنف الإشارة إلى أن الإمام لا يقرؤها في السرية بل في الجهرية فجعل المؤثم سامعاً لأن الغالب سماع الجهر وإن لم يكن سماعه لها شرطاً
His statement: 'upon whoever recites, even if he is an imam, or hears, even if unintentionally, or is a follower without his recitation' – explanation: its causes are three: recitation even if hearing does not occur, like the recitation of the deaf; hearing recitation and other than it; and following an imam who recited it even if the follower did not hear, following his imam, such as if the imam recited silently or the follower was not present at the recitation and followed him before he prostrated for it. That is why they said: If a mute person sees people prostrating, sujud is not obligatory on him because he did not recite nor hear. And the author [of Kanz] made 'follower' conjoined to 'unintentional', so it implies that the follower is obligated by his hearing, but that is not so; rather, he is obligated by his following (iqtida) even if he did not hear. So if the author had said 'or followed' conjoined to 'recitation', it would have been better, as is not hidden. For it is stated in al-Mujtaba: The causes are three: recitation, hearing, and following. And he said 'even if he is an imam' because it is transmitted in al-Bada'i' that it is disliked for an imam to recite an ayah of sajdah in a prayer where he recites silently, for he cannot avoid either the dislikedness of leaving the sujud if he does not prostrate or causing confusion among the people if he prostrates. End quote. Similarly, he should not recite it in Friday and Eid prayers because of what we mentioned, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, lest it be thought that it is not obligatory upon the imam, so the author explicitly negated that. And we have already presented the conditions of obligation for the reciter and the hearer. And it is corrected in al-Kafi that the cause [for the follower]... It may be said that the author intended to indicate that the imam does not recite it in silent prayers but in loud prayers, so he made the follower a hearer because loud prayers are generally heard, even if hearing it is not a condition.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the causes that make sujud al-tilawah obligatory. The author lists three causes: (1) Recitation (tilawah) by oneself, even if one cannot hear (like a deaf person); (2) Hearing (sama') someone else's recitation, whether one intended to listen or not; (3) Following an imam (iqtida') in congregational prayer when the imam recites an ayah of sajdah, even if the follower did not hear the recitation. The commentary critiques the matn's phrasing, which conjoined 'follower' (mu'tam) to 'unintentional' (ghayr qa'sid) in the phrase 'or hears unintentionally or is a follower'. This suggests that the follower's obligation is due to hearing, but actually it is due to following the imam, not hearing. The author of Kanz should have said 'or follows' as a separate cause. The commentary also addresses the imam's situation: it is disliked for an imam to recite an ayah of sajdah in silent prayers (like zuhr, asr) because either he would omit the sujud (which is disliked) or cause confusion by prostrating in a silent prayer. Similarly, in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, it is better not to recite such verses to avoid confusion. However, the matn explicitly states that the imam is still obligated if he recites it, to counter any misconception that the imam is exempt. The passage ends with a discussion about the silent vs. loud distinction.

Key Terms
ائتمام (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer
صلاة سرية (salat sirriyyah): A prayer in which the imam recites silently (zuhr, asr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a cause that makes sujud al-tilawah obligatory?
A) Reciting an ayah of sajdah
B) Hearing an ayah of sajdah from someone else
C) Seeing people prostrating
D) Following an imam who recites an ayah of sajdah

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah becomes wajib by reciting, hearing, or following an imam; each cause is sufficient on its own.
