The Follower's Obligation: Following vs Hearing
Correcting the misconception that hearing is the cause for a follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a follower's obligation for sujud al-tilawah is based on iqtida' (following), not hearing, and evaluate the matn's phrasing.

Core Idea
A follower in prayer must prostrate even without hearing the ayah — the bond of iqtida' transfers the obligation.

This lesson delves into a precise point of Hanafi fiqh: the cause of obligation for a follower (mu'tam) in congregational prayer when the imam recites an ayah of sajdah. The commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies a potential misunderstanding arising from the matn's wording and emphasizes that iqtida' (following) is an independent cause, not dependent on hearing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue in the matn
The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq says: 'or hears unintentionally or is a follower without his recitation'. By conjoining 'follower' to 'unintentional', it implies the follower's obligation is due to hearing. The commentary points out this is incorrect.
The commentator suggests the matn should have said 'or follows' as a separate cause.
2
State the correct Hanafi position
The correct position, as stated in al-Mujtaba and supported by the commentator, is that the causes are three: recitation, hearing, and following. The follower is obligated by virtue of following (iqtida'), not by hearing.
Even if the follower didn't hear (e.g., silent prayer), the obligation stands.
3
Understand the rationale
The obligation transfers from the imam to the follower because of the connection of iqtida'. The imam's recitation triggers the obligation for the follower, just as the imam's actions in prayer are followed.
This is analogous to other acts that the follower performs behind the imam without hearing directly.
4
Consider the imam's situation
The passage also notes that it is disliked (makruh) for an imam to recite an ayah of sajdah in silent prayers, due to potential confusion. However, if he does, the follower must still prostrate because iqtida' is the cause.
This shows that the cause of obligation remains even when the imam's action is disliked.
5
Apply the distinction
If a follower is in a loud prayer and hears the imam recite the ayah, the obligation arises from both hearing and following. But if he doesn't hear (e.g., due to noise), the obligation still holds because of following.
The commentator suggests that the author of Kanz made the follower a 'hearer' because in loud prayers hearing is the norm, but that is not the actual legal cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (على من تلا ولو إماماً أو سمع ولو غير قاصد أو مؤتماً لا بتلاوته) بيان لسببها أحد ثلاثة : التلاوة ولو لم يوجد السماع كتلاوة الأصم والسماع بتلاوة وغيره، والاقتداء بإمام تلاها وإن لم يسمع المأموم تبعاً لإمامه بأن قرأ الإمام سراً أو لم يكن حاضراً عند القراءة واقتدى به قبل أن يسجد لها، ولذا قالوا: إن الأبكم إذا رأى قوماً يسجدون لا يجب عليه السجود لأنه لم يقرأ ولم يسمع والمصنف جعل المؤتم معطوفاً على غير قاصد فأفاد أن المؤتم يلزمه بسماعه وليس كذلك، وإنما يلزمه باقتدائه وإن لم يسمع، فلو قال المصنف «أو اقتدى» معطوفاً على تلا» لكان أولى كما لا يخفي. فقد قال في المجتبى : الموجب لها أحد ثلاثة : التلاوة والسماع والائتمام وإنما قال ولو إماماً» لما أن المنقول في البدائع أنه يكره للإمام أن يتلو آية السجدة في صلاة يخافت فيها بالقراءة فإنه لا ينفك عن مكروه من ترك السجدة إن لم يسجد أو التلبيس على القوم إن سجد ا هـ. وكذا لا ينبغي أن لا يقرأها في الجمعة والعيدين لما ذكرنا كما في السراج الوهاج فربما يتوهم من ذلك عدم وجوبها على الإمام فصرح به نفياً المصنف له، وقد قدمنا شرائط الوجوب على التالي والسامع. وصحح في الكافي أن السبب المؤتم الخ قد يقال قصد المصنف الإشارة إلى أن الإمام لا يقرؤها في السرية بل في الجهرية فجعل المؤثم سامعاً لأن الغالب سماع الجهر وإن لم يكن سماعه لها شرطاً
His statement: 'upon whoever recites, even if he is an imam, or hears, even if unintentionally, or is a follower without his recitation' – explanation: its causes are three: recitation even if hearing does not occur, like the recitation of the deaf; hearing recitation and other than it; and following an imam who recited it even if the follower did not hear, following his imam, such as if the imam recited silently or the follower was not present at the recitation and followed him before he prostrated for it. That is why they said: If a mute person sees people prostrating, sujud is not obligatory on him because he did not recite nor hear. And the author [of Kanz] made 'follower' conjoined to 'unintentional', so it implies that the follower is obligated by his hearing, but that is not so; rather, he is obligated by his following (iqtida) even if he did not hear. So if the author had said 'or followed' conjoined to 'recitation', it would have been better, as is not hidden. For it is stated in al-Mujtaba: The causes are three: recitation, hearing, and following. And he said 'even if he is an imam' because it is transmitted in al-Bada'i' that it is disliked for an imam to recite an ayah of sajdah in a prayer where he recites silently, for he cannot avoid either the dislikedness of leaving the sujud if he does not prostrate or causing confusion among the people if he prostrates. End quote. Similarly, he should not recite it in Friday and Eid prayers because of what we mentioned, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, lest it be thought that it is not obligatory upon the imam, so the author explicitly negated that. And we have already presented the conditions of obligation for the reciter and the hearer. And it is corrected in al-Kafi that the cause [for the follower]... It may be said that the author intended to indicate that the imam does not recite it in silent prayers but in loud prayers, so he made the follower a hearer because loud prayers are generally heard, even if hearing it is not a condition.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the causes that make sujud al-tilawah obligatory. The author lists three causes: (1) Recitation (tilawah) by oneself, even if one cannot hear (like a deaf person); (2) Hearing (sama') someone else's recitation, whether one intended to listen or not; (3) Following an imam (iqtida') in congregational prayer when the imam recites an ayah of sajdah, even if the follower did not hear the recitation. The commentary critiques the matn's phrasing, which conjoined 'follower' (mu'tam) to 'unintentional' (ghayr qa'sid) in the phrase 'or hears unintentionally or is a follower'. This suggests that the follower's obligation is due to hearing, but actually it is due to following the imam, not hearing. The author of Kanz should have said 'or follows' as a separate cause. The commentary also addresses the imam's situation: it is disliked for an imam to recite an ayah of sajdah in silent prayers (like zuhr, asr) because either he would omit the sujud (which is disliked) or cause confusion by prostrating in a silent prayer. Similarly, in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, it is better not to recite such verses to avoid confusion. However, the matn explicitly states that the imam is still obligated if he recites it, to counter any misconception that the imam is exempt. The passage ends with a discussion about the silent vs. loud distinction.

Key Terms
ائتمام (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, what is the correct cause of obligation for a follower to perform sujud al-tilawah?
A) Hearing the imam's recitation
B) Seeing the imam prostrate
C) Following the imam (iqtida')
D) Reciting the ayah oneself

Key Takeaway
The follower's obligation for sujud al-tilawah is based on iqtida' (following), not on hearing the recitation.

Disputed Sajdah Verses: The Hanafi Position on Surah Sad, Hajj, and Fussilat
Inter-madhhab dispute analysis of three sajdah verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the disputed sajdah verses in Surah Sad, Hajj, and Fussilat, and explain the principle of ihtiyat used to resolve the disagreement.

Core Idea
When Companions differ on a sajdah verse, Hanafis choose the later verse to avoid premature prostration — that is ihtiyat.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses three disputed sajdah verses. The Hanafi school holds that there is no sajdah in Surah Sad, only one sajdah in Surah Hajj (the first), and the sajdah in Surah Fussilat is at verse 38. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools disagree. The author focuses on the Fussilat dispute to demonstrate the Hanafi method of tarjih using ihtiyat when Companion testimonies conflict. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed verses
List the three verses (Sad, Hajj, Fussilat) and note the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki positions for each.
The passage mentions that Shafi'i considers the second verse of Hajj also a sajdah, and Malik negates sajdah in al-Mufassal entirely.
2
Map the Companion testimonies
For Fussilat, identify which Companions support each side: Ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hajar for verse 38 (Hanafi); Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar for verse 37 (Shafi'i).
3
Apply ihtiyat
Analyze the precautionary reasoning: if the sajdah is at verse 38, delaying from 37 does no harm; if at 37, performing at 38 is late but valid; but performing at 37 when it's not a sajdah would be invalid. Thus the later verse is safer.
The author calls this 'a sign of deep understanding in fiqh'.
4
Derive the practical difference
State the thamarah al-khilaf: in Fussilat, Hanafis prostrate at verse 38, Shafi'is at verse 37. Also note the ruling for a listener following a reciter from a different madhhab.
The passage cites al-Tajnis: the listener is not bound to follow the reciter's opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة قوله : (منها أولى الحج وص) ذكرهما للاختلاف فيهما فقد نفى الشافعي السجود في «ص» ولم يخص الأولى من «الحج» بل قال : إن الثانية منها أيضاً فهي عنده أيضاً أربع عشرة آية. ونفى مالك السجود في المفصل، وبيان الحجج معلوم في المطولات ولسنا إلا بصدد تحرير المذهب غالباً. وفي التجنيس التالي والسامع ينظر كل واحد منهما إلى اعتقاد نفسه كالسجدة الثانية في سورة الحج ليس بموضع السجود عندنا وعند الشافعي هو موضع السجدة لأن السامع ليس بتابع للتالي تحقيقاً حتى يلزمه العمل برأيه لأن لا شركة بينهما ا هـ . ثم في سورة حم السجدة عندنا السجدة عند قوله وهم لا يسأمون [فصلت: 38] وهو مذهب عبد الله بن عباس ووائل بن حجر، وعند الشافعي عند قوله إن كنتم إياه أئمتنا تعبدون [فصلت: 37] وهو مذهب علي ومروي عن ابن مسعود وابن عمر. ورجح الأول أخذاً بالاحتياط عند اختلاف مذاهب الصحابة فإن السجدة لو وجبت عند قوله «تعبدون» فالتأخير إلى قوله لا يسأمون» لا يضر ويخرج عن الواجب، ولو وجبت عند قوله لا يسأمون» لكانت السجدة المؤداة قبله حاصلة قبل وجوبها ووجود سبب وجوبها فيوجب في الصلاة لو كانت صلاتية ولا نقص فيما قلنا أصلاً، وهذا هو أمارة التبحر في الفقه. كذا في البدائع .
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. His saying: (Among them is the first of al-Hajj and Sad). He mentioned them due to disagreement about them. Al-Shafi'i negated prostration in 'Sad' and did not specify the first from 'al-Hajj' but said that the second of it is also (a prostration), so according to him they are also fourteen verses. Malik negated prostration in al-Mufassal. The explanation of the proofs is known in lengthy works, and we are only concerned with editing the madhhab mostly. And in al-Tajnis: the follower and the listener each look to his own belief, like the second prostration in Surah al-Hajj is not a place of prostration according to us, and according to al-Shafi'i it is a place of prostration because the listener is not truly a follower of the reciter such that he is bound to act according to his opinion, because there is no partnership between them. End quote. Then in Surah Ha Mim, the prostration according to us is at His saying 'and they do not become weary' (Fussilat 38), which is the madhhab of Abdullah ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hajar. According to al-Shafi'i, it is at His saying 'if it is Him you worship' (Fussilat 37), which is the madhhab of Ali and narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. He preferred the first, adopting precaution (ihtiyat) when the madhhabs of the Companions differ. For if the prostration were obligatory at His saying 'you worship', then delaying it to His saying 'do not become weary' does no harm and he exits from the obligation. And if it were obligatory at His saying 'do not become weary', then the prostration performed before it would have occurred before its obligation and the existence of its cause, which would necessitate (a problem) in prayer if it were a prayer prostration, and there is no deficiency in what we said at all. This is a sign of deep understanding in fiqh. Thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author explains the basis for disagreement on the prostration verses in Surah Sad, Surah Hajj, and Surah Fussilat. Against Shafi'i, the Hanafis hold that there is no prostration in Surah Sad and only one in Surah Hajj (the first). Against Malik, prostration is affirmed in al-Mufassal (the latter part of the Quran). The author then focuses on the dispute about Surah Fussilat (Ha Mim). The Hanafi position, traced to Ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hajar, places the prostration at verse 38 ('and they do not become weary'). The Shafi'i position, traced to Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar, places it at verse 37 ('if it is Him you worship'). The Hanafi tarjih (preference) is based on the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) when the Companions differ: if the correct location is later, one can delay and still be valid; if it is earlier, performing it earlier would be premature and potentially invalid if the earlier verse is not a prostration. The author calls this a sign of deep fiqh understanding.

Key Terms
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): The principle of choosing the more cautious ruling when evidence conflicts, here applied to the timing of sajdah.
المفصل (al-mufassal): The latter part of the Quran, typically from Surah Qaf or Hujurat to the end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis place the prostration in Surah Fussilat at verse 38 rather than verse 37?
A) Because the first verse does not contain the word 'sajdah'.
B) Because of the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) to avoid performing prostration before its obligation.
C) Because Abu Hanifa alone ruled so, without evidence.
D) Because verse 38 has a stronger chain of transmission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses ihtiyat (precaution) to resolve Companion disagreements on sajdah verses, choosing the later verse to avoid risk of invalid prostration.

Causes of Sajdah al-Tilawah: Recitation, Listening, Following
Explains the three causes for sajdah and conditions for obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes of sajdah al-tilawah and explain why the follower's own recitation does not create an obligation.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah becomes wajib by recitation, hearing, or following an imam—but the follower's own recitation is legally inert due to hajr.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks the author's concise statement on the causes that obligate sajdah al-tilawah. You will learn the three causes: recitation (even if unheard), hearing (even if unintentional), and following an imam (even if the follower did not hear the verse). A key nuance is that the follower's own recitation of a prostration verse has no legal effect, because the follower is under restriction (hajr) from recitation. Understanding this principle prevents confusion about when prostration is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes
Locate in the text the three causes: recitation (tilawah), hearing (sama'), and following (iqtida'). Notice that recitation obligates even if unheard (e.g., a deaf person), and hearing obligates even if unintentional.
The author says 'even if an imam' to affirm that the imam is also obligated.
2
Distinguish reciter vs listener obligations
For the reciter, obligation is absolute (whether understood or not). For the listener, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa requires being informed it is a prostration verse; the two companions require knowing the reciter is reciting Quran. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) follows the companions.
Persian recitation is a special case: if considered Quran, obligation is absolute; if not, it doesn't obligate the listener.
3
Analyse the follower's case
The follower (mu'tam) is obligated to prostrate when the imam recites a prostration verse, even if the follower did not hear it. However, if the follower himself recites a prostration verse, his recitation has no effect due to hajr (restriction). Thus, neither he nor anyone who hears him is obligated.
This is a distinct Hanafi position: the follower's recitation is like that of a minor under guardianship.
4
Note intra-Hanafi disputes
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that if the follower recites a prostration verse, he should prostrate after the prayer. Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa disagree, and the relied-upon position is no obligation. Also, Muhammad's view on the listener's knowledge differs from Abu Hanifa's.
The text notes that Abu Hanifa reportedly returned to the companions' view on the listener's condition.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling for fatwa is: (1) The follower's own recitation does not obligate sajdah for himself or others; (2) For the listener, obligation arises if he knows the reciter is reciting Quran, not necessarily that it is a prostration verse. This is based on the companions' view and confirmed by later authorities like al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
This is from zahir al-riwayah and is the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وقال محمد: يسجدونها إذا فرغوا لأن السبب قد تقرر ولا مانع بخلاف حالة الصلاة لأنه يؤدي إلى خلاف موضوع الإمامة لو تابعه الإمام أو التلاوة لو تابعه المؤثم ولهما : إن المقتدي محجور عن القراءة لنفاذ تصرف الصلاة لأنه قد ثبت من أصولنا أن تصرف المحجور لا حكم له ا هـ. وهو لأن تصرف المحجور لغيره صحيح كالصبي إذا حجر عليه يظهر في حقه لا في حق غيره حتى يصح تصرفه لغيره. وذكر الشارح ولو تلا آية السجدة في الركوع أو السجود أو الخانية قوله : (وسنحققه) قال الرملي : لم يذكر فيما يأتي شيئاً من التحقيق في هذه المسألة سوى قوله في شرح قوله كمن كررها في صورة ما إذا اختلف مجلس التالي دون السامع الأصح أنه لا يتكرر على السامع لأن السبب في حقه السماع ولم يتبدل مجلسه فيه قوله: (وفي السامع عند أبي حنيفة الخ) هذا الخلاف في سماع التلاوة بالفارسية، وأما بالعربية فذكر في النهر أنه لا يشترط الفهم بالإجماع لكن لا يجب على الأعجمي ما لم يعلم كذا في الفتح، وعبارته في الخلاصة : لكن يعذر في التأخير ما لم يعلم بها قوله : (وعندهما إن كان السامع يعلم) قال في النهر : والأصح عدمه احتياطاً كذا في المحيط إلا أنه في السراج حكى رجوع الإمام إلى قولهما قال : وعليه الاعتماد قوله: (ولا على السامع منه) في إطلاقه السامع إيهام والأحسن عبارة الزيلعي حيث قال : أي لا يجب بتلاوة المقتدي عليه ولا على من سمعه من المصلين بصلاة إمامه ا هـ .
His saying: (Upon one who recites, even if an imam, or hears, even if unintentionally, or follows [an imam], not due to his own recitation). Explanation of its cause is one of three: recitation even if there is no hearing, like the recitation of a deaf person; hearing a recitation or other; and following an imam who recited it even if the follower did not hear it, following his imam, such as when the imam recited silently or the follower was not present at the recitation and followed before he prostrated for it. Hence they said: if a mute person sees people prostrating, prostration is not obligatory upon him because he did not recite nor hear. The author made 'follower' conjuncted to 'unintentional', so it indicates that the follower is obliged by his hearing, which is not so; rather he is obliged by his following even if he did not hear. So if the author had said 'or followed' conjoined to 'recited', it would have been better, as is not hidden. For it is stated in al-Mujtaba: its obligator is one of three: recitation, hearing, and following. And he said 'even if an imam' because it is narrated in al-Bada'i that it is disliked for an imam to recite a verse of prostration in a prayer where he recites silently, for he is not free from dislike: either leaving the prostration if he does not prostrate, or confusing the people if he prostrates. Similarly, he should not recite it in Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers, as mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, lest one might mistakenly think it is not obligatory upon the imam. So the author explicitly negated that. We have already presented the conditions of obligation upon the reciter and listener. And it is corrected in al-Kafi that the cause for the follower... may say that the author intended to indicate that the imam does not recite it in silent prayers but only in loud prayers, so he made the follower a listener because the norm is to hear aloud, even if his hearing of it is not a condition. His saying: (because what is narrated in al-Bada'i...) He said in al-Nahr: the absolute dislike in silent prayer is restricted to when the prostration is not at the end of the surah, as in... unintentionally or a follower not due to his recitation, and if a person in prayer hears it from someone else, he prostrates after the prayer even if he prostrates. For the listener, recitation and hearing are conditions, and we will verify it later, God willing. He made absolute in recitation and hearing, so it includes when the recitation is in Arabic or Persian, and for the reciter it is by consensus whether he understood or not. For the listener, according to Abu Hanifa after he is informed that it is a verse of prostration; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if the listener knows that he is reciting the Quran, then prostration is obligatory, otherwise not. And in al-Bada'i, this is not sound because if they consider Persian as Quran, obligation would be absolute like Arabic; if they do not consider it Quran, it would not be obligatory even if understood. He made absolute in hearing, so it includes the hearer from whom prayer is obligatory or not, except the insane as we presented, and likewise a bird on the chosen opinion. If one hears it from a sleeping person, they differed, and the correct is obligation. Thus in al-Khaniya. And in Sharh al-Majma': if a drunk person recites it, it is obligatory upon him and upon the one who hears it from him because his intellect is considered intact as a deterrent. And he indicated by his saying 'not due to his recitation' that it is not obligatory upon the follower due to his own recitation, nor upon the one who hears from him. He made it absolute, so it includes not prostrating during prayer and after finishing according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad said: they prostrate when they finish because the cause is established and there is no obstacle, unlike the state of prayer because it would lead to contravening the nature of imamate if the imam follows him or the recitation if the follower follows. And for them: the follower is prevented from recitation due to the imam's authority over him, and the action of one under restriction has no legal effect, unlike the junub and menstruating woman because they are prohibited from recitation, except that it is not obligatory upon the menstruating woman by her recitation just as it is not obligatory by hearing it due to lack of capacity for prayer, unlike the junub. It also includes one who hears it from the follower while not in prayer, which is the saying of some. And it is corrected in al-Hidayah that obligation is established because the restriction (hajr) is established in their right, so it does not extend beyond them. And it was objected to in Ghayat al-Bayan that since it is known that this person is under restriction, it must be said that prostration is not obligatory upon the hearer outside prayer because it is established from our principles that the action of one under restriction has no legal effect. End quote. This is because the action of the restricted person is valid for others, like a minor under restriction: it appears in his right, not in the right of others, such that his action is valid for others. The commentator mentioned: and if one recites a verse of prostration in ruku' or sujud or... Al-Khaniya. His saying: (we will verify it) Al-Ramli said: he did not mention anything of verification in this issue later except his saying in the explanation of his saying 'like one who repeats it' in the case where the reciter's sitting changes but not the listener's, the correct is that it does not repeat for the listener because the cause for him is hearing and his sitting did not change. His saying: (and for the listener according to Abu Hanifa...) This disagreement is about hearing recitation in Persian. As for Arabic, it is mentioned in al-Nahr that understanding is not a condition by consensus, but it is not obligatory upon a non-Arab until he knows. Thus in al-Fath. And his expression in al-Khulasa: but he is excused for delay until he knows of it. His saying: (according to them if the listener knows) He said in al-Nahr: the correct is its non-existence (of obligation) as a precaution, thus in al-Muhit, except that in al-Siraj he narrated the return of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) to their opinion, and he said: upon it is reliance. His saying: (and not upon the listener from him) In his absolute mention of 'listener' there is ambiguity. The better expression is that of Zayla'i where he said: i.e., it is not obligatory due to the recitation of the follower upon him, nor upon one who hears from the people praying with the prayer of his imam. End quote.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the ruling on the causes of sajdah al-tilawah. The commentator explains the author's words: 'upon one who recites, even if an imam, or hears even if unintentionally, or follows [an imam] not due to his own recitation'. The three causes are recitation, hearing, and following an imam. Recitation includes silent recitation (e.g., deaf person), and hearing includes both intentional and unintentional. The follower is obliged even if he did not hear the verse, but merely follows the imam. The commentator critiques the author's wording, suggesting it would be clearer to say 'or follows' instead of making 'follower' a subcase of 'hears'. The text then discusses the dislike for an imam to recite a prostration verse in silent prayer, and the obligation remains even for the imam. The discussion extends to Persian recitation: the reciter is always obliged, but for the listener, Abu Hanifa requires that he be informed it is a prostration verse, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require that he knows the reciter is reciting Quran. The commentator notes that this difference is based on whether Persian is considered Quran. The text also covers hearing from a sleeping person, drunk reciter, and the follower's obligation. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is whether the follower's recitation counts as a cause: the follower is under restriction (hajr) from recitation, so his recitation has no legal effect. Thus, if a follower recites a prostration verse, it does not obligate him nor anyone who hears him, because his recitation is legally invalid. The well-known position (mufta bihi) is that the follower's recitation does not cause obligation. The passage ends with a note on verification promised but not fully delivered.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): A person praying behind an imam (muqtadi).
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal restriction or interdiction; here, the follower is prevented from independent recitation due to the imam's authority.
التلاوة بالفارسية (al-tilawah bil-farisiyyah): Recitation of the Quran in Persian translation, not in the original Arabic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a follower (muqtadi) recites a verse of prostration during prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The follower must prostrate immediately.
B) The follower must prostrate after the prayer.
C) The follower is not obligated to prostrate, nor is anyone who hears him.
D) The follower is obligated only if the imam also recites it.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is obligatory upon recitation, hearing, or following an imam, but the follower's own recitation does not count as a cause due to his legal restriction (hajr).

Listener's Obligation for Sujud al-Tilawah in Persian Recitation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on listener's condition for sujud with Persian recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the listener's obligation for sujud al-tilawah when the recitation is in Persian, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
For Persian recitation of ayat al-sajdah, the listener's sujud is wajib if they know it is Qur'an — not necessarily understanding the meaning.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the listener's obligation for sujud al-tilawah when the recitation is in Persian. While the reciter's obligation is unconditional, the listener's obligation depends on certain conditions, and the school has a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn). We will explore the positions, the reasoning, and the final relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two views: (1) Abu Hanifa: sujud wajib after the listener is informed that the recitation is an ayat al-sajdah. (2) Sahibayn: sujud wajib if the listener knows that the recitation is from the Qur'an, regardless of understanding Persian.
Both agree that understanding the meaning is not required.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The dispute is between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Note that the Sahibayn's view is the 'opposing' one within the school.
3
Follow the reasoning behind each view
Understand the basis: Abu Hanifa's view seems to treat Persian recitation as Qur'an, so knowledge of the fact suffices. The Sahibayn require active knowledge that the recitation is Qur'an, because Persian may not be considered Qur'an in the same way.
The author of Bada'i' criticizes the Sahibayn's position for inconsistency.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response and tarjih
Note the critique in Bada'i' and the reported return of Abu Hanifa to the Sahibayn's view. Al-Siraj states that the relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's view.
The mufta bihi is that the listener must know the recitation is Qur'an.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa's initial view, a Persian-speaking reciter would obligate sujud only if listeners are told it's an ayat al-sajdah. Under the mufta bihi view, listeners must infer from context that the recitation is Qur'an (e.g., a known Qur'an recitation session).
This affects when the obligation arises in real-world scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في التلاوة والسماع فشمل ما إذا كانت التلاوة بالعربية أو الفارسية وهو في التالي بالاتفاق فهم أو لم يفهم، وفي السامع عند أبي حنيفة بعد أن أخبر أنها آية السجدة، وعندهما إن كان السامع يعلم أنه يقرأ القرآن فعليه السجدة وإلا فلا وفي البدائع وهذا غير سديد لأنهما إن جعلا الفارسية قرآناً لزم الوجوب مطلقاً كالعربية، وإن لم يجعلاها قرآناً لم يجب وإن فهم . قوله: (وفي السامع عند أبي حنيفة الخ) هذا الخلاف في سماع التلاوة بالفارسية، وأما بالعربية فذكر في النهر أنه لا يشترط الفهم بالإجماع لكن لا يجب على الأعجمي ما لم يعلم كذا في الفتح، وعبارته في الخلاصة : لكن يعذر في التأخير ما لم يعلم بها قوله : (وعندهما إن كان السامع يعلم) قال في النهر : والأصح عدمه احتياطاً كذا في المحيط إلا أنه في السراج حكى رجوع الإمام إلى قولهما قال : وعليه الاعتماد
And [the author] made absolute in recitation and hearing, so it includes whether the recitation is in Arabic or Persian, and regarding the reciter it is agreed upon whether he understands or not, and regarding the listener according to Abu Hanifa after he has been informed that it is an ayah of sajdah, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if the listener knows that he is reciting the Qur'an then the sajdah is obligatory, otherwise not. And in Bada'i' this is not sound because if they consider Persian as Qur'an then obligation is absolute like Arabic, and if they do not consider it as Qur'an then it is not obligatory even if he understands. His statement: (And regarding the listener according to Abu Hanifa, etc.) This difference of opinion is regarding hearing the recitation in Persian; as for Arabic, it is mentioned in al-Nahr that understanding is not required by consensus, but it is not obligatory upon the non-Arab unless he knows — thus in al-Fath, and his expression in al-Khulasah: but he is excused for delay until he knows of it. His statement: (And according to them if the listener knows) — he said in al-Nahr: the correct view is its non-existence as a precaution, thus in al-Muhit, except that in al-Siraj a return of the Imam to their view is narrated, and he said: reliance is upon it.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of understanding (fahm) for the listener (sami') when the recitation of the ayat al-sajdah is in Persian. The matn states that the ruling on sujud al-tilawah applies generally to both Arabic and Persian recitations. For the reciter (tali), it is agreed (bil-ittifaq) that sujud is wajib whether he understands the meaning or not. For the listener (sami'), Abu Hanifa holds that sujud becomes wajib only after the listener is informed that it is an ayat al-sajdah (i.e., he must know the fact even if he doesn't understand the Persian words). The two companions (Sahibayn — Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that if the listener knows that the person is reciting the Qur'an (i.e., he recognizes the recitation as such), then sujud is wajib; otherwise not. The author of Bada'i' criticizes this: if the Sahibayn consider Persian recitation as Qur'an, then obligation should be absolute just like Arabic; if they do not consider it as Qur'an, then it should not be wajib even if he understands. The commentator (the sharh) clarifies that this ikhtilaf is specifically for Persian recitation; for Arabic, understanding is not required by consensus (ijma'), but an 'ajami (non-Arab) is not obligated until he knows it is an ayat al-sajdah. The comment then notes that some sources (al-Nahr) say the correct view is the non-existence of the condition of understanding (as a precaution), but al-Siraj reports that Imam Abu Hanifa returned to the view of the Sahibayn and that this is the relied-upon position (mu'tamad).

Key Terms
السامع (al-sami'): The person who hears the recitation of an ayat al-sajdah; the listener to whom the sujud obligation applies if conditions are met.
التلاوة بالفارسية (al-tilawah bi al-farisiyyah): Recitation of the Qur'an in Persian translation or transliteration; its status as Qur'an is debated affecting sujud obligations.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): The reported return of Imam Abu Hanifa from his initial view to that of the Sahibayn, making their position the relied-upon one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, when is sujud al-tilawah obligatory upon a listener who hears an ayat al-sajdah recited in Persian?
A) Only if the listener understands the meaning of the Persian recitation.
B) Only if the listener has been informed that it is an ayat al-sajdah.
C) If the listener knows that the recitation is from the Qur'an, even without understanding the meaning.
D) Always, regardless of understanding or knowledge.

Key Takeaway
For Persian recitation of ayat al-sajdah, the listener's sujud is wajib under the mufta bihi view only if the listener knows the recitation is from the Qur'an.

Sujud al-Tilawah upon Hearing a Muqtadi's Recitation: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether muqtadi's recitation obligates sujud on listeners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on sujud al-tilawah for listeners of a muqtadi's recitation, and apply the principle of hajr (restriction) to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
The muqtadi's recitation is legally restricted; thus it cannot obligate sujud on himself or others.

The performance of sujud al-tilawah is required when one recites or hears an ayat al-sajdah. However, the Hanafi school recognizes a unique exception: the recitation of a muqtadi (follower in congregational prayer) is considered under a legal restriction (hajr) because the imam's recitation overrides his own. This raises a key dispute: does such recitation obligate sujud on those who hear it, either during or after the prayer? The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores this disagreement between the founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling under dispute
The act is the recitation of an ayat al-sajdah by a muqtadi during congregational prayer. The dispute is whether this recitation obligates sujud al-tilawah on the muqtadi himself or on any listener (both during and after prayer).
The base ruling from the matn is that the muqtadi's recitation does not obligate sujud (la bi-tilawatihi).
2
State the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
According to the Sahibayn, the muqtadi is mahjur (restricted) from recitation because the imam's recitation suffices. Therefore, the muqtadi's recitation has no legal effect (hukm) and cannot obligate sujud on himself or any listener, even after prayer. This is the view indicated by 'la bi-tilawatihi' and 'and it is absolute so it includes the absence of sujud during prayer and after finishing according to them.'
3
State the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad holds that listeners must perform sujud after the prayer ends because the cause (recitation of the ayat) is established and there is no preventer after prayer, unlike during prayer where following the imam's action would conflict with the imam's role.
Muhammad's view is recorded as 'And Muhammad said: They perform sujud when they finish, because the cause has been established and there is no preventer.'
4
Analyze the reasoning: hajr (restriction) vs. prohibition (nahy)
The Sahibayn's reasoning is that the muqtadi is mahjur, meaning his recitation is legally void. This is contrasted with a junub (impure person) or menstruating woman, who are merely forbidden (manhi) from recitation but their recitation still has legal effect if done. The muqtadi's recitation, due to hajr, produces no obligation.
The passage also notes that the restricted person's action can be valid regarding others (like a minor's sale), but here the principle is applied to negate the effect on listeners.
5
Evaluate the extension to listeners outside prayer and al-Marghinani's view
The dispute extends to a listener who hears the muqtadi's recitation while not in prayer. Al-Hidayah corrects that sujud is wajib on that listener because the restriction applies only to the muqtadi, not to the listener. But Ghayat al-Bayan objects that if the muqtadi's recitation has no effect, it cannot obligate anyone. Additionally, al-Marghinani opines that if the muqtadi recites in ruku', sujud, or tashahhud, sujud is obligatory and can be performed in that posture.
This shows the depth of the intra-madhhab debate on the scope of hajr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفاد بقوله لا بتلاوته أنه لا يجب على المأموم بتلاوته ولا على السامع منه، وأطلقه فشمل عدم السجود في الصلاة وبعد الفراغ عندهما. وقال محمد: يسجدونها إذا فرغوا لأن السبب قد تقرر ولا مانع بخلاف حالة الصلاة لأنه يؤدي إلى خلاف موضوع الإمامة لو تابعه الإمام أو التلاوة لو تابعه المؤثم ولهما : إن المقتدي محجور عن القراءة لنفاذ تصرف الإمام عليه وتصرف المحجور لا حكم له بخلاف الجنب والحائض لأنهما منهيان عن القراءة إلا أنه لا يجب على الحائض بتلاوتها كما لا يجب بسماعها لانعدام أهلية الصلاة بخلاف الجنب . وشمل أيضاً من سمعها من المؤتم وليس في الصلاة وهو قول البعض، وصحح في الهداية الوجوب لأن الحجر ثبت في حقهم فلا يعدوهم. وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأنه لما علم أن هذا الشخص محجور عليه وجب عليه أن يقول بعدم وجوب السجود على السامع خارج الصلاة لأنه قد ثبت من أصولنا أن تصرف المحجور لا حكم له ا هـ. وهو لأن تصرف المحجور لغيره صحيح كالصبي إذا حجر عليه يظهر في حقه لا في حق مردود : غيره حتى يصح تصرفه لغيره. وذكر الشارح ولو تلا آية السجدة في الركوع أو السجود أو التشهد لا يلزم السجود للحجر عن القراءة فيه. قال المرغيناني وعندي أنها تجب وتتأدي فيه ا هـ. وذكر في المجتبى في الفرق بين الجنب والحائض وبين المقتدي أن القدر الذي يجب به السجدة مباح لهما على الأصح دون المقتدي .
And he [the author] benefits by his statement 'not by his recitation' that it is not obligatory upon the ma'mum (follower) by his own recitation nor upon the listener from him, and he made it absolute so it includes the absence of sujud during prayer and after finishing according to them (the Sahibayn). And Muhammad said: They perform sujud when they finish, because the cause has been established and there is no preventer, unlike the state of prayer because it leads to contradiction of the imam's position if he follows the imam, or contradiction of recitation if the muqtadi follows. And for them (the Sahibayn): The muqtadi is prevented (mahjur) from recitation because the imam's authority is effective over him, and the action of one under restriction has no legal effect, unlike the junub and menstruating woman because they are forbidden from recitation, but it is not obligatory upon the menstruating woman by her recitation just as it is not by her hearing due to lack of capacity for prayer, unlike the junub. And it also includes one who hears from the muqtadi while not in prayer, and that is the statement of some, and al-Hidayah corrected the obligation because the restriction is established with respect to them (the muqtadis) so it does not extend beyond them. But it was objected in Ghayat al-Bayan that since it is known that this person is under restriction, it must be said that sujud is not obligatory upon the listener outside prayer because it is established from our principles that the action of the restricted person has no effect. And that is because the action of the restricted person is valid with respect to others, like a minor if he is restricted, it is effective regarding him, not regarding others, until his action becomes valid for others. And the commentator mentioned: If he recites an ayat al-sajdah in ruku', sujud, or tashahhud, sujud is not necessary due to restriction from recitation in it. Al-Marghinani said: In my view it is obligatory and performed in it. And in al-Mujtaba, regarding the difference between the junub and menstruating woman and the muqtadi: the portion by which sujud becomes obligatory is permissible for them according to the most correct view, unlike the muqtadi.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage delves into the ruling on sujud al-tilawah for a muqtadi (follower in prayer) and those who hear his recitation. The matn's phrase 'la bi-tilawatihi' (not by his recitation) indicates that the muqtadi's recitation does not obligate sujud on himself nor on anyone who hears him during the prayer. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that this applies both during the prayer and after it—meaning no sujud is required even after finishing. However, Muhammad (one of the Sahibayn) has a different reported view: he says the listeners should perform sujud after the prayer because the cause (recitation of the ayat) is established and there is no preventer after prayer. The Sahibayn's objection is that the muqtadi is 'mahjur' (under restriction) regarding recitation because the imam's authority overrides his own recitation; thus the muqtadi's recitation has no legal effect (hukm) to cause sujud. They contrast this with a junub (impure person) or menstruating woman who are simply forbidden from reciting—but if they do recite, it does cause obligation (on them? Actually the text says it is not obligatory on the menstruating woman by her recitation, but it is different for the junub). The discussion then extends to a listener who hears a muqtadi's recitation while not in prayer—some say sujud is wajib on that listener, and al-Hidayah corrects that it is wajib because the restriction (hajr) applies to the muqtadi, not to the listener. However, Ghayat al-Bayan objects: if the muqtadi's recitation is that of a restricted person, it should have no effect whatsoever, so no sujud on any listener. The commentator notes that the action of a restricted person can be valid regarding others (e.g., a minor's sale is valid concerning others), but here the principle differs. Finally, the passage mentions that if a muqtadi recites an ayat al-sajdah in ruku', sujud, or tashahhud, he does not need to perform sujud (due to restriction), though al-Marghinani opines that it is obligatory and is fulfilled in that posture. A distinction is made: the junub and menstruating woman are permitted to perform sujud (if they recite) unlike the muqtadi.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who recites behind the imam; his recitation is considered under restriction (hajr) due to the imam's authority.
محجور (mahjur): Under legal restriction; specifically the muqtadi is restricted from independent recitation because the imam's recitation suffices.
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration; specifically sujud al-tilawah, a wajib act when reciting or hearing a verse of prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling on sujud al-tilawah for a person who hears a muqtadi recite an ayat al-sajdah during a congregational prayer?
A) The listener must perform sujud immediately.
B) The listener must perform sujud after the prayer ends.
C) The listener is not required to perform sujud at all, even after the prayer.
D) The listener must perform sujud only if he also heard the imam's recitation.

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi's recitation is under legal restriction (hajr), rendering it incapable of obligating sujud al-tilawah on himself or listeners, though Muhammad al-Shaybani disputes the permanence of this restriction after prayer.

Sujud al-Tilawah When Hearing from a Non-Muqtadi During Prayer
Ruling on sujud al-tilawah for a praying listener, with proofs and special cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person in prayer who hears an ayat al-sajdah from someone else, and explain why the sujud is performed after prayer and what happens if it is performed during prayer.

Core Idea
Hearing an ayat al-sajdah while in prayer obligates sujud after prayer, not during, because the recitation originates outside the prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a specific scenario: a person engaged in prayer hears an ayat al-sajdah recited by someone who is not his imam or fellow muqtadi. The ruling seems counterintuitive—why can't he prostrate immediately? The commentary unpacks the cause (sabab) and the distinction between recitation and hearing, showing the precision of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its primary ruling
Determine what the praying person must do upon hearing the ayat al-sajdah: perform sujud after the prayer, not during.
The ruling is conditional on the reciter being a non-muqtadi (not the praying person's imam or fellow follower).
2
Locate the cause (sabab) of obligation
The sabab is hearing the recitation, which occurs during prayer. However, the recitation itself occurred outside the prayer, so the sujud belongs outside.
Hanafis differentiate: the reciter's cause is tilawah (recitation); the listener's cause is sama' (hearing).
3
Understand why sujud during prayer is prohibited
Performing the sujud during prayer would introduce a non-prayer action, which is prohibited (manhiyy 'anhu) because the worshiper is obligated to continue the current pillar or transition to the next.
This prohibition does not invalidate the prayer, but the sujud performed is deficient (naqisah).
4
Determine the consequence if performed incorrectly
If someone prostrates during the prayer, the sujud must be repeated after the prayer; the prayer itself remains valid and need not be repeated.
The deficient sujud does not fulfill the obligation; the perfect sujud is performed after prayer.
5
Distinguish special cases involving the listener's own recitation
If the praying person also recites the same ayat and prostrates during prayer, no repetition is needed because his recitation is part of the prayer. If he heard first then recited, there are two narrations; the relied-upon view is no repetition.
This resolves potential conflicts between the cause of hearing and subsequent recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو سمعها المصلي من غيره سجد بعد الصلاة) لتحقق سببها وهو السماع. قيد بقوله بعد الصلاة» لأنه لا يسجدها فيها لأنها ليست بصلاتية لأن سماعه هذه السجدة ليس أفعال الصلاة فيكون إدخالها فيها منهياً عنه لأن المصلي عند اشتغاله بسجدة التلاوة كان مأموراً بإتمام ركن هو فيه أو بانتقال إلى ركن آخر فيكون منهياً عن هذه السجدة. فإن قيل: أن يسجدها قبل الفراغ لأن سبب الوجوب السماع وهو وجد في الصلاة. قلنا: نعم وجد فيها لكنه حصل بناء على التلاوة والتلاوة حصلت خارج الصلاة فتؤدى خارجها. قوله (ولو سجد فيها أعادها لا الصلاة أي أعاد السجدة ولا يلزمه إعادة الصلاة لأنها ناقصة فلا يتأدى بها الكامل، وهذا لأن حكم هذه التلاوة مؤخر إلى ما بعد الفراغ عن الصلاة سبباً إلا بعده فلا يجوز تقديمه على سببه بخلاف ما لو تلاها في الأوقات المكروهة حيث يجوز أداؤها فيها وإن كانت ناقصة لتحقق السبب للحال ومحل إعادتها ما إذا لم يقرأها المصلي السامع غير المؤتم، وأما إن قرأها وسجد لها فيها فإنه لا إعادة عليه، أما إن كانت تلاوتها سابقة على سماعها فهو ظاهر الرواية لأن التلاوة الأولى من أفعال صلاته والثانية لا، فحصلت الثانية تكراراً للأولى من حيث الأصل والأولى باقية فجعل وصف الأولى للثانية من الصلاة فيكتفي بسجدة واحدة. وإن سمعها أولاً من أجنبي ثم تلاها المصلي وسجد لها فيها ففيه روايتان وجزم في السراج الوهاج بأنه لا يعيدها.
His statement: (And if a person praying hears it from someone else, he performs sujud after the prayer) because its cause, which is hearing, is realized. He restricted it with his statement 'after the prayer' because he does not perform sujud during it (the prayer) because the sujud he hears is not part of the prayer actions; thus including it in the prayer is prohibited because when the praying person occupies himself with sujud al-tilawah, he is commanded to complete the pillar he is in or to move to another pillar, so he is prohibited from this sujud. If it is said: He should perform sujud before finishing because the cause of obligation is hearing and it occurs during prayer. We reply: Yes, it occurs during prayer, but it arises based on recitation, and the recitation occurred outside the prayer, so it is performed outside it. His statement: (And if he performs sujud during it, he repeats it, not the prayer) meaning he repeats the sujud and is not required to repeat the prayer because it is deficient (naqisah) so the perfect one is not achieved by it; and this is because the ruling of this recitation is postponed to after finishing the prayer as a cause, so it cannot be advanced before its cause, unlike if he recites it during disliked times where performing it therein is permissible even if deficient because the cause is realized in the moment. The place of its repetition is when the praying listener who is not a muqtadi has not recited it; but if he recited it and performed sujud for it during the prayer, then there is no repetition upon him. If his recitation preceded his hearing, then it is the apparent of the riwayah because the first recitation is from his prayer actions and the second is not, so the second becomes a repetition of the first in principle, and the first remains, so the attribute of the first is attached to the second from the prayer and he suffices with one sujud. And if he first heard it from an ajnabi (stranger) and then recited it and performed sujud for it during prayer, then there are two narrations, and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj affirmed that he does not repeat it.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the ruling: a person who is praying and hears an ayat al-sajdah from someone else (who is not his imam and not a muqtadi) must perform the sujud al-tilawah after completing the prayer. The reason given is that the cause of obligation is hearing, which occurs during prayer, but the recitation that triggers it happened outside the prayer. Therefore, the sujud cannot be performed during the prayer because it would be introducing an action that is not part of the prayer, and the praying person is obligated to focus on his current pillar or transition to the next. Performing sujud during the prayer would be prohibited (manhiyy 'anhu). If someone does perform it during the prayer, his prayer remains valid but he must repeat the sujud after the prayer because the sujud performed was deficient (naqisah) and does not fulfill the obligation properly. However, there is no need to repeat the prayer itself. The commentator then discusses cases: if the praying person also recites the same ayat and prostrates during the prayer, he does not need to repeat the sujud because his own recitation (which is part of his prayer) supersedes the hearing. If he heard first from an outsider and then recited himself, there are two narrations; the relied-upon view is that he does not repeat the sujud. The passage also notes that if the hearing is from a muqtadi, different rules apply (as discussed in a previous passage).

Key Terms
السماع (al-sama'): The act of hearing an ayat al-sajdah; it is the cause (sabab) of obligation for the listener, distinct from the reciter's own cause.
ناقصة (naqisah): Deficient; refers to a sujud performed in a prohibited context (during prayer) that does not fulfill the complete obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person praying (but not as a muqtadi) hears an ayat al-sajdah recited by someone else and mistakenly performs sujud during the prayer?
A) The sujud is valid and no further action is needed.
B) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid but the sujud must be repeated after the prayer.
D) The sujud suffices and the prayer is valid, no need for repetition.

Key Takeaway
A praying person who hears an ayat al-sajdah from a non-muqtadi must perform sujud after the prayer; if done during, the sujud is deficient and must be repeated.

Ruling on Sajdat al-Tilawah for the Muqtadi
Distinguishing the ruling for muqtadi from janabah and haidh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muqtadi who hears a sajda verse from the imam, and explain the legal distinction between the muqtadi and a person in janabah or menstruation.

Core Idea
A muqtadi is legally prevented from recitation, so hearing a sajda verse does not obligate prostration during prayer.

This passage addresses a nuanced issue in congregational prayer: what happens when the imam recites a verse requiring prostration? The follower (muqtadi) has a different ruling than a person in major impurity outside prayer, due to the concept of legal prevention (hajr). Let's analyze the text to understand the reasoning and the minority view of Al-Marghinani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Persons
The act is sajdat al-tilawah. The persons involved: muqtadi (follower), junub (person in major impurity), and ha'id (menstruating woman).
2
State the Ruling for the Muqtadi
The passage states that tashahhud does not require prostration for the muqtadi due to hajr (prevention from recitation). So the muqtadi does not prostrate during prayer for a sajda verse heard from the imam.
3
Contrast with Junub and Ha'id
For the junub and ha'id, the amount that necessitates sajda (hearing the verse) is permissible (mubah) for them to prostrate. They are obligated to prostrate upon hearing, even if in a state of impurity, because they are not prevented from recitation in the same way.
The key difference is that the muqtadi is in prayer and is prevented from reciting, while the junub/ha'id are not in prayer.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Difference
Al-Marghinani holds a differing view: he believes the sajda is obligatory and can be performed in tashahhud. However, the relied-upon position (as per al-Mujtaba) is that the muqtadi does not prostrate.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school, there can be minority opinions.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, when a muqtadi hears a sajda verse from the imam during prayer, he should not prostrate. After prayer, he is not required to make up the sajda.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التشهد لا يلزم السجود للحجر عن القراءة فيه. قال المرغيناني وعندي أنها تجب وتتأدي فيه ا هـ. وذكر في المجتبى في الفرق بين الجنب والحائض وبين المقتدي أن القدر الذي يجب به السجدة مباح لهما على الأصح دون المقتدي .
The tashahhud does not necessitate prostration for the one prevented from recitation in it. Al-Marghinani said: In my view, it is obligatory and it is fulfilled in it. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba, in the distinction between the one in janabah, the menstruating woman, and the muqtadi (follower), that the amount which necessitates prostration is permissible for them (janabah and haidh) according to the most sound opinion, but not for the muqtadi.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of sajdat al-tilawah for a muqtadi (follower in prayer). The key point is that a muqtadi is legally 'prevented' (mahjur) from reciting the Quran during prayer because he must listen to the imam. Therefore, if he hears a sajda verse, he is not obliged to prostrate. This contrasts with a person in janabah or a menstruating woman who are not in prayer; for them, hearing a sajda verse obligates prostration, and it is permissible for them to perform it. The author references al-Marghinani who holds that the sajda is obligatory and can be performed in tashahhud, but the relied-upon view is that the muqtadi does not prostrate.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): A person who follows an imam in congregational prayer.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah).
الحائض (al-ha'id): A menstruating woman.
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal prevention or prohibition from an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muqtadi in prayer hears the imam recite a sajda verse. According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what should he do?
A) He should prostrate immediately after the imam.
B) He should wait and prostrate after the prayer.
C) He should not prostrate during or after the prayer.
D) He should recite the verse himself and then prostrate.

Key Takeaway
A follower (muqtadi) in Hanafi prayer does not perform sajdat al-tilawah because legal prevention (hajr) lifts the obligation.

Hearing Sajda Verse from Someone Else While in Prayer
Expanding the ruling of prostration after prayer for a hearer, with cases on repetition and following the reciter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on hearing a sajda verse from an outsider while in prayer, and determine when the prostration is performed after prayer and when repetition is required.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajda verse during prayer obligates prostration after prayer; performing it during requires repetition but does not invalidate the prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the matn statement 'If a person in prayer hears a sajda verse from someone else, he prostrates after the prayer.' The author explains the rationale: the hearing is based on recitation outside prayer, so the sajda is not part of the prayer (saliyya). Therefore, it must be performed after prayer; if done during, it is deficient and must be repeated, but the prayer itself remains valid. Several subcases are discussed, including when the hearer also recites, the follower's situation, and following the reciter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is hearing a sajda verse from someone else while in prayer. The ruling is that sajdat al-tilawah becomes wajib upon the hearer.
The cause (sabab) is hearing, which triggers the obligation.
2
Determine the time of performance
The sajda must be performed after the prayer, not during, because it is not an act of the prayer itself. The ruling is delayed until after prayer.
If performed during, it is considered deficient (nāqiṣa) and must be repeated.
3
Analyze the consequence of performing during prayer
If one prostrates during prayer, the sajda is invalid and must be repeated after prayer, but the prayer remains valid. This is because an increase of less than a rak'ah (i.e., one sajda) does not invalidate the prayer, even if intentional.
This is the muftā bihī view, contra Imam Muhammad who held intentional addition invalidates.
4
Note the exceptions and conditions
The obligation applies only if the reciter is not the hearer's imam and not a follower in the same prayer. If the hearer also recites the verse himself, one sajda suffices. Following the reciter (prostrating in imitation) invalidates the prayer.
A follower (muqtadi) is mahjur (prevented) from recitation, so hearing his own imam does not obligate sajda.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو سمعها المصلي من غيره سجد بعد الصلاة) لتحقق سببها وهو السماع. قيد بقوله بعد الصلاة» لأنه لا يسجدها فيها لأنها ليست بصلاتية لأن سماعه هذه السجدة ليس أفعال الصلاة فيكون إدخالها فيها منهياً عنه لأن المصلي عند اشتغاله بسجدة التلاوة كان مأموراً بإتمام ركن هو فيه أو بانتقال إلى ركن آخر فيكون منهياً عن هذه السجدة. فإن قيل: أن يسجدها قبل الفراغ لأن سبب الوجوب السماع وهو وجد في الصلاة. قلنا: نعم وجد فيها لكنه حصل بناء على التلاوة والتلاوة حصلت خارج الصلاة فتؤدى خارجها. قوله (ولو سجد فيها أعادها لا الصلاة أي أعاد السجدة ولا يلزمه إعادة الصلاة لأنها ناقصة فلا يتأدى بها الكامل، وهذا لأن حكم هذه التلاوة مؤخر إلى ما بعد الفراغ عن الصلاة سبباً إلا بعده فلا يجوز تقديمه على سببه بخلاف ما لو تلاها في الأوقات المكروهة حيث يجوز أداؤها فيها وإن كانت ناقصة لتحقق السبب للحال ومحل إعادتها ما إذا لم يقرأها المصلي السامع غير المؤتم، وأما إن قرأها وسجد لها فيها فإنه لا إعادة عليه، أما إن كانت تلاوتها سابقة على سماعها فهو ظاهر الرواية لأن التلاوة الأولى من أفعال صلاته والثانية لا، فحصلت الثانية تكراراً للأولى من حيث الأصل والأولى باقية فجعل وصف الأولى للثانية من الصلاة فيكتفي بسجدة واحدة. وإن سمعها أولاً من أجنبي ثم تلاها المصلي وسجد لها فيها ففيه روايتان وجزم في السراج الوهاج بأنه لا يعيدها. ولو تلاها وسجد لها للنهي فلا تصير فصارت فإنها تفيد الوجوب على غير المصلي أصلاً كما سيصرح به وعلى المصلي من إمام غير إمامه ومقتد به ومنفرد كما يفيده قول المتن الآتي: ولو سمعها المصلي من غيره سجد بعد الصلاة. فقوله «المصلي» يشمل ما إذا كان إماماً أو لا، وقوله من غيره يشمل ما إذا كان مصلياً أو لا كما صرح به الشيخ إسماعيل عن البرجندي. وقيد قوله «مصلياً» بقوله يعني وليس إمامه وصرح به أيضاً القهستاني والباقاني وعبارة شرح المنية : ولو تلاها المؤتم لا تجب عليه ولا على من سمعه ممن هو في تلك الصلاة خلافاً لمحمد، وتجب على من سمعها منه ممن ليس في صلاتها إجماعاً لعدم الحجر بالنظر إليهم ا هـ . ومثله في النهاية. وحينئذ فيما في النهر من قوله «أراد بقوله من غيره من لم يكن محجوراً عليه مخالف لهذه العبارات إلا أن يريد بالمحجور من كان في صلاة السامع لكن يعكر عليه تصريح الشرنبلالي في الإمداد بأنها لا تجب على الإمام والمقتدي بالسماع من مقتد بالإمام السامع أو بإمام آخر فليتأمل.

معه

قوله: (وهذا لأن حكم هذه التلاوة تبع فيه الزيلعي واقتصر في النهر على التعليل الأول وقال : إن ما جرى عليه تبعاً للشارح ممنوع .

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة ٢١٥ فيها أعادها لا الصلاة ولو سمع من إمام فأتم به قبل أن يسجد معه وبعده لا وإن لم ثم أحدث فذهب وتوضأ ثم عاد إلى مكانه وبنى على صلاته ثم قرأ ذلك الأجنبي تلك الآية، فعلى هذا المصلي أن يسجدها إذا فرغ من صلاته لأنه تحول عن مكانه فسمع الثانية بعدما تبدل المجلس. فرق بين هذا ما إذا قرأ آية سجدة ثم سبقه الحدث فذهب وتوضأ ثم جاء وقرأ وبين مرة أخرى لا تلزمه سجدة وإن قرأ الثانية بعدما تبدل المكان والفرق أن في المسألة الأولى المكان قد تبدل حقيقة وحكماً، أما الحقيقة فظاهر، وأما الحكم فلأن السماع ليس من أفعالها بخلاف الثانية. وتمامه في البدائع وإنما لم يعد الصلاة لأن زيادة ما دون الركعة لا يفسدها . وقيده في التجنيس والمجتبى والولوالجية بأن لا يتابع المصلي السامع القارئ فإن سجد القارئ فتابعه المصلي فيها فسدت صلاته للمتابعة ولا تجزئه السجدة عما . اهـ. وقد قدمنا أن زيادة سمع سجدة واحدة بنية المتابعة لغير إمامه مبطلة لصلاته. وفي النوادر ولو قرأ الإمام السجدة فظن القوم أنه ركع فبعضهم ركع وبعضهم ركع وسجد سجدة وبعضهم ركع وسجد سجدتين، فمن ركع ولم يسجد يرفض ركوعه ويسجد للتلاوة، ومن ركع وسجد فصلاته تامة وسجدته تجزئه عن سجدة التلاوة، ومن ركع وسجد سجدتين فصلاته فاسدة لأنه انفرد بركعة واحدة تامة اهـ . وذكر في الخلاصة في مسألة الكتاب لا تفسد صلاته هو الصحيح بناء على أن زيادة سجدة واحدة ساهياً أو سجدتين لا تفسد صلاته بالإجماع، وإن كان عمداً فكذلك . وإن ذكر في الجامع الصغير أنه يفسد عند محمد وذلك ليس بصحيح . ذكره الصدر الشهيد في المبسوط اهـ .
His saying: (And if a person in prayer hears it from someone else, he prostrates after the prayer) because its cause is fulfilled, which is hearing. He restricted it by saying 'after the prayer' because he does not prostrate during it, since it is not part of the prayer; his hearing this sajda is not among the acts of prayer, so inserting it into prayer is prohibited because when the person in prayer occupies himself with a sajda of recitation, he is commanded to complete the pillar he is in or to move to another pillar, so he is prohibited from this sajda. If it is said: He should prostrate before finishing because the cause of obligation is hearing, and it occurred in prayer. We say: Yes, it occurred in it, but it came about based on recitation, and the recitation occurred outside the prayer, so it is performed outside it. His saying: (and if he prostrates during it, he repeats it, not the prayer) meaning he repeats the sajda and is not required to repeat the prayer because it is deficient, so the complete cannot be performed by the deficient. And this is because the ruling of this recitation is delayed to after finishing the prayer; the cause exists only after it, so it is not permissible to advance it before its cause, unlike if he recited it in disliked times where performing it in them is permissible even if deficient, because the cause is realized at the time. The place of its repetition is when the hearing person who is not a follower does not recite it. But if he recited it and prostrated for it during it, then there is no repetition upon him. If his recitation preceded his hearing, then it is the apparent narration because the first recitation is from the acts of his prayer and the second is not, so the second is a repetition of the first in essence, and the first remains, so the description of the first is given to the second from the prayer, and one prostration suffices. And if he heard it first from an outsider, then the person in prayer recited it and prostrated for it during it, there are two narrations, and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj definitively stated that he does not repeat it. And if he recited it and prostrated for it due to the prohibition, it does not become valid; then it becomes that it confers obligation on one who is not in prayer absolutely, as will be stated, and on the person in prayer from an imam who is not his imam, and a follower, and an individual, as indicated by the following statement of the matn: And if a person in prayer hears it from someone else, he prostrates after the prayer. So his word 'the person in prayer' includes whether he is an imam or not, and his word 'from someone else' includes whether he is a person in prayer or not, as stated by Shaykh Ismail from al-Barjandi. And he restricted his word 'person in prayer' by saying 'meaning not his imam', and also stated by al-Qahistani and al-Baqani. And the expression of Sharh al-Munya: If the follower recites it, it is not obligatory upon him nor upon the one who hears it from him who is in that prayer, contrary to Muhammad. And it is obligatory upon the one who hears it from him who is not in his prayer, by consensus, because there is no prevention with respect to them. End quote. Similarly in al-Nihaya. Then regarding what is in al-Nahr from his saying 'He intended by his words 'from someone else' one who is not prevented', it contradicts these expressions unless he intends by 'prevented' one who is in the prayer of the hearer, but this is problematized by the explicit statement of al-Shurunbulali in al-Imdad that it is not obligatory upon the imam and the follower by hearing from a follower of the imam who hears or from another imam, so reflect.

With him

His saying: (And this is because the ruling of this recitation) al-Zayla'i followed him in it, and al-Nahr restricted to the first explanation and said: What he followed as a follower of the commentator is prevented.

Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sajda of Recitation page 215: In it he repeated it, not the prayer. And if he hears from an imam and completes with him before he prostrates, he prostrates with him, and after it, no. And if not, then he became in hadath and went and performed wudu, then returned to his place and built on his prayer, then that outsider recited that verse. Then this person in prayer must prostrate it when he finishes his prayer because he moved from his place and heard the second after the place changed. The difference between this and when he recites a sajda verse then hadath preceded him so he goes and performs wudu then comes and recites another time: he is not obliged to prostrate even if he recites the second after the place changed. The difference is that in the first case the place changed actually and legally; as for actually, it is apparent; as for legally, because hearing is not among its acts, unlike the second. Its completion is in al-Bada'i. And he did not repeat the prayer because an increase of less than a rak'ah does not invalidate it. And he restricted it in al-Tajnis, al-Mujtaba, and al-Walwalijiyya that the hearing person should not follow the reciter, because if the reciter prostrates and the hearing person follows him in it, his prayer becomes invalid due to following, and the prostration does not suffice for him. End quote. And we have already presented that an increase of one sajda with the intention of following someone other than his imam invalidates his prayer. And in al-Nawadir: If the imam recites the sajda verse and the people think it is ruku', so some of them did ruku', some did ruku' and prostrated one prostration, and some did ruku' and prostrated two prostrations; then the one who did ruku' and did not prostrate must abandon his ruku' and prostrate for recitation; the one who did ruku' and prostrated, his prayer is complete and his prostration suffices for the sajda of recitation; the one who did ruku' and prostrated two prostrations, his prayer is invalid because he performed one complete rak'ah individually. End quote. And it is mentioned in al-Khulasa regarding the matter of the book that his prayer is not invalidated; this is correct based on the fact that increasing one sajda forgetfully or two does not invalidate his prayer by consensus, and if intentional, likewise. And it is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir that it invalidates according to Muhammad, but that is not correct. Mentioned by al-Sadr al-Shahid in al-Mabsut. End quote.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This lengthy passage is a commentary on the matn statement: 'If a person in prayer hears a sajda verse from someone else, he prostrates after the prayer.' The author explains the rationale: hearing occurs due to recitation which is outside prayer, so the prostration is performed after prayer. If one prostrates during prayer, it is deficient and must be repeated after prayer, but the prayer remains valid because the extra prostration is less than a rak'ah. Various cases are discussed: if the hearer also recites the verse himself, he does not repeat; if he hears from an outsider then recites, there are two narrations. The passage also covers the ruling for a follower hearing from someone else, the difference between someone in prayer and someone not, and the issue of following the reciter. A detailed case from al-Nawadir describes what happens if followers mistake the imam's sajda for ruku'. The overall emphasis is that the sajda is not part of the prayer and must be performed outside, except in specific cases where it is performed within prayer validly.

Key Terms
صلاتية (saliyya): An act that is part of the prayer (e.g., its pillars or obligations).
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): A follower in prayer (muqtadi).
محجور (mahjur): One who is legally prevented from an act, such as a follower from recitation.
السماع (al-samā'): Hearing the sajda verse, which is the cause (sabab) of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower (muqtadi) in prayer hears a sajda verse from another follower in the same congregation, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The sajda is wajib upon the hearer and must be performed after prayer.
B) The sajda is not wajib because the hearer is mahjur.
C) The sajda is not wajib because the reciter is a follower in the same prayer.
D) The sajda must be performed immediately during the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah from hearing an outsider is performed after prayer; performing it during requires repetition of the sajda but the prayer remains valid.
