Joining Imam After Sajdat al-Tilawah
Ruling on follower joining after imam's tilawah sajda with reasoning and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a latecomer who joins after the imam's sajdat al-tilawah and explain the Hanafi reasoning and dispute.

Core Idea
If you join after the imam's recitation sajda, you do not prostrate with him, and whether you make it up later is disputed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rai'q clarifies the follower's obligation regarding sajdat al-tilawah. It addresses the timing of joining the imam and the status of the missed sajda. Understanding this ruling requires applying the Hanafi principle of mudrik (catching a rak'ah) and the concept of saliyya (prayer-integral acts).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes joining the imam before he prostrates for sajdat al-tilawah vs. after he has already prostrated.
The first scenario: follower joins before imam's sajda. Second: after imam's sajda.
2
Determine the ruling for each
If he joins before, he prostrates with the imam. If after, he does not prostrate during the prayer.
The text says 'sajada ma'ahu' for before, and 'la' for after.
3
Analyze the reasoning (qiyas)
The ruling for after is analogized to catching the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr, where the latecomer does not recite qunut. Similarly, the latecomer here missed the rak'ah of recitation, so he does not perform the associated sajda.
The illa is missing the specific part of the prayer (rak'ah with sajda).
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
There is disagreement whether the missed sajda should be made up after prayer. Some say it is saliyya (part of prayer) and cannot be performed outside. The apparent meaning of al-Hidayah suggests it is not saliyya and should be made up after prayer.
The mufta bihi is to prostrate after prayer according to al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو سمع من إمام فأتم به قبل أن يسجد سجد معه وبعده لا) أي لو ائتم به بعد أن سجدها الإمام لا يسجدها لأنه في الأول تابع له فيسجد معه وإن لم يسمع، وفي الثاني صار مدركاً لها بإدراك تلك الركعة كمن أدرك الإمام في ركوع ثالثة الوتر فإنه لا يقنت فيما يأتي به بعد فراغ الامام. قيد بقوله سجد معه لأن الإمام لو لم يسجد لا يسجد المأموم وإن سمعها لأنه إن سجدها في الصلاة وحده صار مخالف إمامه، وإن سجد بعد الفراغ وهي صلاتية لا تقضى خارجها. وأطلق في قوله وبعده لا فشمل ما إذا دخل معه في الركعة الثانية وفيه اختلاف وظاهر الهداية يقتضي أن يسجد لها بعد الفراغ لأنه لما لم يدرك ركعه التلاوة لم يصر مدركاً لها وليست صلاتية فيقضي خارجها، وقيل هي صلاتية فلا تقضى خارجها قوله (وإن لم يقتد سجدها لتقرر السبب في حقه وعدم المانع .
His saying: (And if he hears from an imam and completes with him before he prostrates, he prostrates with him, and after it, no) means if he follows him after the imam has prostrated it, he does not prostrate it because in the first case he is a follower and prostrates with him even if he did not hear; in the second case he becomes one who catches it by catching that rak'ah, like one who catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr, then he does not recite the qunut in what he performs after the imam finishes. He restricted it by his saying 'he prostrates with him' because if the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate even if he hears it, because if he prostrates in prayer alone, he becomes opposing his imam, and if he prostrates after finishing, while it is saliyya, it is not made up outside. And he generalized in his saying 'and after it no', so it includes if he enters with him in the second rak'ah, and there is a difference of opinion; the apparent meaning of al-Hidayah requires that he prostrate after finishing, because since he did not catch the rak'ah of recitation, he did not catch it, and it is not saliyya, so he makes it up outside. And it is said it is saliyya, so it is not made up outside. His saying: (And if he does not follow, he prostrates it because the cause is established for him and there is no preventer).
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for a follower who joins an imam after the imam has already performed sajdat al-tilawah. If he joins before the imam prostrates, he prostrates with him. If he joins after, he does not prostrate because he missed the rak'ah in which the sajda occurred; he is like someone who catches the imam in ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr and does not recite qunut. There is a dispute: some say the missed sajda is saliyya (part of prayer) and cannot be made up outside, while al-Hidayah suggests it should be made up after prayer since it was not caught and is not saliyya. The passage also clarifies that if the follower does not follow an imam (i.e., praying alone), he prostrates immediately.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): One who catches a part of the prayer with the imam.
صلاتية (saliyya): An act that is considered part of the prayer and thus cannot be performed outside.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration of recitation, performed upon hearing/reciting a verse of prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person joins the congregation after the imam has already performed sajdat al-tilawah, what should he do?
A) He must prostrate immediately after joining.
B) He prostrates with the imam in the next sajda.
C) He does not prostrate at all during the prayer, and may need to prostrate after according to some views.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The timing of joining the imam determines whether you prostrate for sajdat al-tilawah; if you miss the rak'ah, you do not prostrate and may need to do so after prayer according to the dominant view.

Sajda in Prayer: Not Repeated Outside
Stating the principle that sajda in prayer is not made up outside

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a sajda performed in a valid prayer cannot be made up outside, and explain the exceptional case when the prayer becomes invalid before the sajda is performed.

Core Idea
A sajda performed in a valid prayer is complete; only a missed sajda before invalidation is made up outside.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: a sajdat al-tilawah performed during a valid prayer becomes part of the prayer (saliyya) and cannot be repeated outside. However, if the verse was recited but the sajda not yet performed, and then the prayer becomes invalid, the sajda must be performed outside because it never became part of a valid prayer. This distinction highlights the importance of timing and validity in determining obligations.

Guided Path
1
Define 'saliyya'
Identify the key term صلاتية: an act that belongs to the prayer and cannot be separated from it. This is central to the ruling.
The term appears only in this context; understanding it unlocks the principle.
2
State the general rule
If a sajda is performed during a valid prayer, it becomes saliyya and cannot be made up outside. The reason: acts in prayer are more complete and virtuous.
3
Analyze the condition of prayer validity
The rule applies only when the prayer is valid throughout the sajda. If the prayer becomes invalid, the status of the sajda depends on whether it was already performed.
Validity is determined at the moment of performing the sajda.
4
Distinguish two subcases
Case A: Sajda performed in a valid prayer, then prayer invalidated → no repetition because the sajda was already complete. Case B: Sajda not performed before invalidation → wajib outside because the recitation is no longer part of a valid prayer.
The invalidator does not retroactively nullify already valid parts of the prayer.
5
Examine the reasoning (ta'lil)
The principle 'the complete cannot be performed by the deficient' explains why the sajda cannot be performed outside: outside prayer is deficient compared to inside prayer.
This is a qiyas based on the superiority of recitation in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولم تقض الصلاتية خارجها أي خارج الصلاة لأن السجدة المتلوة في الصلاة أفضل من غيرها لأن قراءة القرآن في الصلاة أفضل منها في غيرها فلم يجز أداؤها خارج الصلاة لأن الكامل لا يتأدى بالناقص. وهذا إذا لم تفسد الصلاة، أما إن تلاها في الصلاة ولم يسجد ثم فسدت الصلاة فعليه السجدة خارجها لأنها لما فسدت بقي مجرد تلاوة فلم تكن صلاتية، ولو أداها فيها ثم فسدت لا يعيد السجدة لأن بالمفسد لا يفسد جميع أجزاء الصلاة
His saying: (And the saliyya (prayer-related) is not performed outside it, meaning outside the prayer) because the sajda recited in prayer is superior to other than it, because recitation of Quran in prayer is superior to recitation outside it, so it is not permissible to perform it outside prayer because the complete cannot be performed by the deficient. And this is if the prayer is not invalidated. As for if he recited it in prayer and did not prostrate, then the prayer became invalid, then he must perform the sajda outside it, because when the prayer became invalid, only the bare recitation remained, so it was not saliyya. And if he performed it in it (the prayer) and then the prayer became invalid, he does not repeat the sajda, because with the invalidator, not all parts of the prayer are invalidated.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage establishes a key principle: a sajdat al-tilawah that is performed during prayer is considered 'saliyya' (part of the prayer) and therefore cannot be made up outside the prayer. The reasoning is that acts performed in prayer are more virtuous and complete; performing them outside would be deficient. However, if one recited the verse in prayer but did not prostrate, and then the prayer becomes invalid, the sajda must be performed outside because the recitation is no longer part of a valid prayer. Conversely, if one did prostrate and then the prayer becomes invalid, the sajda is not repeated because the invalidator does not nullify all components of the prayer retrospectively.

Key Terms
صلاتية (saliyya): An act that is considered part of the prayer and cannot be performed outside prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a sajda verse in prayer and prostrates, but then his prayer becomes invalid for another reason, must he repeat the sajda?
A) Yes, because the prayer is invalid.
B) No, because the sajda was already performed and is not affected by the invalidator.
C) Yes, but only if he didn't intend it properly.
D) No, but he must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
A sajda performed in a valid prayer is complete and not repeated outside; only a sajda omitted before prayer invalidation is made up outside.

Following the Imam in Sajdat al-Tilawah and the Effect of Extra Prostration
Expansion of matn ruling on following imam in sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a follower must prostrate for sajdat al-tilawah and explain why adding one or two extra sajdahs does not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
A follower prostrates with the imam if he joins before the prostration; after, he does not. Extra sajdahs do not invalidate prayer by consensus.

This lesson delves into the rulings of sajdat al-tilawah when praying behind an imam. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the critical moment of joining—before or after the imam's prostration—and the legal consequences of adding extra sajdahs, whether forgetful or intentional. We will examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement on this matter and the relied-upon consensus that preserves the validity of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the follower's obligation regarding sajdat al-tilawah
Determine when a follower must prostrate upon hearing the imam recite a sajdah verse: if he joins before the imam prostrates, he prostrates with him; if he joins after, he does not. Note the exception: if he did not join at all (not a follower), he prostrates it regardless.
The key is the state of being a follower (muqtadi) and the timing of joining.
2
Analyze the effect of adding extra sajdahs
The passage states that adding one or two sajdahs, whether forgetful or intentional, does not invalidate the prayer. This is based on consensus (ijma). Note the opposing view of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan that intentional addition invalidates, but it is deemed incorrect.
The ruling is consistent with the principle that increasing less than a rak'ah does not invalidate.
3
Understand the mutaba'ah condition for non-imam
If the worshipper who hears a sajdah from a non-imam follows that reciter by prostrating with him, his prayer becomes invalid. The act of following (mutaba'ah) is only valid when done behind one's own imam.
This highlights the strictness of mutaba'ah: intentional following of a non-imam in a prayer action invalidates the prayer.
4
Apply the rule to the al-Nawadir scenarios
Consider the case where followers mistake the imam's prostration for bowing. Each scenario (rak' only, rak' + one sajdah, rak' + two sajdahs) has a distinct ruling, reinforcing the principle that extra sajdahs can be accommodated without invalidation, but an extra full rak'ah (two sajdahs) invalidates because it constitutes an independent rak'ah.
Two sajdahs plus the preceding bowing form a full rak'ah, which is a significant increase.
5
Assess the intra-Hanafi dispute and the mufta bihi
Muhammad ibn al-Hasan held that intentional addition of even one sajdah invalidates prayer. The majority, cited in al-Khulasa and al-Mabsut, holds it does not. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view, supported by consensus (ijma).
The dispute is within the Hanafi school; the tarjih is by al-Sadr al-Shahid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة فيها أعادها لا الصلاة ولو سمع من إمام فأتم به قبل أن يسجد معه وبعده لا وإن لم ثم أحدث فذهب وتوضأ ثم عاد إلى مكانه وبنى على صلاته ثم قرأ ذلك الأجنبي تلك الآية، فعلى هذا بعدما تبدل المكان والفرق أن في المسألة الأولى المكان قد تبدل حقيقة وحكماً، أما الحقيقة فظاهر، وأما الحكم فلأن السماع ليس من أفعالها بخلاف الثانية. وتمامه في البدائع وإنما لم يعد الصلاة لأن زيادة ما سجدة واحدة بنية المتابعة لغير إمامه مبطلة لصلاته. وفي النوادر ولو قرأ الإمام السجدة فظن القوم أنه ركع فبعضهم ركع وبعضهم ركع وسجد سجدة وبعضهم ركع وسجد سجدتين، فمن ركع ولم يسجد يرفض ركوعه ويسجد للتلاوة، واحدة ساهياً أو سجدتين لا تفسد صلاته بالإجماع، وإن كان عمداً فكذلك . وإن ذكر في الجامع الصغير أنه يفسد عند محمد وذلك ليس بصحيح . ذكره الصدر الشهيد في المبسوط اهـ . قوله (ولو) سمع من إمام فأتم به قبل أن يسجد سجد معه وبعده لا) أي لو ائتم به بعد أن سجدها الإمام لا يسجدها لأنه في الأول تابع له فيسجد معه وإن لم يسمع، وفي الثاني صار مدركاً لها بإدراك تلك الركعة كمن أدرك الإمام في ركوع ثالثة الوتر فإنه لا يقنت فيما يأتي به بعد فراغ الامام. قيد بقوله سجد معه لأن الإمام لو لم يسجد لا يسجد المأموم وإن سمعها لأنه إن سجدها في الصلاة وحده صار مخالف إمامه، وإن سجد بعد الفراغ وهي صلاتية لا تقضى خارجها. وأطلق في قوله وبعده لا فشمل ما إذا دخل معه في الركعة الثانية وفيه اختلاف وظاهر الهداية يقتضي أن يسجد لها بعد الفراغ لأنه لما لم يدرك ركعه التلاوة لم يصر مدركاً لها وليست صلاتية فيقضي خارجها، وقيل هي صلاتية فلا تقضى خارجها قوله (وإن لم يقتد سجدها لتقرر السبب في حقه وعدم المانع .
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Recitation: In it he repeats it, not the prayer. And if he hears from an imam and joins him before he prostrates, he prostrates with him, and after it he does not. And if not, then he had an event and went and performed ablution, then returned to his place and continued his prayer, then that outsider recited that verse, so this worshipper must prostrate it when he finishes his prayer because he changed from his place and heard the second after the session changed. Difference between this and if he recited a verse of prostration then an event preceded him, so he went and performed ablution, then came and recited another time, no prostration is incumbent upon him even if he recited the second after the place changed. The difference is that in the first case the place changed in reality and in ruling; as for reality it is apparent, as for ruling because hearing is not among its actions unlike the second. Its completion is in al-Badai. And he did not repeat the prayer because an increase less than a rak'ah does not invalidate it. And he restricted it in al-Tajniss, al-Mujtaba, and al-Walwaljiyya that the worshipper who hears should not follow the reciter; if the reciter prostrated and the worshipper followed him in it, his prayer becomes invalid due to following, and the prostration does not suffice him. And we have already stated that an increase of one prostration with the intention of following someone other than his imam invalidates his prayer. And in al-Nawadir: If the imam recited the prostration verse and the people thought he was bowing, so some bowed, some bowed and prostrated once, and some bowed and prostrated twice; then whoever bowed and did not prostrate, he abandons his bowing and prostrates for recitation; whoever bowed and prostrated, his prayer is complete and his prostration suffices him for the prostration of recitation; whoever bowed and prostrated twice, his prayer is invalid because he performed a complete rak'ah independently. And it is mentioned in al-Khulasa in the issue of the book that it does not invalidate his prayer; that is the correct view based on the consensus that adding one prostration forgetfully or two does not invalidate his prayer, and if intentional, likewise. And it is mentioned in al-Jami al-Saghir that it invalidates according to Muhammad, but that is not correct. Al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned it in al-Mabsut. His saying: (And if) he hears from an imam and joins him before he prostrates, he prostrates with him, and after it he does not; meaning if he joins him after the imam prostrated it, he does not prostrate it, because in the first case he is a follower, so he prostrates with him even if he did not hear, and in the second case he becomes a perceiver of it by perceiving that rak'ah, like one who catches the imam in the bowing of the third of witr, he does not recite the qunut in what he performs after the imam finishes. He restricted by his saying 'he prostrates with him' because if the imam did not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate even if he heard it, because if he prostrates it in the prayer alone, he becomes opposing his imam, and if he prostrates after finishing, and it is a prayer-related prostration, it is not performed outside. And he made absolute in his saying 'and after it he does not' so it includes if he enters with him in the second rak'ah, and there is disagreement. The apparent meaning of al-Hidayah necessitates that he prostrates for it after finishing because since he did not perceive the rak'ah of recitation, he did not become perceiver of it, and it is not prayer-related, so he performs it outside. And it is said it is prayer-related, so it is not performed outside. His saying: (And if he does not follow) he prostrates it because the cause is established in his right and there is no preventer.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling on sajdat al-tilawah in relation to following the imam. The commentary clarifies that if a person hears a sajdah verse from an imam and joins the prayer before the imam prostrates, he must prostrate with him; if he joins after the imam has prostrated, he does not prostrate. The text then discusses cases where a person hears a sajdah from a non-imam after moving from his place, imposing a new sajdah. It also covers the validity of prayer when an extra sajdah is added: consensus holds that one or two extra sajdahs, whether forgetful or intentional, do not invalidate the prayer, contrary to a less reliable opinion attributed to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. The commentary also addresses scenarios from al-Nawadir where followers mistake the imam's prostration for bowing, detailing the rulings for each case. The key principle is that the follower must act in accordance with the imam's action; prostrating alone without the imam or following a non-imam invalidates the prayer. The phrase-by-phrase explanation of the matn 'wa law sami'a min imam' is provided, emphasizing the conditions of being a follower and the concept of 'idrak' (catching the rak'ah) which determines whether the sajdah is performed inside or outside the prayer.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran (15 verses).
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): The act of following the imam in prayer actions with the intention of following.
الإدراك (al-idrak): The legal concept of catching a rak'ah or action with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person joins the imam after the imam has already prostrated for sajdat al-tilawah?
A) He must prostrate with the imam.
B) He does not prostrate for that sajdah.
C) He must prostrate after the prayer.
D) His prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
A follower prostrates for sajdat al-tilawah only if he joins before the imam prostrates; extra sajdahs, even intentional, do not invalidate the prayer by consensus.

Sajdah in Prayer: No Makeup, Bowing Substitutes by Istihsan
Expansion of a matn principle with proof and internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-tilawah omitted during prayer and differentiate between the qiyas and istihsan approaches to substitution by bowing.

Core Idea
Sajdah missed in prayer carries sin even without makeup; bowing substitutes by istihsan, not qiyas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key principle: sajdat al-tilawah performed during prayer is not repeated outside. It addresses the consequence of omission—sin remains—and the nuance of bowing (ruku') substituting for the sajdah. An intra-Hanafi dispute between qiyas and istihsan is resolved in favour of istihsan, the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exception
State that sajdat al-tilawah performed in prayer is not made up outside. Note the exception: if a woman menstruates after reciting the verse, the sajdah is waived.
Menstruation is a valid excuse that removes the obligation entirely.
2
Analyse the consequence of omission
If the sajdah is omitted without excuse, the person sins. The obligation is 'dropped' in the sense that no makeup is required, but the sin remains and requires repentance.
Common error: thinking 'dropped' means no sin. The text explicitly warns against this.
3
Examine the substitution argument
Some scholars (Muhammad al-Shaybani) considered that bowing can substitute for the sajdah by qiyas (analogy) because both are acts of humility. Others argued by istihsan (juristic preference) that bowing is contrary to the explicit command for prostration, so it should not substitute.
Muhammad's own statement: 'By qiyas, bowing and prostration are equal; by istihsan, he should prostrate.'
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that bowing does suffice by istihsan. This is the position adopted by later scholars (al-Mujtaba, al-Badai) and is given precedence.
Tarjih authority: the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq prefers the istihsan view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما يفسد الجزء المقارن فيمتنع البناء عليه كذا في القنية ويستثنى من فسادها ما إذا فسدت بالحيض. قال في الخلاصة : المرأة إذا قرأت آية السجدة في صلاتها فلم تسجد حتى حاضت تسقط عنها السجدة. وفي فتح القدير : ثم صواب النسبة فيه صلوية برد ألفه واواً وحذف التاء وإذ كانوا قد حذفوها في نسبة المذكر إلى المؤنث كنسبة الرجل إلى بصرة مثلاً فقالوا بصري لا بصرتي كيلا يجتمع تاءان في نسبة المؤنث فيقولون بصرتية فكيف بنسبة المؤنث إلى المؤنث اهـ. وفي العناية : إنه خطأ مستعمل وهو عند الفقهاء خير من صواب نادر انتهى . ثم مقتضى قواعدهم أنه إذا لم يسجد في الصلاة حتى فرغ فإنه يأثم لأنه لم يؤد الواجب ولم يمكن قضاؤها لما ذكرنا وهذا متن الواجبات الذي إذا فات وقته تقرر الإثم على المكلف والمخرج له عنه التوبة كسائر الذنوب وإياك أن تفهم من قولهم بسقوطها عدم الإثم فإنه خطأ فاحش كما رأيت بعضهم يقع فيه. ثم رأيت بعد ذلك التصريح به في البدائع قال : وإذا لم يسجد لم يبق عليه إلا الإثم ومحل سقوطها ما إذا لم يركع لصلاته ولم يسجد لها صلبية، أما إن ركع أو سجد صلبية فإنه ينوب عنها إذا كان على الفور ولم يذكره المصنف وحاصله على ما ذهب إليه الأصوليون أن الركوع ينوب عن سجدة التلاوة قياساً لما فيه من معنى الخضوع ولا ينوب استحساناً لأنه خلاف المأمور به. وقدم القياس هنا على الاستحسان لقوة أثره الباطن وعكسه في المجتبى فقال : تلاها وركع للتلاوة مكان السجود يجزئه قياساً لا استحساناً، والأصح أنه يجزئه استحساناً لا قياساً وبه قال علماؤنا اهـ. ووجه الأصح أن القياس لا يقتضي عدم جوازه لأنه الأمر الظاهر بالسجود والركوع خلاف السجود، ولكن الحق الأول لتصريح محمد به فإنه قال في الكتاب : فإن أراد أن يركع بالسجدة نفسها هل يجزئه ذلك قال : أما في القياس فالركوع في ذلك والسجدة سواء لأن كل ذلك صلاة، وأما في الاستحسان فينبغي له أن يسجد وبالقياس نأخذ اهـ. وحاصله على ما ذكره الفقهاء كما في البدائع ملخصاً أن المتلوة خارج الصلاة تؤدى على نعت سجدات الصلاة والمتلوة في الصلاة الأفضل أن يسجد لها ثم إذا سجد وقام يكره له أن يركع كما رفع رأسه، سواء كان آية السجدة في وسط السورة أو عند ختمها. وبقي بعدها إلى الختم قدر آيتين أو ثلاث فينبغي أن يقرأ ثم يركع فينظر إن كانت الآية في الوسط فإنه ينبغي أن يختمها ثم يركع، وإن كانت
And only the concurrent part becomes invalid, so building upon it is prevented. Thus in al-Qunya. And an exception from its invalidity is when it becomes invalid by menstruation. He said in al-Khulasa: If a woman recites a verse of prostration in her prayer and does not prostrate until she menstruates, the prostration is waived from her. And in Fath al-Qadir: Then the correct attribution is 'salawiyya' by changing its alif to waw and dropping the ta, and since they dropped it in the attribution of masculine to feminine like the attribution of a man to Basra, they say Basri not Basriyya, so that two tas do not combine in the attribution of feminine to feminine; how then with the attribution of feminine to feminine? In al-Inaya: It is a common mistake, and it is better among jurists than a rare correct form. Then the implication of their principles is that if he does not prostrate in the prayer until he finishes, he sins because he did not perform the wajib and cannot make it up for what we mentioned. This is the text of obligations: when its time passes, sin is established upon the accountable, and the way out is repentance like other sins. Beware of understanding from their statement of its dropping the absence of sin, for that is a grave mistake as I have seen some fall into it. Then I saw after that explicit mention in al-Badai: He said: If he does not prostrate, nothing remains upon him except sin. And the place of its dropping is when he did not bow for his prayer and did not prostrate for it as a prayer-related prostration. But if he bowed or prostrated as a prayer-related prostration, it substitutes for it if it was immediately, and the author did not mention it. Its summary according to what the usuliyyun went to is that bowing substitutes for sajdat al-tilawah by qiyas because of the meaning of humility it contains, and it does not substitute by istihsan because it is contrary to the commanded. Here qiyas is given precedence over istihsan due to the strength of its inner effect, and the opposite in al-Mujtaba: He said: If he recited and bowed for recitation instead of prostration, it suffices by qiyas not by istihsan, and the most correct is that it suffices by istihsan not by qiyas, and our scholars said this. The face of the most correct is that qiyas does not necessitate its non-permissibility because the apparent command is for prostration and bowing is contrary to prostration, but the first is correct due to the explicit statement of Muhammad, for he said in the book: If he intends to bow for the prostrating verse itself, does it suffice him? He said: As for qiyas, bowing in that and prostration are equal because all of that is prayer; as for istihsan, he should prostrate, and by qiyas we take. Its summary according to what the jurists mentioned as in al-Badai is that the recitation outside prayer is performed in the manner of prayer prostrations, and the recitation in prayer it is better to prostrate for it. Then if he prostrates and stands, it is disliked for him to bow as soon as he raises his head, whether the verse of prostration is in the middle of the surah or at its end. And if there remains after it to the end about two or three verses, it is better that he recites then bows. He looks: if the verse is in the middle, it is better that he completes it then bows; and if it is
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn principle that sajdat al-tilawah performed during prayer is not repeated outside the prayer. The commentary begins by stating that only the concurrent part of the prayer becomes invalid, so one cannot build upon it. An exception is made for invalidity due to menstruation: if a woman recites a sajdah verse in prayer and menstruates before prostrating, the sajdah is waived. The commentator then discusses the sin of omitting the sajdah: if one does not prostrate until finishing prayer, he sins and cannot make it up; repentance is required. A crucial nuance: the sin is not removed by the ruling that the sajdah is 'dropped' — that only means no makeup is required, but the sin remains. The text then addresses the substitution of bowing (ruku') for the sajdah. There is a dispute between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). Muhammad al-Shaybani held that bowing suffices by qiyas because both are part of prayer, but by istihsan one should prostrate. The preferred view in the school is that bowing suffices by istihsan, as reported from 'our scholars'. The practical ruling is that outside prayer, the sajdah is performed like a normal prostration; inside prayer, it is better to prostrate, and after prostrating it is disliked to immediately bow. If the sajdah verse is in the middle of a surah, it is better to complete the surah before bowing; if at the end, one may bow after it.

Key Terms
الصلاتية (al-salawiyya): That which is performed within the context of prayer; here, a sajdah performed during prayer is considered 'salatiyya' (prayer-related) and thus not repeated outside.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; choosing a ruling that deviates from strict analogy for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, can bowing (ruku') substitute for sajdat al-tilawah during prayer?
A) No, never.
B) Yes, by qiyas only.
C) Yes, by istihsan (juristic preference), and it is the mufta bihi view.
D) Yes, but only if the sajdah verse is at the end of the surah.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah missed in prayer is not made up; sin remains unless a valid excuse, and bowing substitutes by istihsan.

Sajdah in Invalidated Nafl Prayer Not Repeated
Final part of commentary on matn phrase regarding sajdah in invalidated nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the repetition of sajdah al-tilawah when performed in a nafl prayer that later becomes invalid, and explain the underlying principle that the sajdah retains its prayer-related character.

Core Idea
A sajdah performed in a valid prayer stands independently; invalidation of the prayer does not erase it.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: you recite a sajdah verse during a supererogatory (nafl) prayer, prostrate, and then the prayer becomes invalid (e.g., by intentional speech). Do you need to repeat that sajdah when making up the prayer? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer based on the principle that the sajdah, once performed, retains its validity as a prayer-related act, even if the surrounding prayer is spoiled. We will explore the textual source and the legal reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is performing a sajdah al-tilawah within a nafl prayer that later becomes invalid. The ruling from al-Khaniyya is that the prayer must be made up (qada wajib), but the sajdah is not repeated.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the explicit text from al-Khaniyya cited in the commentary: 'A supererogatory prayer worshipper, if he recites a verse and prostrates for it, then his prayer becomes invalid, its makeup is obligatory upon him but he is not required to repeat that prostration.'
Al-Khaniyya is a later fatwa collection, but its ruling is considered authoritative (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
3
Trace the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The underlying principle: the sajdah, when performed in a valid prayer, acquires the status of a 'prayer-related act' (salatiyya). Invalidation of the prayer does not strip the sajdah of this character; it remains valid and does not need to be repeated.
This reasoning is described as 'more in line with the rules' (بالقواعد أليق) in the commentary.
4
Note the practical implication and mufta bihi
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is: if a nafl prayer containing a performed sajdah becomes invalid, the prayer is made up but the sajdah is not repeated. This applies regardless of the cause of invalidation (except possibly menstruation as discussed).
The commentator notes that this ruling makes an exception for menstruation unnecessary, unless the woman prostrated after the prayer had already become invalid by menstruation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو أداها فيها ثم فسدت لا يعيد السجدة قال في النهر لكن في الخانية لوتلاها في نافلة فأفسدها وجب قضاؤها دون السجدة وهذا بالقواعد أليق لأنها بالإفساد لم تخرج عن كونها صلاتية، وبهذا التقرير استغنى عن قول البحر ويستثنى من فسادها ما إذا فسدت بالحيض» إلا أن يحمل ما في الخانية على ما إذا كان بعد سجودها ا هـ . أقول : كلام الخانية صريح في ذلك ونصه : مصلي التطوع إذا قرأ آية وسجد لها ثم فسدت صلاته وجب عليه قضاؤها ولا تلزمه إعادة تلك السجدة .
His saying: (And if he performs it in it then it becomes invalid, he does not repeat the prostration). He said in al-Nahr: But in al-Khaniyya, if he recited it in a supererogatory prayer and invalidated it, its makeup is obligatory without the prostration. And this is more in line with the rules because by invalidation it does not exit from being prayer-related. And with this formulation, the statement of al-Bahr 'and an exception from its invalidity is when it becomes invalid by menstruation' becomes unnecessary, unless the statement in al-Khaniyya is interpreted as after her prostration. end quote. I say: The statement of al-Khaniyya is explicit in that and its text: A supererogatory prayer worshipper, if he recites a verse and prostrates for it, then his prayer becomes invalid, its makeup is obligatory upon him but he is not required to repeat that prostration.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage explains the final matn phrase concerning a sajdah performed within a prayer that later becomes invalid. The commentary from al-Nahr cites a ruling from al-Khaniyya: if a person recites a sajdah verse in a nafl (supererogatory) prayer and prostrates, then the prayer becomes invalid, he must make up the prayer (qada) but does not need to repeat the sajdah. The reason is that even though the prayer was invalidated, the sajdah retains its character as a prayer-related act (salatiyya) and thus is not repeated outside. This ruling is considered more consistent with the school's principles. The commentator notes that this obviates the exception made by al-Bahr for menstruation, unless the case in al-Khaniyya is understood to be after the woman had already prostrated. Finally, the commentator affirms the clarity of al-Khaniyya's text: the sajdah is not to be repeated after invalidation of a nafl prayer.

Key Terms
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Supererogatory (nafl) prayer, as opposed to obligatory prayer.
القضاء (al-qada): The makeup of an obligatory or supererogatory act after its time.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): Prostration of recitation, performed upon reciting specific Quranic verses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Repeat both the prayer and the sajdah.
B) Repeat the prayer but not the sajdah.
C) Repeat only the sajdah.
D) Nothing, as both are invalidated.

Key Takeaway
A sajdah performed in a valid nafl prayer retains its validity even if the prayer later becomes invalid; it does not need to be repeated when making up the prayer.

Ruling on Missing Sajdah al-Tilawah in Prayer
States the ruling on missing sajdah al-tilawah in prayer and clarifies that sin remains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on missing sajdah al-tilawah in prayer and explain why sin remains, including the exception for menstruation.

Core Idea
Missing sajdah al-tilawah in prayer incurs sin that only repentance removes—it is not made up later.

Sajdah al-tilawah is a wajib act when a verse of prostration is recited or heard. But what happens if it is missed within prayer? The Hanafi school clarifies that once the prayer ends, the opportunity to perform it is gone, and the sin for neglecting a wajib remains. However, there is an exception for menstruation, which waives the obligation entirely. Let us examine the ruling and the common misunderstanding about the term 'sqt' (waiving).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib according to the Hanafi school when a verse of prostration is recited or heard, including during prayer.
This is a separate wajib, not a pillar of the prayer.
2
Note the exception
If a woman recites an ayat al-sajdah in prayer and then menstruates before prostrating, the prostration is waived (tasqut). She does not need to perform it later.
Menstruation is a preventer that lifts the obligation.
3
Determine the consequence of missing it
If the sajdah is missed during prayer and not performed before the prayer ends, it cannot be made up. The person is sinful because a wajib was omitted.
The sin remains and is only removed by repentance.
4
Recognize the common error
The author warns that 'sqt' (waiving) does not mean absence of sin; it means the act is no longer required after its time, but the sin for missing it remains until repentance.
Do not confuse legal waiving with forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it only invalidates the concurrent part, so building upon it is prevented. Thus in al-Qunyah. And from its invalidation is excepted when it is invalidated by menstruation. He said in al-Khulasah: If a woman recites a verse of prostration in her prayer and does not prostrate until she menstruates, the prostration is waived for her. And in Fath al-Qadir: Then the correct nisbah in it is 'salwiyyah' by changing its alif to waw and dropping the ta'. And since they had dropped it in the nisbah of masculine to feminine, like the nisbah of a man to Basrah, they said 'Basri' not 'Bastiyy' to avoid two ta's in the feminine nisbah, so they would say 'Bastiyyah'. So how about the nisbah of feminine to feminine? In al-Inayah: It is a common error, and according to the jurists it is better than a rare correct one. Then the implication of their rules is that if he does not prostrate in the prayer until he finishes, he sins because he did not perform the obligatory act and it cannot be made up for the reason we mentioned. And this is the text of obligations: when its time passes, sin is established upon the responsible person, and the way out for him is repentance like other sins. And beware of understanding from their statement 'waived' that there is no sin, for that is a serious error as I have seen some fall into.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling on sajdah al-tilawah when it is missed within prayer. The author first notes an exception: if a woman recites a verse of prostration in prayer and then menstruates before prostrating, the prostration is waived. Then he discusses the linguistic form of the nisbah 'salwiyyah'—a side note on proper Arabic. The core ruling: if one does not prostrate during prayer until after finishing the prayer, he is sinful because the wajib act was not performed and it cannot be made up after the prayer. The author strongly warns against the misconception that 'sqt' (waiving) implies no sin; rather, the sin remains and only repentance removes it.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
سقط (saqata): To fall or be waived; in legal context, the obligation is removed but the sin for missing it remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a woman recites an ayat al-sajdah in prayer and then menstruates before prostrating?
A) She must prostrate after her menstruation ends.
B) The prostration is waived and she need not perform it.
C) She must repeat the prayer.
D) She incurs a sin for not prostrating.

Key Takeaway
Missing sajdah al-tilawah in prayer is a sin that cannot be undone by a makeup prostration; only repentance suffices, except when waived by valid excuse like menstruation.

Ruku' Substituting for Sajdah al-Tilawah: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Presents the Hanafi dispute on ruku' substituting for sajdah al-tilawah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether ruku' substitutes for sajdah al-tilawah and identify the mufta bihi position with its proof.

Core Idea
Ruku' suffices for sajdah al-tilawah by qiyas; the inner meaning of humility outweighs the literal command.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a subtle dispute within the Hanafi school: if a person recites an ayat al-sajdah in prayer and bows (ruku') immediately for that recitation, does it count as fulfilling the wajib sajdah? The answer hinges on whether we give precedence to the inner meaning of humility (qiyas) or to the literal command to prostrate (istihsan). The text presents both views and ultimately resolves the issue by citing the explicit ruling of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, identify the main ruling: sajdah al-tilawah is wajib. The dispute is whether ruku' can serve as a substitute when recited in prayer.
2
Identify the opposing view within the school
Some Hanafis (e.g., the author of al-Mujtaba) argued that ruku' does not substitute, because the command is to prostrate, and bowing is different.
This is the istihsan position.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the istihsan argument: adhering to the apparent text (zahir) of the command over analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response relies on Imam Muhammad's explicit statement in al-Kitab that by qiyas, ruku' and sajdah are equal because both are prayer. The inner meaning of khudu' (humility) is the effective cause.
This response gives precedence to qiyas over istihsan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical outcome: if ruku' suffices, no additional prostration is needed; if not, one must prostrate or repeat. The school adopts the qiyas view as mufta bihi.
Tarjih is based on Imam Muhammad's authority and later Hanafi consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم رأيت بعد ذلك التصريح به في البدائع قال : وإذا لم يسجد لم يبق عليه إلا الإثم ومحل سقوطها ما إذا لم يركع لصلاته ولم يسجد لها صلبية، أما إن ركع أو سجد صلبية فإنه ينوب عنها إذا كان على الفور ولم يذكره المصنف وحاصله على ما ذهب إليه الأصوليون أن الركوع ينوب عن سجدة التلاوة قياساً لما فيه من معنى الخضوع ولا ينوب استحساناً لأنه خلاف المأمور به. وقدم القياس هنا على الاستحسان لقوة أثره الباطن وعكسه في المجتبى فقال : تلاها وركع للتلاوة مكان السجود يجزئه قياساً لا استحساناً، والأصح أنه يجزئه استحساناً لا قياساً وبه قال علماؤنا اهـ. ووجه الأصح أن القياس لا يقتضي عدم جوازه لأنه الأمر الظاهر بالسجود والركوع خلاف السجود، ولكن الحق الأول لتصريح محمد به فإنه قال في الكتاب : فإن أراد أن يركع بالسجدة نفسها هل يجزئه ذلك قال : أما في القياس فالركوع في ذلك والسجدة سواء لأن كل ذلك صلاة، وأما في الاستحسان فينبغي له أن يسجد وبالقياس نأخذ اهـ.
Then after that I saw explicit mention in al-Bada'i: He said: And if he does not prostrate, nothing remains upon him except sin. And the place of its waiver is when he did not bow for his prayer and did not prostrate for it in the obligatory prostration. But if he bowed or performed the obligatory prostration, it substitutes for it if it was immediate, though the author did not mention it. Its summary according to what the usuliyyun went to is that bowing substitutes for the prostration of recitation by qiyas because it contains the meaning of humility, and it does not substitute by istihsan because it is contrary to what is commanded. And here qiyas is given precedence over istihsan due to the strength of its inner effect, and the opposite in al-Mujtaba: He said: He recited and bowed for recitation in place of prostration; it suffices by qiyas, not by istihsan. And the more correct opinion is that it suffices by istihsan, not qiyas, and it is the view of our scholars. And the justification of the more correct is that qiyas does not necessitate its impermissibility because the apparent command is to prostrate, and bowing is contrary to prostration. But the truth is the first view because of the explicit statement of Muhammad (al-Shaybani), for he said in al-Kitab: If he wants to bow for the prostration itself, does that suffice? He said: As for qiyas, bowing in that and prostration are equal because all of it is prayer. As for istihsan, he should prostrate, and by qiyas we take.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the dispute within the Hanafi school on whether ruku' (bowing) can substitute for sajdah al-tilawah when recited in prayer. The preferred opinion (al-asahh) according to some is that it suffices by istihsan, not qiyas. However, the author notes that the ultimate truth is the first view (qaul) because Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani explicitly stated in his book that by qiyas, both bowing and prostration are equal, and the school takes by qiyas. The reasoning: qiyas gives precedence to the inner meaning of humility common to both acts, while istihsan adheres to the literal command of prostration. The text narrates a back-and-forth between different Hanafi authorities, but the final operative ruling is that ruku' does substitute for sajdah al-tilawah in prayer, taking by qiyas.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a common effective cause ('illah). Here, the 'illah is the meaning of humility (khudu').
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from a clear analogy in favor of a stronger evidence or public interest. Here, it prefers the literal command over analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this passage, if a person recites an ayat al-sajdah in prayer and then bows (ruku') for that recitation, what is the ruling?
A) It does not suffice; he must prostrate after the prayer.
B) It suffices by qiyas, and he does not need to prostrate separately.
C) It suffices only if he intended the sajdah with the ruku'.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that ruku' performed immediately for an ayat al-sajdah in prayer suffices by qiyas, not istihsan.

Conditions for Ruku' Substituting for Sajdah al-Tilawah
Details conditions for ruku' substituting for sajdah al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which ruku' in prayer substitutes for sajdah al-tilawah, derive the ruling from the Hanafi proof (Companion practice and qiyas), and apply the condition of immediacy (fawr) to determine validity.

Core Idea
Ruku' substitutes for sajdah al-tilawah only if performed immediately, with intention, and without reciting three or more verses after the verse of prostration.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a nuanced Hanafi ruling: can a ruku' movement in prayer fulfill the wajib act of sajdah al-tilawah? The answer is yes, under strict conditions. We will explore the proofs from Companion practice (Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar) and the operative qiyas, as well as the criteria of immediacy and intention. Understanding this substitution illuminates the Hanafi method of balancing qiyas and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sajdah al-tilawah is wajib in the Hanafi school. The act under discussion is the substitution of this wajib by the ruku' movement in prayer. The ruling is that substitution is valid when conditions are met.
This is not the default ruling; it is a concession based on specific proofs.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a narration from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed bowing instead of prostration in prayer. This is treated as near-ijma' because no opposition is recorded. Additionally, qiyas is employed: the ruku' and sajdah are both acts of humility, so one can stand for the other.
The author chooses qiyas over istihsan in this case because the evidence for qiyas was stronger.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Companion practice demonstrates permissibility. The qiyas reasoning: ruku' and sajdah share the same essential meaning (khushu'), so ruku' can substitute. The strength of this proof led the Hanafis to adopt it.
The passage explicitly states that the evidence of qiyas became strong, so they took by it.
4
Identify the conditions (shurut)
Two main conditions are discussed: (1) Immediacy (fawr): the ruku' must be performed soon after reciting the ayat al-sajdah, without reciting three or more verses. (2) Intention (niyyah): the worshipper must intend that this ruku' fulfills the sajdah. Some scholars do not require intention, but the preferred view (mufta bihi) requires it.
The measure of fawr is specified as not reciting three verses; reciting three breaks it.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
There is intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether intention is necessary and on the exact number of verses that break fawr. Qadhi Khan allowed ruku' outside prayer to substitute, but this is weaker. The passage refutes Muhammad ibn Salamah's view that only the obligatory prostration substitutes.
The author resolves by citing Imam Muhammad's own text and the conditions from al-Mujtaba.

السماء انشقت» اهـ. واختلف فيما إذا ركع على الفور للصلاة وسجد هل المجزئ عن سجدة التلاوة الركوع أو سجدة الصلاة؟ قوله : (لا يجوز (بالإجماع أي بإجماع الذين شرطوا النية في نيابته عنها. كذا في حاشية نوح أفندي قوله : (واختار قاضيخان الخ) قال في النهر : فالمروي في الظاهر أنه يجوز كذا في البزازية لكن في نسختي البزازية في غير الظاهر وكذا رأيته في نسخة أخرى من البزازية، ثم إن ما في الخانية لا يدل على And its summary according to what the jurists mentioned as in al-Bada'i, summarized: That the recited verse outside prayer is performed in the manner of prayer prostrations, and the recited verse in prayer—it is better to prostrate for it. Then when he prostrates and stands up, it is disliked for him to bow just as he raised his head, whether the verse of prostration is in the middle of the surah or at its end. And if after it until the end there remains the measure of two or three verses, then he should recite and then bow. So one looks: if the verse is in the middle, then he should complete it and then bow. And if it is his saying: (And if he performs it in it and then it becomes invalid, he does not repeat the prostration. He said in al-Nahr: But in al-Khaniyyah, if he recited it in a supererogatory prayer and invalidated it, he must make up the prayer but not the prostration. And this is more fitting with the principles because by invalidation it does not cease being prayer-related. And by this explanation, the statement of al-Bahr 'except when invalidated by menstruation' is rendered unnecessary, unless what is in al-Khaniyyah is interpreted as after her prostration. I say: The words of al-Khaniyyah are explicit in that, and its text: A voluntary prayer performer if he recites a verse and prostrates for it, then his prayer becomes invalid—he must make up the prayer, and he is not required to repeat that prostration. [PAGE_217] ...two verses... at the end, then he should recite verses from another surah and then bow. And if there remains to the end the measure of two or three, as in Bani Isra'il and Idha al-Sama'unshaqqat, he should recite the rest of the surah and then bow. If he joins another surah to it, it is better. And if he did not prostrate but only bowed, it is mentioned in al-Asl that by qiyas they are equal and by istihsan it does not suffice, and by qiyas we take. And the difference between them is that what is apparent of meanings is qiyas, and what is hidden is istihsan; there is no preponderance in the hidden due to its hiddenness, nor in the apparent due to its apparentness; so one returns to seeking preponderance from the meanings associated with them. So when the hidden becomes strong, they take by it; and when the apparent becomes strong, they take by it. And here the evidence of qiyas became strong, so they took by it because it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed bowing instead of prostration in prayer, and no opposition came from others, so it was like consensus. Then they differed about the place of qiyas and istihsan. The general opinion says it is in establishing bowing in place of prostration in prayer. Some said it is outside prayer: if he recited outside prayer and bowed—this is not sound; it does not suffice by qiyas or istihsan because bowing outside prayer is not made an act of worship, so it cannot take the place of a worship act. And from Muhammad bin Salamah: The obligatory prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) takes the place of sajdah al-tilawah, not bowing. This is refuted by what Muhammad stated in the book as we mentioned earlier. And if he did not bow for the recitation, it is not valid even if he intended it for the prostration. Likewise, the obligatory prostration does not substitute for it if the recitation was long because it becomes a debt for its obligatory nature as immediate, and a debt is paid with what is owed, not with what is upon him; bowing and prostration are upon him, so the debt is not fulfilled. And if the recitation is not long, the bowing or obligatory prostration in their substitution for sajdah al-tilawah do not require intention; the obligatory act substitutes for the greeting of the mosque even without intention. Some mashayikh said intention is needed. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that if he does not have intention at the time of bowing, it does not suffice. If he intends during the bow, there are two opinions. If he intends after raising his head from it, it is not valid by consensus. Most mashayikh did not specify a measure for the length of recitation; apparently they delegated that to the mujtahid's opinion. Some said: if he recites one or two verses, it is not long; if he recites three, it becomes long and enters the realm of making up. The apparent view is that three does not negate immediacy. Qadhi Khan chose that bowing outside prayer substitutes for it. And in al-Mujtaba: Bowing only substitutes with two conditions: one is intention, and the second is that there should not intervene between the recitation and the bowing three verses, except when the three verses are from the end of a surah like Bani Isra'il and Idha al-Sama'unshaqqat. And there is a difference of opinion regarding if he bows immediately for the prayer and prostrates: does the bowing suffice for sajdah al-tilawah or the prostration of the prayer? His saying: 'It is not valid by consensus' meaning by consensus of those who stipulated intention for its substitution. So in the marginal gloss of Nawh Afandi. His saying: 'And Qadhi Khan chose...' He said in al-Nahr: The reported view in the apparent is that it is permissible, as in al-Bazzaziyyah, but in my copies of al-Bazzaziyyah, it is in the non-apparent; and likewise I saw it in another copy of al-Bazzaziyyah. Then what is in al-Khaniyyah does not indicate his preference, for he said: It is reported that it is permissible. His saying: 'Is the sufficient for sajdah al-tilawah...'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This lengthy passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq continues the discussion on the substitution of ruku' for sajdah al-tilawah, now focusing on conditions and specific scenarios. The author summarizes: In prayer, it is preferable to prostrate for the sajdah verse. If one prostrates and stands up, it is disliked to then bow (as if for the prayer) right after raising the head. The timing matters: if the verse is in the middle of a surah, one should complete the surah and then bow. If near the end (e.g., remaining two or three verses), one may recite a few verses or another surah before bowing. The passage then discusses whether ruku' suffices for sajdah if one does not prostrate; the adopted view (by qiyas) is that it does. It cites a narration from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar allowing this, which is treated like consensus. It then refutes the opinion that only the obligatory prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) substitutes. It discusses intention (niyyah): for an immediate substitution, intention may not be required for the obligatory act, but some scholars require it. The condition of immediacy (fawr) is key: if one recites three or more verses after the ayat al-sajdah, the immediacy is broken and the ruku' no longer substitutes. Qadhi Khan's opinion that ruku' outside prayer can also substitute is mentioned but may be weak. The passage ends with a fragmented discussion about whether the ruku' or the prayer's sajdah suffices, citing various sources.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the requirement that the substitution (ruku' or sajdah) must be performed immediately after reciting the verse, without a significant delay.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention; the act of intending that the ruku' or sajdah is for fulfilling sajdah al-tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of later Hanafi scholars as presented in this passage, what breaks the condition of immediacy (fawr) and prevents ruku' from substituting for sajdah al-tilawah?
A) Reciting one additional verse after the ayat al-sajdah.
B) Reciting three or more verses after the ayat al-sajdah.
C) Performing another act of worship between recitation and ruku'.
D) Praying in a different language.

Key Takeaway
Ruku' in prayer substitutes for sajdah al-tilawah only if performed immediately (before reciting three more verses) and with proper intention; this is based on Companion practice and qiyas.

intermediate
8 min
Ruku' Substituting for Sujud al-Tilawah in Prayer
Establishes ruku' can replace sujud al-tilawah in prayer via qiyas and Sahabi practice, rejecting contrary views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ruku' substituting for sujud al-tilawah in prayer and explain the qiyas argument supporting it.

Core Idea
In prayer, ruku' suffices for sujud al-tilawah because qiyas and Sahabi practice outweigh istihsan.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq resolves a classical Hanafi debate: can bowing (ruku') replace the specific prostration of recitation (sujud al-tilawah) when recited inside prayer? The author presents the qiyas-istihsan conflict and explains why the school adopts qiyas, supported by the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar. The lesson walks through the reasoning and the scope of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is substituting ruku' for sujud al-tilawah in prayer. The ruling: it is valid (sahih) per the relied-upon view.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas equating ruku' and sujud as acts of humility, strengthened by the athar of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar who allowed it, with no reported opposition — forming near consensus.
Dalil is both qiyas and athar, considered like ijma'.
3
Trace wajh al-dalalah
The common illa is humility and worship. Both ruku' and sujud are acts of submission; the qiyas is jali (clear) because the meaning is apparent.
The apparent meaning (zahir) of the acts supports equality.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Istihsan says ruku' does not suffice; Muhammad ibn Salama says only the prayer's own sujud (sulbiyya) substitutes. The text rejects these.
The disagreement is within the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The school prefers qiyas because the apparent meaning is strong and the Sahabi practice constitutes near consensus, giving qiyas greater weight.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq sides with qiyas, adopting it from al-Asl.

آيتين
عند الختم فينبغي أن يقرأ آيات من سورة أخرى ثم يركع، وإن كان بقي إلى الختم قدر أو ثلاث كما في بني إسرائيل وإذا السماء انشقت ينبغي أن يقرأ بقية السورة ثم يركع، فإن وصل إليها سورة أخرى فهو أفضل، ولو لم يسجد وإنما ركع ذكر في الأصل أن القياس أنهما سواء والاستحسان أنه لا يجزئه وبالقياس نأخذ . - والتفاوت مابينهما أن ما ظهر من المعاني فقياس وما خفي فاستحسان ولا ترجيح في الخفي لخفائه ولا للظاهر لظهوره فيرجع إلى طلب الرجحان إلى ما اقترن بهما من المعاني، فمتى قوي الخفي أخذوا به، ومتى قوي الظاهر أخذوا به، وههنا قوي دليل القياس فأخذوا به لما روي عن ابن مسعود وابن عمر

طالت
أنهما أجازا أن يركع عن السجود في الصلاة ولم يرد عن غيرهما خلافه فكان كالإجماع. ثم اختلفوا في محل القياس والاستحسان؛ فذكر العامة أنه في إقامة الركوع مقام السجدة في الصلاة وقال بعضهم: إنه خارج الصلاة بأن تلاها في غير الصلاة فركع وليس هذا بسديد بل لا يجزئه ذلك قياساً واستحساناً، لأن الركوع خارج الصلاة لم يجعل قربة فلا ينوب مناب القربة. وعن محمد بن سلمة أن السجدة الصلبية هي التي تقوم مقام سجدة التلاوة لا الركوع. ويرده ما صرح به محمد في الكتاب كما أسلفناه.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. 217. Two verses. At the completion [of the surah], he should read verses from another surah then bow. And if there remains only one or three verses to the end, as in Bani Isra'il and Idha al-Sama'u Inshaqqat, he should read the rest of the surah then bow. If he connects to another surah, it is better. And if he did not prostrate but only bowed, it is mentioned in al-Asl that the qiyas is that they are equal, and istihsan is that it does not suffice him, and we take by qiyas. The difference between them is that what is apparent of meanings is qiyas and what is hidden is istihsan. There is no preference for the hidden due to its hiddenness nor for the apparent due to its apparentness, so one resorts to seeking preference through the meanings associated with them. So when the hidden is strong, they take it; when the apparent is strong, they take it. Here the proof of qiyas is strong, so they took it due to what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed bowing for prostration in prayer, and no opposition from others is reported, so it is like consensus. Then they differed about the locus of qiyas and istihsan: The general view is that it is in substituting ruku' for sajda in prayer. And some said: It is outside prayer, that he recited outside prayer and bowed. This is not correct; rather it does not suffice him by qiyas and istihsan, because bowing outside prayer is not made an act of worship, so it does not substitute for an act of worship. And from Muhammad ibn Salama that the obligatory prostration [of the prayer] is what substitutes for the tilawah prostration, not ruku'. It is refuted by what Muhammad explicitly stated in the book as we have previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. It begins with practical guidance: when reciting a sajda verse near the end of a surah, it is recommended to read a few verses from another surah before bowing for ruku'. If only one or three verses remain, it is better to read them and then bow. The core issue is whether bowing (ruku') can substitute for the specific prostration of recitation (sujud al-tilawah) in prayer. The author cites al-Asl (the foundational text by Imam Muhammad) which presents two positions: qiyas (analogy) equates ruku' and sujud as similar acts, so bowing would suffice; istihsan (juristic preference) says it does not. The school takes by qiyas because the proof for it is stronger, supported by the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar, which amounts to a near-consensus (ka-al-ijma'). Then a dispute arises about the scope: some say the substitution applies only inside prayer, others say it applies outside as well. The correct view is that outside prayer, bowing is not an independent act of worship, so it cannot substitute. Another objection from Muhammad ibn Salama holds that only the prayer's own prostration (al-sajda al-sulbiyya) can substitute for tilawah prostration, not ruku'. This is refuted by the explicit text of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) in al-Asl. Thus, the relied-upon position is that inside prayer, bowing (with conditions) suffices for sujud al-tilawah.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran; an act of worship in the Hanafi school.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that treats two cases equally due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas due to a stronger indication in a particular case.
ركوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer, a pillar (rukn). In this context, it is evaluated as a substitute for sujud al-tilawah.
سجدة صلبية (sajda sulbiyya): The obligatory prostration that is part of the prayer itself (not the extra tilawah prostration).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the primary reason that ruku' can substitute for sujud al-tilawah in prayer?
A) Because istihsan clearly indicates it.
B) Because qiyas, supported by the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar, is stronger.
C) Because the Quran explicitly commands it.
D) Because the consensus of all scholars is on this.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ruku' suffices for sujud al-tilawah inside prayer, based on qiyas and Sahabi practice, and this is the mufta bihi ruling.

Length of Recitation and Substitution for Sujud al-Tilawah
Details the condition of recitation length for substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on how the length of recitation after a sajda verse affects whether ruku' or sujud can substitute for sujud al-tilawah, and identify the threshold that makes the prostration a 'debt' (qada').

Core Idea
Short recitation (1-2 verses) allows substitution without intention; three verses or more turns it into a debt requiring separate performance.

Sujud al-tilawah is an immediate obligation upon reciting a sajda verse during prayer. However, Hanafi fiqh allows this prostration to be substituted by the prayer's own ruku' or sujud under certain conditions. A key condition is the length of recitation: if additional verses are recited after the sajda verse before performing the substitute, the obligation may become a debt (qada') that cannot be fulfilled by a simple bow. This lesson explores the dispute over the exact length that triggers this change and the practical implications for the worshiper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed: substituting ruku' or sujud for sujud al-tilawah. The passage rules that if the reading is long (taalat al-qira'ah), the prayer's own sujud does not substitute; if short, it may.
2
Define 'long reading'
The passage reports that most mashayikh left the definition to the mujtahid, but some set it at three verses. If one or two verses are read, it is short; three or more is long.
There is also an exception for verses from the end of a surah.
3
Understand the debt (qada') concept
When the reading becomes long, the tilawah prostration becomes a debt ('dian') that must be repaid with what one 'owns', not what one 'owes'. Since ruku' and sujud are themselves obligations (owed), they cannot repay the debt.
This is an analogy to financial debt repayment.
4
Apply to scenarios
Consider cases: if one recites a sajda verse and immediately bows, the bow substitutes; if one recites three more verses before bowing, the bow no longer suffices and a separate sujud al-tilawah is required after prayer.
The immediate bowing is a substitute only if reading was short.

ولو لم يركع القراءة لم يجز وإن نواه عن السجدة وكذا السجدة الصلبية لا تنوب عنها إذا طالت القراءة لأنها صارت ديناً لوجوبها مضيقاً والدين يقضي بما له لا بما عليه، والركوع والسجود عليه فلا يتأدى به الدين. وإذا لم تطل القراءة لا يحتاج الركوع أو السجدة الصلبية في إقامتهما عن سجود التلاوة إلى النية فالفرض ينوب عن تحية المسجد وإن لم ينو، ومن المشايخ من قال : يحتاج إلى النية. وذكر الأسبيجابي أنه لو لم توجد النية منه عند الركوع لا يجزئه، ولو نوى في الركوع فيه قولان ولونوى بعد رفع الرأس منه لا يجوز ،بالإجماع، وأكثر المشايخ لم يقدروا لطول القراءة شيئاً فكان الظاهر أنهم فوضوا ذلك إلى رأي المجتهد. وبعضهم قالوا : إن قرأ آية أو آيتين لم تطل وإن قرأ ثلاثاً طالت وصارت بمحل القضاء، والظاهر أن الثلاثة لا تعدم الفور اهـ. واختار قاضيخان أن الركوع خارج الصلاة ينوب عنها وفي المجتبى : وإنما ينوب الركوع عنها بشرطين: أحدهما النية، والثاني أن لا يتخلل بين التلاوة والركوع ثلاث آيات إلا إذا كانت الآيات الثلاث من آخر السورة كـ «بني إسرائيل وإذا السماء انشقت» اهـ. واختلف فيما إذا ركع على الفور للصلاة وسجد هل المجزئ عن سجدة التلاوة الركوع أو السجود؟ فقيل الركوع لأنه أقرب وقيل السجود لأن الركوع بدون النية لا يجزئ وفي السجود اختلاف وفائدته تظهر فيما إذا تلا الفاتحة وعشرين آية مثلاً آخرها آية السجدة وركع عقبهاثم رفع رأسه وقرأ عشر آيات مثلاً ثم سجد ولم يكن نواها في الركوع يجب عليه سجدة التلاوة على حدة، أما إذا سجد عقب الركوع فإنه خرج عن العهدة لا محالة في ظاهر الرواية نواها في الركوع أو لم ينو .اهـ. وفي القنية : ولو نواها في الركوع عقب التلاوة ولم ينوها المقتدي لا ينوب عنه ويسجد إذا سلم الإمام ويعيد القعدة ولوتركها تفسد صلاته اهـ. ثم قال : السجود أولى من الركوع لها في صلاة الجهر دون المخافته . وقيد المصنف بكونها لا تقضى خارجها لأنه لو أخرها من ركعة إلى ركعة فإنها تقضى ما دام في الصلاة لأن الصلاة واحدة لكن لا يلزم جواز التأخير، بل المراد الإجزاء لما في البدائع من أنها واجبة على الفور وأنه إذا أخرها حتى طالت القراءة تصير قضاء ويأثم لأن هذه السجدة صارت من الصلاة ملحقة بنفس التلاوة، ولذا فعلت فيها مع أنها ليست من أصل الصلاة بل زائدة بخلاف غير الصلاتية فإنها واجبة على التراخي على ما هو المختار اهـ .
