قوله : (وفي القنية ولو نواها في الركوع الخ) قال في النهر : وينبغي حمله على الجهرية ا هـ . قلت : لعل وجهه ـ والله تعالى أعلم - ما يأتي عن القنية أيضاً أن الركوع أولى في صلاة المخافتة، وعلله في التتارخانية بقوله : لئلا يلتبس الأمر على القوم فإنه يفيد أنه لا يلزم القوم نيتها في الركوع لأنه لا علم لهم بتلاوته وإلا لم يحصل عليهم التباس بخلاف الجهرية. قال بعض الفضلاء : فإن قلت لم لا ينوب السجود الذي بعد هذا الركوع عن السجدة التلاوية في حق المقتدي؟ قلت : لأنه لما نوى الإمام الركوع تعين له فلا ينوب عن سجدة التلاوية في حق المقتدي وإن نواه. فإن قلت: من أين
And if he did not bow during the recitation, it is not valid even if he intended it for the prostration. Likewise, the obligatory prostration [of the prayer] does not substitute for it when the reading is long, because it has become a debt due to its immediate obligation, and a debt is repaid with what one owns not what one owes; bowing and prostration are owed, so the debt is not fulfilled by them. And when the reading is not long, there is no need for intention for either bowing or the prayer's own prostration to substitute for the tilawah prostration, just as an obligatory prayer substitutes for the greeting of the mosque even without intention. Some mashayikh said: intention is needed. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that if he does not have intention at the time of bowing, it does not suffice; if he intends during bowing, there are two opinions; and if he intends after raising his head, it is not allowed by consensus. Most mashayikh did not specify a precise length for long reading, leaving it to the mujtahid's opinion. Some said: if he reads one or two verses, it is not long; if he reads three, it becomes long and becomes a matter of qada' (debt). The apparent view is that three does not eliminate fawr (immediacy). Qadi Khan chose that bowing outside prayer does substitute; in al-Mujtaba, bowing substitutes only with two conditions: one is intention, and the second is that no three verses intervene between recitation and bowing, except if the three verses are from the end of a surah like Bani Isra'il and Idha al-Sama'u Inshaqqat. And there is dispute: if he bowed immediately for the prayer and then prostrated, which suffices for tilawah prostration, the bowing or the prostration? It is said bowing because it is closer; and it is said prostration because bowing without intention does not suffice, and there is dispute about prostration. Its benefit appears if he recited al-Fatihah and twenty verses, the last being a sajda verse, and he bowed after it, then raised his head and recited ten verses, then prostrated without having intended it in the bowing, he must perform a separate tilawah prostration. But if he prostrated after bowing, he is absolved definitively in the apparent riwaya, whether he intended it in bowing or not. In al-Quniyya: if he intended it in bowing after recitation but the follower did not intend it, it does not substitute for the follower, and he must prostrate when the imam says salam and repeat the qa'dah; if he leaves it, his prayer is invalid. Then he said: prostration is better than bowing for it in loud prayer, not in quiet prayer. And the author restricted it to not being made up outside the prayer because if he delays it from one rak'ah to another, it is made up as long as he is in the prayer because the prayer is one; but permissibility of delay is not meant, rather sufficiency (ijza') is meant, as in al-Bada'i' that it is wajib immediately and if he delays until the reading becomes long, it becomes qada' and he sins, because this prostration has become part of the prayer attached to the recitation itself, so it is performed in it even though it is not part of the original prayer but supererogatory, unlike non-prayer prostrations which are wajib with delay according to the chosen view. [Commentary:] 'Dispute over actions, bowing or prostration.' I say: the apparent meaning is bowing with intention; otherwise, it seems that what suffices is prostration, as indicated by what we said: it is mentioned in al-Tatar Khaniyya from al-Muhit this hesitation, then he mentioned after it that there is no dispute that bowing does not substitute without intention, and dispute about prostration. On this, the author's statement 'because bowing...' is unclear. Reflect. 'And about prostration there is dispute' meaning dispute about its sufficiency without intention. Muhammad ibn Salama and a group of Balkh imams said: it does not substitute unless he intends; others said intention is not a condition. As for bowing, there is no that it does not substitute without intention. Thus mentioned by Shaykh Isma'il and others from al-Muhit. But it has passed from al-Bada'i' the equal treatment between bowing and prostration in not needing intention, which contradicts this. In al-Khulasa, they agreed that the tilawah prostration is fulfilled by the prayer's prostration even if he did not intend tilawah, and they differed about bowing. Al-Fath has transmitted from al-Bada'i' consensus on sufficiency of the prayer's sujud without intention, so it agrees with al-Khulasa and al-Bada'i' in opposition to al-Muhit in both sections. But al-Fath mentioned the full text of al-Bada'i' and at its end the explicit statement of the necessity of intention for the prayer's sujud to substitute for tilawah when the reading is not long, which is the original case. Then he said: thus what was transmitted earlier of consensus on not requiring intention is not correct. 'And in al-Quniyya: if he intended in bowing...' al-Nahr said: it should be interpreted for loud prayer. I say: perhaps its reason—Allah knows best—is what comes from al-Quniyya also that bowing is better in quiet prayer, and he stated in al-Tatar Khaniyya: so that the people are not confused, because it indicates that the people are not obliged to intend it in bowing since they do not know his recitation, otherwise no confusion would occur for them, unlike in loud prayer. Some virtuous ones said: if you say why does the prostration after this bowing not substitute for the tilawah prostration in the follower's case? I say: because when the imam intended bowing, it became specific to him, so it does not substitute for the tilawah prostration in the follower's case even if he intended it. If you say: from where...
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on substitution of ruku' or sujud for sujud al-tilawah, focusing on conditions and intra-Hanafi disputes. It begins with a ruling: if one does not bow at all after reciting a sajda verse, bowing later is invalid, even if intended. Similarly, the prayer's own sujud (sajda sulbiyya) cannot substitute if the reading was 'long' (taalat al-qira'ah), defined by some as three or more verses, because the prostration becomes an immediate debt that cannot be paid with an obligation (i.e., the prayer's sujud is owed, not owned). If the reading is short (one or two verses), the prayer's sujud may substitute without intention, just as a fard prayer suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid without specific intention. But many Hanafi scholars require intention for substitution by ruku'. There is a dispute about the exact length that makes the prostration a 'debt' (qada): most left it to the jurist's discretion, but some set three verses as the threshold. Qadi Khan held that bowing outside prayer can substitute (contrary to earlier), with conditions of intention and no three intervening verses except at surah ends. Then a dispute arises whether ruku' or the following sujud is the actual substitute: some say ruku' because it is closer to recitation; others say sujud because ruku' without intention fails, while sujud has different opinions. The practical benefit appears in a scenario where one recites many verses, bows without intention, then later prostrates: if sujud is the substitute, he is absolved; if ruku' was intended but without intention, he must repeat sujud al-tilawah separately. The passage also addresses the follower (muqtadi): if the imam intends in bowing, the follower's intention does not automatically substitute; the follower must still prostrate after the imam's salam, and if he leaves it, his prayer is invalid. There is a preference for sujud over ruku' in loud prayer, and ruku' in quiet prayer. Finally, it discusses the nature of sujud al-tilawah in prayer: it becomes part of the prayer and must be performed immediately; delay without valid cause makes it qada and sinful. The super-commentary (qala) clarifies disagreements about intention for sujud vs ruku', citing various sources like al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Khulasa, and al-Fath, concluding that the matter is contested and the relied-upon view requires intention for ruku' but not for sujud according to some. The text ends with a discussion of the follower's case in loud vs quiet prayer.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligation; here it refers to the tilawah prostration becoming a debt if delayed until the reading becomes long.
سجدة صُلبية (sajda sulbiyya): The prostration that is a pillar of the prayer, as opposed to the tilawah prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if a person reads three or more verses after a sajda verse and then bows?
A) The bow substitutes for sujud al-tilawah.
B) The bow does not substitute, and separate sujud al-tilawah is required.
C) The bow substitutes only if intended.
D) The entire prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
A bow (ruku') only substitutes for sujud al-tilawah if the recitation remains short (less than three additional verses) and, according to the majority, with proper intention.

Intention for Substitution and the Follower's Ruling
Details the intention requirement and the follower's case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether intention is required for ruku' and sujud to substitute for sujud al-tilawah, and apply the ruling for the follower (muqtadi) in congregational prayer.

Core Idea
Intention for substitution is required for ruku' but disputed for sujud; the follower must independently perform sujud al-tilawah if the imam's substitution does not include him.

A key point of debate among Hanafi jurists is whether a worshiper must consciously intend (niyyah) that his ruku' or sujud is meant to fulfill the obligation of sujud al-tilawah. The answer differs for bowing and prostrating, and also depends on whether one is praying alone or following an imam. This lesson examines the arguments and the practical consequences for the follower (muqtadi), who may not be covered by the imam's intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The passage discusses whether intention is required for the prayer's ruku' or sujud to substitute for sujud al-tilawah. Two main positions: some require intention for ruku', others do not; for sujud, there is disagreement.
2
Analyze the two views
View 1 (majority of Hanafi mashayikh): intention is needed for ruku' substitution; for sujud, some say intention is not needed based on al-Khulasa and al-Bada'i'. View 2 (some Balkh imams): intention is needed for both.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq leans towards requiring intention for ruku'.
3
Apply to the follower (muqtadi)
If the imam intends the ruku' to substitute for tilawah, that intention does not automatically benefit the follower. According to al-Quniyya, the follower must still perform sujud al-tilawah after the prayer, and if he omits it, his prayer becomes invalid.
This is because the follower's own intention is separate.
4
Distinguish loud vs quiet prayer
In loud prayer, sujud is preferred over ruku' for substitution; in quiet prayer, ruku' is preferred. This affects the follower's ability to know the imam's intention.
In quiet prayer, the followers may not know the imam's recitation, so they are not required to intend substitution in ruku'.

Source Text

ولو لم يركع القراءة لم يجز وإن نواه عن السجدة وكذا السجدة الصلبية لا تنوب عنها إذا طالت القراءة لأنها صارت ديناً لوجوبها مضيقاً والدين يقضي بما له لا بما عليه، والركوع والسجود عليه فلا يتأدى به الدين. وإذا لم تطل القراءة لا يحتاج الركوع أو السجدة الصلبية في إقامتهما عن سجود التلاوة إلى النية فالفرض ينوب عن تحية المسجد وإن لم ينو، ومن المشايخ من قال : يحتاج إلى النية. وذكر الأسبيجابي أنه لو لم توجد النية منه عند الركوع لا يجزئه، ولو نوى في الركوع فيه قولان ولونوى بعد رفع الرأس منه لا يجوز ،بالإجماع، وأكثر المشايخ لم يقدروا لطول القراءة شيئاً فكان الظاهر أنهم فوضوا ذلك إلى رأي المجتهد. وبعضهم قالوا : إن قرأ آية أو آيتين لم تطل وإن قرأ ثلاثاً طالت وصارت بمحل القضاء، والظاهر أن الثلاثة لا تعدم الفور اهـ. واختار قاضيخان أن الركوع خارج الصلاة ينوب عنها وفي المجتبى : وإنما ينوب الركوع عنها بشرطين: أحدهما النية، والثاني أن لا يتخلل بين التلاوة والركوع ثلاث آيات إلا إذا كانت الآيات الثلاث من آخر السورة كـ «بني إسرائيل وإذا السماء انشقت» اهـ. واختلف فيما إذا ركع على الفور للصلاة وسجد هل المجزئ عن سجدة التلاوة الركوع أو السجود؟ فقيل الركوع لأنه أقرب وقيل السجود لأن الركوع بدون النية لا يجزئ وفي السجود اختلاف وفائدته تظهر فيما إذا تلا الفاتحة وعشرين آية مثلاً آخرها آية السجدة وركع عقبهاثم رفع رأسه وقرأ عشر آيات مثلاً ثم سجد ولم يكن نواها في الركوع يجب عليه سجدة التلاوة على حدة، أما إذا سجد عقب الركوع فإنه خرج عن العهدة لا محالة في ظاهر الرواية نواها في الركوع أو لم ينو .اهـ. وفي القنية : ولو نواها في الركوع عقب التلاوة ولم ينوها المقتدي لا ينوب عنه ويسجد إذا سلم الإمام ويعيد القعدة ولوتركها تفسد صلاته اهـ. ثم قال : السجود أولى من الركوع لها في صلاة الجهر دون المخافته . وقيد المصنف بكونها لا تقضى خارجها لأنه لو أخرها من ركعة إلى ركعة فإنها تقضى ما دام في الصلاة لأن الصلاة واحدة لكن لا يلزم جواز التأخير، بل المراد الإجزاء لما في البدائع من أنها واجبة على الفور وأنه إذا أخرها حتى طالت القراءة تصير قضاء ويأثم لأن هذه السجدة صارت من الصلاة ملحقة بنفس التلاوة، ولذا فعلت فيها مع أنها ليست من أصل الصلاة بل زائدة بخلاف غير الصلاتية فإنها واجبة على التراخي على ما هو المختار اهـ .

قوله : (وفي القنية ولو نواها في الركوع الخ) قال في النهر : وينبغي حمله على الجهرية ا هـ . قلت : لعل وجهه ـ والله تعالى أعلم - ما يأتي عن القنية أيضاً أن الركوع أولى في صلاة المخافتة، وعلله في التتارخانية بقوله : لئلا يلتبس الأمر على القوم فإنه يفيد أنه لا يلزم القوم نيتها في الركوع لأنه لا علم لهم بتلاوته وإلا لم يحصل عليهم التباس بخلاف الجهرية. قال بعض الفضلاء : فإن قلت لم لا ينوب السجود الذي بعد هذا الركوع عن السجدة التلاوية في حق المقتدي؟ قلت : لأنه لما نوى الإمام الركوع تعين له فلا ينوب عن سجدة التلاوية في حق المقتدي وإن نواه. فإن قلت: من أين
And if he did not bow during the recitation, it is not valid even if he intended it for the prostration. Likewise, the obligatory prostration [of the prayer] does not substitute for it when the reading is long, because it has become a debt due to its immediate obligation, and a debt is repaid with what one owns not what one owes; bowing and prostration are owed, so the debt is not fulfilled by them. And when the reading is not long, there is no need for intention for either bowing or the prayer's own prostration to substitute for the tilawah prostration, just as an obligatory prayer substitutes for the greeting of the mosque even without intention. Some mashayikh said: intention is needed. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that if he does not have intention at the time of bowing, it does not suffice; if he intends during bowing, there are two opinions; and if he intends after raising his head, it is not allowed by consensus. Most mashayikh did not specify a precise length for long reading, leaving it to the mujtahid's opinion. Some said: if he reads one or two verses, it is not long; if he reads three, it becomes long and becomes a matter of qada' (debt). The apparent view is that three does not eliminate fawr (immediacy). Qadi Khan chose that bowing outside prayer does substitute; in al-Mujtaba, bowing substitutes only with two conditions: one is intention, and the second is that no three verses intervene between recitation and bowing, except if the three verses are from the end of a surah like Bani Isra'il and Idha al-Sama'u Inshaqqat. And there is dispute: if he bowed immediately for the prayer and then prostrated, which suffices for tilawah prostration, the bowing or the prostration? It is said bowing because it is closer; and it is said prostration because bowing without intention does not suffice, and there is dispute about prostration. Its benefit appears if he recited al-Fatihah and twenty verses, the last being a sajda verse, and he bowed after it, then raised his head and recited ten verses, then prostrated without having intended it in the bowing, he must perform a separate tilawah prostration. But if he prostrated after bowing, he is absolved definitively in the apparent riwaya, whether he intended it in bowing or not. In al-Quniyya: if he intended it in bowing after recitation but the follower did not intend it, it does not substitute for the follower, and he must prostrate when the imam says salam and repeat the qa'dah; if he leaves it, his prayer is invalid. Then he said: prostration is better than bowing for it in loud prayer, not in quiet prayer. And the author restricted it to not being made up outside the prayer because if he delays it from one rak'ah to another, it is made up as long as he is in the prayer because the prayer is one; but permissibility of delay is not meant, rather sufficiency (ijza') is meant, as in al-Bada'i' that it is wajib immediately and if he delays until the reading becomes long, it becomes qada' and he sins, because this prostration has become part of the prayer attached to the recitation itself, so it is performed in it even though it is not part of the original prayer but supererogatory, unlike non-prayer prostrations which are wajib with delay according to the chosen view. [Commentary:] 'Dispute over actions, bowing or prostration.' I say: the apparent meaning is bowing with intention; otherwise, it seems that what suffices is prostration, as indicated by what we said: it is mentioned in al-Tatar Khaniyya from al-Muhit this hesitation, then he mentioned after it that there is no dispute that bowing does not substitute without intention, and dispute about prostration. On this, the author's statement 'because bowing...' is unclear. Reflect. 'And about prostration there is dispute' meaning dispute about its sufficiency without intention. Muhammad ibn Salama and a group of Balkh imams said: it does not substitute unless he intends; others said intention is not a condition. As for bowing, there is no that it does not substitute without intention. Thus mentioned by Shaykh Isma'il and others from al-Muhit. But it has passed from al-Bada'i' the equal treatment between bowing and prostration in not needing intention, which contradicts this. In al-Khulasa, they agreed that the tilawah prostration is fulfilled by the prayer's prostration even if he did not intend tilawah, and they differed about bowing. Al-Fath has transmitted from al-Bada'i' consensus on sufficiency of the prayer's sujud without intention, so it agrees with al-Khulasa and al-Bada'i' in opposition to al-Muhit in both sections. But al-Fath mentioned the full text of al-Bada'i' and at its end the explicit statement of the necessity of intention for the prayer's sujud to substitute for tilawah when the reading is not long, which is the original case. Then he said: thus what was transmitted earlier of consensus on not requiring intention is not correct. 'And in al-Quniyya: if he intended in bowing...' al-Nahr said: it should be interpreted for loud prayer. I say: perhaps its reason—Allah knows best—is what comes from al-Quniyya also that bowing is better in quiet prayer, and he stated in al-Tatar Khaniyya: so that the people are not confused, because it indicates that the people are not obliged to intend it in bowing since they do not know his recitation, otherwise no confusion would occur for them, unlike in loud prayer. Some virtuous ones said: if you say why does the prostration after this bowing not substitute for the tilawah prostration in the follower's case? I say: because when the imam intended bowing, it became specific to him, so it does not substitute for the tilawah prostration in the follower's case even if he intended it. If you say: from where...
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on substitution of ruku' or sujud for sujud al-tilawah, focusing on conditions and intra-Hanafi disputes. It begins with a ruling: if one does not bow at all after reciting a sajda verse, bowing later is invalid, even if intended. Similarly, the prayer's own sujud (sajda sulbiyya) cannot substitute if the reading was 'long' (taalat al-qira'ah), defined by some as three or more verses, because the prostration becomes an immediate debt that cannot be paid with an obligation (i.e., the prayer's sujud is owed, not owned). If the reading is short (one or two verses), the prayer's sujud may substitute without intention, just as a fard prayer suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid without specific intention. But many Hanafi scholars require intention for substitution by ruku'. There is a dispute about the exact length that makes the prostration a 'debt' (qada): most left it to the jurist's discretion, but some set three verses as the threshold. Qadi Khan held that bowing outside prayer can substitute (contrary to earlier), with conditions of intention and no three intervening verses except at surah ends. Then a dispute arises whether ruku' or the following sujud is the actual substitute: some say ruku' because it is closer to recitation; others say sujud because ruku' without intention fails, while sujud has different opinions. The practical benefit appears in a scenario where one recites many verses, bows without intention, then later prostrates: if sujud is the substitute, he is absolved; if ruku' was intended but without intention, he must repeat sujud al-tilawah separately. The passage also addresses the follower (muqtadi): if the imam intends in bowing, the follower's intention does not automatically substitute; the follower must still prostrate after the imam's salam, and if he leaves it, his prayer is invalid. There is a preference for sujud over ruku' in loud prayer, and ruku' in quiet prayer. Finally, it discusses the nature of sujud al-tilawah in prayer: it becomes part of the prayer and must be performed immediately; delay without valid cause makes it qada and sinful. The super-commentary (qala) clarifies disagreements about intention for sujud vs ruku', citing various sources like al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Khulasa, and al-Fath, concluding that the matter is contested and the relied-upon view requires intention for ruku' but not for sujud according to some. The text ends with a discussion of the follower's case in loud vs quiet prayer.

Key Terms
نِيَّة (niyyah): Intention to perform sujud al-tilawah through the ruku' or sujud of the prayer.
مقتدي (muqtadi): A follower in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a follower in a quiet prayer does not intend the ruku' for sujud al-tilawah but the imam did?
A) The follower is excused because he cannot hear the recitation.
B) The follower must perform sujud al-tilawah after the prayer and repeat the qa'dah.
C) The follower's prayer is invalid because he omitted the obligation.
D) The imam's intention covers the follower.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the follower's obligation to perform sujud al-tilawah is not automatically fulfilled by the imam's intention; the follower must independently ensure its performance.

intermediate

Sujūd al-Tilāwah: Reciting Sajdah Verses Both Outside and Inside Prayer
Expands the ruling on sujūd al-tilāwah when recited both outside and inside prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on sujūd al-tilāwah when a sajdah verse is recited both outside and inside prayer, determining whether one prostration suffices and identifying the conditions for valid performance.

Core Idea
One prostration in prayer covers recitations outside and inside prayer if the assembly (majlis) is united.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario from the Hanafi fiqh of sujūd al-tilāwah: a person recites a sajdah verse outside prayer, prostrates, and then later recites the same verse inside prayer. The central question is whether the prostration performed in prayer suffices for both recitations. The passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq presents two opinions and clarifies the relied-upon position, along with important details about intention and the follower's situation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal problem
A person recites a sajdah verse outside prayer, performs sujūd al-tilāwah, then later recites the same verse inside prayer. Does the prostration in prayer cover the earlier recitation, or must he prostrate again?
The key factor is whether the recitations occur in the same 'assembly' (majlis).
2
Examine the two opinions mentioned
Some scholars say ruku' (bowing) can substitute for sajdah in prayer because it is closer, but others argue that sajdah is required because ruku' without intention does not suffice. Note the disagreement even about sajdah without intention.
The text does not name the scholars; it presents the ikhtilāf generically.
3
Apply the relied-upon view (zāhir al-riwāyah)
According to the apparent transmission (zāhir al-riwāyah), if one prostrates after bowing (or intends the sajdah in ruku'?), it counts regardless of intention. However, if one does not intend it in ruku' and only prostrates later, a separate prostration is needed.
The practical illustration with reciting 20 verses clarifies this.
4
Distinguish between prayer and non-prayer prostrations
Inside prayer, sujūd al-tilāwah is attached to the prayer and is obligatory immediately (fawran). Outside prayer, it is obligatory with delay (tarākhī) according to the chosen view. Delaying inside prayer until the recitation becomes long makes it a make-up (qadā') and involves sin.
This distinction affects whether one can delay the prostration within the same prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقتد سجدها ولم تقض الصلاتية خارجها ولو تلاها خارج الصلاة فسجد وأعادها فيها السجود؟ فقيل الركوع لأنه أقرب وقيل السجود لأن الركوع بدون النية لا يجزئ وفي السجود اختلاف وفائدته تظهر فيما إذا تلا الفاتحة وعشرين آية مثلاً آخرها آية السجدة وركع عقبها ثم رفع رأسه وقرأ عشر آيات مثلاً ثم سجد ولم يكن نواها في الركوع يجب عليه سجدة التلاوة على حدة، أما إذا سجد عقب الركوع فإنه خرج عن العهدة لا محالة في ظاهر الرواية نواها في الركوع أو لم ينو .اهـ. وفي القنية : ولو نواها في الركوع عقب التلاوة ولم ينوها المقتدي لا ينوب عنه ويسجد إذا سلم الإمام ويعيد القعدة ولوتركها تفسد صلاته اهـ. ثم قال : السجود أولى من الركوع لها في صلاة الجهر دون المخافته . وقيد المصنف بكونها لا تقضى خارجها لأنه لو أخرها من ركعة إلى ركعة فإنها تقضى ما دام في الصلاة لأن الصلاة واحدة لكن لا يلزم جواز التأخير، بل المراد الإجزاء لما في البدائع من أنها واجبة على الفور وأنه إذا أخرها حتى طالت القراءة تصير قضاء ويأثم لأن هذه السجدة صارت من الصلاة ملحقة بنفس التلاوة، ولذا فعلت فيها مع أنها ليست من أصل الصلاة بل زائدة بخلاف غير الصلاتية فإنها واجبة على التراخي على ما هو المختار اهـ.
If he follows [the Imam] and prostrates, and the prayer prostration does not suffice for [recitations] outside it. And if he recites it outside prayer and prostrates, and then recites it again in prayer, [does he need] another prostration? Some said: bowing (ruku') because it is closer; some said: prostration because bowing without intention does not suffice, and there is disagreement about prostration. Its benefit appears when he recited al-Fatiha and twenty verses ending with a prostration verse, bowed after it, then raised his head and recited ten more verses, then prostrated without having intended it in bowing: he must perform a separate prostration of recitation. But if he prostrated after bowing, he fulfills the requirement inevitably in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), whether he intended it in bowing or not. End. And in al-Qunyah: If he intended it in bowing after recitation, but the follower did not intend it, it does not suffice for him; he prostrates when the Imam says salam and repeats the sitting; if he omits it, his prayer is invalid. End. Then he said: Prostration is preferable to bowing for it in loud prayer, not in quiet prayer. The author restricted it to not being made up outside prayer because if he delays it from one rak'ah to another, it is made up as long as he is in prayer because the prayer is one. But this does not permit delay; rather, it means acceptance. According to al-Bada'i', it is obligatory immediately, and if he delays it until the recitation becomes long, it becomes a make-up and he sins because this prostration became part of the prayer attached to the recitation itself. Hence, it is performed in it even though it is not part of the original prayer but an addition, unlike the non-prayer prostration that is obligatory with delay according to the chosen view. End.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the sharh (expansion) of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses the case of a person who recites an ayah of sajdah outside prayer, then recites it again inside prayer. The question is whether one prostration suffices for both recitations. The author mentions two opinions: some say ruku' (bowing) can substitute because it is closer, but others say sajdah (prostration) is needed because ruku' without niyyah (intention) is insufficient. There is disagreement about whether sajdah without niyyah suffices. The practical benefit appears when someone recites a long passage ending with a prostration verse, bows, then later prostrates without intention: he needs a separate prostration. However, if he prostrates after bowing, it counts in zahir al-riwaya regardless of intention. The passage also quotes al-Qunyah regarding a follower who does not intend the prostration in the imam's ruku' – the follower must prostrate after the imam's salam and repeat the sitting; otherwise the prayer is invalid. Then it states that in loud prayer, sajdah is preferred over ruku' for this prostration. The author comments on the matn's restriction that the prostration is not made up outside prayer: if delayed within the same prayer, it is made up (qada') because the prayer is a single unit, but delay is not permissible without necessity. According to al-Bada'i', it is obligatory immediately (fawran); delay until lengthy recitation makes it a make-up and sinful, because the prostration becomes annexed to the recitation within the prayer. This contrasts with non-prayer prostrations (ghayr salatiyyah) which are obligatory with delay (tarakhi) according to the chosen view.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that commands prostration.
صلاتية (ṣalātiyyah): The prostration of recitation performed during the prayer while in the state of prayer.
الغير صلاتية (ghayr al-ṣalātiyyah): The prostration of recitation performed outside of prayer, i.e., when not in salah.
اتحاد المجلس (ittiḥād al-majlis): The unity of the sitting or place where recitation occurs; if one recites multiple sajdah verses in one sitting, one prostration may suffice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi relied-upon view (zāhir al-riwāyah), what is required when a sajdah verse is recited outside prayer and then again inside prayer in the same assembly?
A) Two separate prostrations are always required.
B) The prostration inside prayer suffices for both recitations.
C) The prostration outside prayer must be repeated inside.
D) Only the outside prostration counts; the inside recitation requires a separate sajdah.

Key Takeaway
One prostration in prayer suffices for recitations both outside and inside prayer if the assembly (majlis) is united, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Ruku' and Sajdah as Substitutes for Sajdah al-Tilawah: Intention Requirements
Presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether ruku' can substitute for prostration of recitation and whether intention is required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi positions on whether ruku' can substitute for sajdah al-tilawah and explain the requirement of intention for each act.

Core Idea
Ruku' requires intention to substitute for sajdah; sajdah of prayer suffices without intention according to the relied-upon view.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a worshipper fulfill the obligatory prostration of recitation by bowing or prostrating during prayer, and does intention matter? Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks the positions from al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Khulasah, and al-Fath, revealing a subtle methodological divide between zahir al-riwaya and later scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts in question
The acts are ruku' (bowing) and sajdah (prostration) performed during prayer. The question is whether either can fulfill the wajib of sajdah al-tilawah after reciting a sajdah verse.
2
Note the disagreement on sajdah
Muhammad ibn Salamah and a group from Balkh hold that intention (niyyah) is required for sajdah to substitute. Others, including the majority, say intention is not a condition. The relied-upon view is that it is not required.
The passage cites al-Khulasah reporting consensus on sajdah without intention.
3
Observe the consensus on ruku'
There is no disagreement that ruku' does not substitute for sajdah al-tilawah without intention. Intention is necessary.
This is reported from al-Muhit and accepted by all.
4
Evaluate the source conflict
Al-Bada'i' appears to treat ruku' and sajdah equally (both require no intention), but al-Fath clarifies that al-Bada'i' explicitly requires intention when the recitation is not long. Thus the alleged consensus on sajdah being unconditional is challenged.
Later Hanafi master al-Fath reconciles the sources.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that sajdah suffice without intention, but ruku' does not. This is the position of zahir al-riwaya supported by al-Khulasah and al-Bada'i' as interpreted by al-Fath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلاف أفعال الركوع أو السجود) أقول : الظاهر أن المراد الركوع مع النية وإلا فالذي يظهر تعين أن المجزي هو السجود يدل على ما قلناه أنه ذكر في التتارخانية عن المحيط هذا الترديد، ثم ذكر عقبه أنه لا خلاف أن الركوع لا ينوب بدون النية وذكر الخلاف في السجود تأمل. وعلى هذا فقول المؤلف «لأن الركوع الخ» غير ظاهر تأمل قوله : (وفي السجود اختلاف) أي اختلاف في أجزائه بدون النية فقال محمد بن سلمة وجماعة من أئمة بلخ: لا ينوب ما لم ينو، وغيرهم قالوا النية ليست بشرط وأما الركوع فلا في أنه لا ينوب بدون النية هكذا ذكره الشيخ إسماعيل وغيره عن المحيط، لكن قد مر عن البدائع التسوية بين الركوع والسجود في عدم الاحتياج إلى النية فهو مخالف لما هنا، وفي الخلاصة أجمعوا أن سجدة التلاوة تتأدى بسجدة الصلاة وإن لم ينو التلاوة واختلفوا في الركوع. وقد نقل في الفتح عن البدائع الإجماع على إجزاء الصلبية بدون نية فتوافق ما في الخلاصة والبدائع على مخالفة ما في المحيط في الفصلين لكن ذكر في الفتح عبارة البدائع بطولها وفي آخرها التصريح بوجوب النية في إيقاع الصلبية عن التلاوة فيما إذا لم تطل القراءة على ما هو أصل الصورة ثم قال : فلم يصح ما تقدم من نقل الإجماع على عدم اشتراطها ا هـ .
(Disagreement concerning the actions of bowing or prostration.) I say: The apparent meaning is bowing with intention; otherwise, it appears that what suffices is prostration. This is indicated by what we said: in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muhit, this hesitation is mentioned, then after it, there is no disagreement that bowing does not substitute without intention, and disagreement on prostration is considered. According to this, the author's statement 'because bowing...' is not apparent. Consider his statement: 'And in prostration there is disagreement' i.e., disagreement regarding its sufficiency without intention. Muhammad ibn Salamah and a group of scholars from Balkh said: It does not suffice unless he intends. Others said intention is not a condition. As for bowing, there is no disagreement that it does not suffice without intention. Thus Sheikh Isma'il and others reported from al-Muhit. But it has passed from al-Bada'i' the equal treatment between bowing and prostration in not needing intention, which contradicts what is here. And in al-Khulasah: They agreed that the prostration of recitation is performed by the prostration of prayer even if he did not intend recitation, but they disagreed on bowing. And it is transmitted in al-Fath from al-Bada'i' consensus on the sufficiency of the prayer prostration without intention, so it agrees with al-Khulasah and al-Bada'i' in opposing what is in al-Muhit in both chapters. But al-Fath mentions the full text of al-Bada'i' and at its end, the explicit statement of the necessity of intention in performing the prayer prostration for recitation when the recitation is not long, as per the original case. Then he said: So what was previously transmitted of consensus on not requiring it is not correct. End.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding whether ruku' (bowing) can substitute for the prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah) during prayer, and whether intention (niyyah) is required. The author (Ibn Nujaym) comments on the matn's statement 'disagreement concerning the actions of bowing or prostration'. He clarifies that the intended meaning is bowing with intention; otherwise, only prostration suffices. The text reports from al-Tatarkhaniyyah citing al-Muhit that there is no dispute that ruku' without intention does not substitute, but there is disagreement on prostration: Muhammad ibn Salamah and a group from Balkh hold that intention is necessary for prostration to suffice, while others say intention is not a condition. The author notes that al-Bada'i' treats bowing and prostration equally, not requiring intention, contradicting al-Muhit. Al-Khulasah reports consensus that the prayer prostration suffices for recitation even without intention, but there is disagreement on ruku'. Al-Fath cites al-Bada'i' as explicitly requiring intention in the original case (when recitation is not long), thereby refuting the alleged consensus. The passage thus highlights a key methodological difference: the authority of different sources (zahir al-riwaya vs. nawadir) and how later scholars reconciled them.

Key Terms
الركوع (al-rukūʿ): Bowing in prayer, which some consider a possible substitute for sajdah al-tilawah if done with intention after reciting a sajdah verse.
الصلبية (al-ṣalbiyyah): The prostration that is part of prayer (i.e., the sajdah performed in each rak'ah), distinct from the prostration of recitation.
نية (niyyah): Intention; here specifically the intention to perform sajdah al-tilawah when bowing or prostrating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view in this passage, what is required for ruku' (bowing) to substitute for sajdah al-tilawah?
A) No intention is needed.
B) Intention is necessary.
C) It can never substitute.
D) It substitutes only in loud prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ruku' does not substitute for sajdah al-tilawah without intention, but the prayer’s own prostration does suffice without separate intention according to the relied-upon view.

Unity of Assembly and Overlap of Sajdah Prostrations
Commentary on conditions for overlapping sajdah prostrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of unity of assembly (ittihād al-majlis) to determine when a single sajdah al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations inside and outside prayer.

Core Idea
One prostration in prayer covers both outside and inside recitations if the assembly is united.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi school: when a person recites a sajdah verse outside prayer and then again inside the same prayer assembly, does one prostration suffice? The commentary from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the principle of tadākhul (overlap) based on the strength of the prayer prostration and the unity of the assembly. Understanding this rule clarifies common scenarios in daily worship and deepens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists reason about overlapping obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The passage addresses the case where a sajdah verse is recited outside prayer (e.g., while sitting at home), then later recited again during a prayer in the same general setting (e.g., the same prayer itself). Note whether a prostration was already done outside.
The ruling depends on the order and the presence of an earlier prostration.
2
Apply the Principle of Tadākhul
Recognize that tadākhul (overlap) allows one act (prayer prostration) to cover multiple triggers (recitations) if the assembly (majlis) is the same. This is based on the Hanafi rule that acts of worship in the same category can overlap under certain conditions.
Tadākhul is a recurring concept in Hanafi fiqh, e.g., in wudu, ghusl, and prayers.
3
Determine the Stronger Element
The passage states that the prayer prostration is 'stronger' (aqwā) than the outside prostration because it is part of the prayer. Therefore, the weaker (outside) becomes subordinate to the stronger, so one prayer prostration suffices for both recitations.
The concept of strength (quwwa) is based on the link to the prayer which has its own requirement for prostration.
4
Check the Condition of Unity of Assembly
If the assembly changes (e.g., the outside recitation occurred in a different place or after the prayer ended), separate prostrations are required. Unity of assembly is a necessary condition for overlap to apply.
The passage emphasizes that ittihād al-majlis must exist; otherwise, each recitation demands its own prostration.
5
Handle the Case of First Recitation Inside Prayer
If the first recitation was inside prayer (e.g., during the prayer itself) and after salam the verse is recited again, a new prostration is required because the first recitation has no legal existence after the prayer ends.
The passage uses the principle that the first recitation 'has no existence' after salam, so it cannot be counted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو تلاها خارج الصلاة فسجد وأعادها فيها) أي أعاد تلاوتها في الصلاة (سجد أخرى) لأن الصلاتية أقوى فلا تكون تبعاً للأضعف قوله ( وإن لم يسجد أو لا كفته واحدة) وهي صلاتية تنوب عنها وعن الخارجية لأن المجلس متحد والصلاتية أقوى فصارت الأولى تبعاً لها، فلو لم يسجد في الصلاة سقطتا لأن الخارجية أخذت حكم الصلاتية فسقطت تبعاً لها . أراد بالاكتفاء أن يكون بشرط اتحاد المجلس فإن تبدل مجلس التلاوة مع مجلس الصلاة فلكل سجدة . وإنما أفردها بالذكر مع دخولها تحت قوله كمن كررها في مجلس لا في مجلسين لمخالفتها لها في أنه إذا سجد للخارجية لا تكفي عن الصلاتية بخلاف ما إذا لم تكن صلاتية وسجد للأولى ثم أعادها فإن السجدة السابقة تكفي . والحاصل أنه يجب التداخل في هذه على وجه تكون الثانية مستتبعة للأولى إن لم يسجد للأولى لأن اتحاد المجلس يوجب التداخل، وكون الثانية قوية منع من جعل الأولى مستتبعة إذ استتباع الضعيف للقوي عكس المعقول ونقض للأصول فوجب التداخل على الوجه المذكور. وأشار إلى أنه لو تلاها المصلي بعدما سمعها من غيره مرة أو مراراً تكفيه سجدة واحدة. وقيد بكون الأولى تلاها خارج الصلاة لأنه لو قرأها في الصلاة أولاً ثم سلم فأعادها في مكانه ذكر في كتاب الصلاة أنه يلزمه أخرى لأن المتلوة في الصلاة لا وجود لها لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، والموجود هو الذي يستتبع دون المعدوم بخلاف ما إذا كانت الأولى خارجة فإنها باقية بعد
His statement: 'If he recites it outside prayer and prostrates, and repeats it in prayer' i.e., he repeats the recitation in prayer (then he prostrates another) because the prayer prostration is stronger, so it cannot be subordinate to the weaker. His statement: 'And if he does not prostrate, or one suffices him' means a single prostration, which is the prayer one, suffices for both the inside and outside recitations because the assembly (majlis) is united and the prayer prostration is stronger, so the former becomes subordinate to it. If he did not prostrate in prayer, both are dropped because the outside one took the ruling of the prayer one and thus dropped in its wake. He meant by 'sufficing' that it is conditional on unity of the assembly. If the assembly of recitation changes from the assembly of prayer, then each has its own prostration. He singled it out for mention even though it falls under his statement 'like one who repeats it in one assembly, not in two' because it differs from it in that if he prostrates for the outside one, it does not suffice for the prayer one, unlike when there is no prayer one and he prostrates for the first and then repeats it: the previous prostration suffices. The summary: There must be overlapping (tadakhul) in such a way that the second is a follower of the first if he did not prostrate for the first, because unity of assembly necessitates overlapping, and because the second is strong prevents making the first a follower, since a weak one following a strong one is contrary to reason and violates principles, so overlapping must be in the mentioned manner. He indicated that if the prayer recites it after hearing it from someone else once or repeatedly, one prostration suffices. He restricted it to the first being recited outside prayer because if he recited it in prayer first, then said salam and repeated it in the same place, it is mentioned in the Book of Prayer that he must do another because the recited verse in prayer has no existence, neither in reality nor legally; what exists is what follows, not the non-existent. Unlike when the first is outside, it remains after.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the ruling on reciting a sajdah verse outside prayer, then inside prayer, and the effect of prostration. The key point is that if the assembly (majlis) is the same when reciting both outside and inside prayer, one prostration in prayer suffices for both, because the prayer prostration is stronger (aqwā) and the outside recitation becomes subordinate. However, if the assembly changes (e.g., the outside recitation occurred in a different place or time), separate prostrations are required. The passage clarifies that if one prostrates for the outside recitation first, it does not cover the later prayer recitation; rather, the prayer prostration is needed. The underlying principle is tadakhul (overlap) based on unity of assembly. The author also notes that if the first recitation was inside prayer and then after salam one repeats it, a new prostration is required because the first recitation 'has no existence' in legal terms (it was part of the prayer which has ended). The passage reinforces the importance of ittihad al-majlis and the relative strength of prayer-based acts.

Key Terms
اتحاد المجلس (ittiḥād al-majlis): The condition that multiple recitations of sajdah verses occur in the same sitting or place (e.g., within the same prayer or same session outside prayer) for one prostration to suffice.
التداخل (al-tadākhul): The overlapping of multiple acts such that one suffices for all, e.g., one prostration for multiple recitations in the same assembly.
المقتدي (al-muqtadī): The follower in prayer, who is bound by the imam's actions but may need to supplement his own intention for sajdah al-tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the condition for one prostration to suffice for recitations both outside and inside prayer?
A) The outside recitation must be performed first.
B) The inside recitation must be followed by a separate intention.
C) The assembly (majlis) must be the same for both recitations.
D) The outside recitation must be recited loudly.

Key Takeaway
One sajdah al-tilawah in prayer can cover outside recitations only if both occur in the same assembly, due to the stronger nature of the prayer prostration and the principle of tadakhul.

One Prostration for Multiple Recitations in One Sitting
Commentary explaining the matn: one prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that one sujud al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations of a sajdah verse in one sitting, and identify the condition of unity of sitting.

Core Idea
Multiple recitations in one sitting require only one prostration – the cause is merged.

When you recite or hear the same sajdah verse multiple times in a single sitting, do you need to prostrate each time? The Hanafi school, relying on the Prophet's practice and the principle of hardship, rules that one prostration suffices. This lesson unpacks the rule and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Consider a person who recites the same sajdah verse multiple times in one gathering (sitting) without any interruption that changes the sitting.
The sitting (majlis) is defined by the physical place and continuity of the gathering.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, one prostration is sufficient for all those recitations.
This is based on the principle of tadakhul (overlapping) in the cause.
3
Cite the primary evidence
The hadith of Jibril (as) descending multiple times with the sajdah verse, and the Prophet (saw) prostrating only once.
The hadith is narrated by several companions and is considered zanni al-thubut.
4
Explain the legal basis
The sitting gathers scattered acts; requiring a prostration for each recitation would cause hardship, especially for teachers and students, and hardship is removed in Shariah.
Also, the principle 'al-majlis jami' al-mutafarriqat' (the sitting unites the scattered) is applied.
5
Identify the condition and exceptions
The condition is unity of the sitting (ittihad al-majlis). If the sitting changes (e.g., by leaving or speaking), then each recitation requires its own prostration.
The change of sitting can be actual or legal (e.g., by prayer).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة

قوله (ولو تلاها خارج الصلاة فسجد وأعادها فيها أي أعاد تلاوتها في الصلاة (سجد أخرى لأن الصلاتية أقوى فلا تكون تبعاً للأضعف قوله ( وإن لم يسجد أو لا كفته واحدة) وهي صلاتية تنوب عنها وعن الخارجية لأن المجلس متحد والصلاتية أقوى فصارت الأولى تبعاً لها، فلو لم يسجد في الصلاة سقطتا لأن الخارجية أخذت حكم الصلاتية فسقطت تبعاً لها . أراد بالاكتفاء أن يكون بشرط اتحاد المجلس فإن تبدل مجلس التلاوة مع مجلس الصلاة فلكل سجدة . وإنما أفردها بالذكر مع دخولها تحت قوله كمن كررها في مجلس لا في مجلسين لمخالفتها لها في أنه إذا سجد للخارجية لا تكفي عن الصلاتية بخلاف ما إذا لم تكن صلاتية وسجد للأولى ثم أعادها فإن السجدة السابقة تكفي . والحاصل أنه يجب التداخل في هذه على وجه تكون الثانية مستتبعة للأولى إن لم يسجد للأولى لأن اتحاد المجلس يوجب التداخل، وكون الثانية قوية منع من جعل الأولى مستتبعة إذ استتباع الضعيف للقوي عكس المعقول ونقض للأصول فوجب التداخل على الوجه المذكور. وأشار إلى أنه لو تلاها المصلي بعدما سمعها من غيره مرة أو مراراً تكفيه سجدة واحدة. وقيد بكون الأولى تلاها خارج الصلاة لأنه لو قرأها في الصلاة أولاً ثم سلم فأعادها في مكانه ذكر في كتاب الصلاة أنه يلزمه أخرى لأن المتلوة في الصلاة لا وجود لها لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، والموجود هو الذي يستتبع دون المعدوم بخلاف ما إذا كانت الأولى خارجة فإنها باقية بعد التلاوة حكماً. وذكر في النوادر أنه لا يلزمه. ووفق الزاهد السرخسي بينهما بحمل الأولى على ما إذا أعادها بعد الكلام ، وحمل الثاني على ما إذا كان قبله ، فلو لم يسجدها في الصلاة حتى سجدها الآن قال في الأصل : أجزأه ههنا وهو محمول على ما إذا أعادها بعد السلام قبل الكلام لأنه لم يخرج عن حرمة الصلاة فكأنه كررها في الصلاة وسجد إذ لا يستقيم هذا الجواب فيما إذا أعادها بعد الكلام لأن الصلاتية قد سقطت عنه : بالكلام كذا في البدائع وصحح التوفيق في المحيط، وهذا يفيد أن الصلاتية تقضى بعد السلام قبل أن يتكلم وإن لم يأت بمنافٍ لحرمتها فينبغي أن يقيد قولهم الصلاتية لا تقضى خارجها بهذا وأن يراد بالخارج الخارج عن حرمتها .

يعلم المقتدي أن إمامه نواه في الركوع؟ قلت يمكن أن يخبره الإمام قبل أن يتكلم أو يخرج من المسجد فيأتي به قوله : (بشرط اتحاد المجلس) ذكر في النهر عن البدائع عدم الاشتراط فقال : اتحد المجلس أو اختلف وكذا قال في الدرر وإن اختلف . قال الرملي ومثل ما في البحر في غاية البيان والنهاية والزيلعي وغيرها، فظاهر ما في النهر نقلاً عن البدائع والدرر مخالف لما في البحر وغيره والظاهر أن فيه اختلافاً، وينبغي ترجيح ما في البحر تأمل ا هـ . قلت : ذكر في النهر بعد ما نقلناه عنه وهذا على إطلاقه ظاهر الرواية وفي رواية النوادر لا تكفيه الواحدة، ومنشأ الخلاف هل بالصلاة يتبدل المجلس أو لا ا.هـ. أي هل يتبدل حكماً أم لا يتبدل أصلاً كما بسطه في غاية البيان ثم قال: وأفرد هذه المسألة بالذكر مع دخولها تحت قوله كمن كررها في مجلس» إلى آخر ما ذكره أخوه هنا. وحينئذ فما في النهر مشكل لأن تعميمه أولاً ينافي ما ذكره منشأ للخلاف وما بعده وقد ذكر الخلاف الشارح الزيلعي ولكن بعد تعليله لكفاية الواحدة باتحاد المجلس كما على المؤلف ولا غبار عليه وقد ذكر في الشرنبلالية ما يفيد الجواب حيث ذكر أن قول الدرر وإن اختلف المجلس بناء على تسليم الوجه لرواية النوادر وهو أ أن المجلس يتبدل بالصلاة حكماً وإلا فعلى الظاهر فهو متحد حقيقة وحكماً، ويمكن حمل ما في النهر على هذا، وعليه فلا مخالفة بينه وبين ما في البحر وغيره ولا خلاف تأمل قوله : (ثم سلم) قال الرملي : يعني ثم سلم ولم يسجد لها فيها فلو سجد لها فيها وأعادها في مكانه لا تلزمه أخرى كما يستفاد من إطلاق قولهم كمن كررها في مجلس» وعلى

سجد أخرى وإن لم يسجد أو لا كفته واحدة كمن كررها في مجلس لا في مجلسين التلاوة حكماً. وذكر في النوادر أنه لا يلزمه. ووفق الزاهد السرخسي بينهما بحمل الأولى على ما إذا أعادها بعد الكلام ، وحمل الثاني على ما إذا كان قبله ، فلو لم يسجدها في الصلاة حتى سجدها الآن قال في الأصل : أجزأه ههنا وهو محمول على ما إذا أعادها بعد السلام قبل الكلام لأنه لم يخرج عن حرمة الصلاة فكأنه كررها في الصلاة وسجد إذ لا يستقيم هذا الجواب فيما إذا أعادها بعد الكلام لأن الصلاتية قد سقطت عنه : بالكلام كذا في البدائع وصحح التوفيق في المحيط، وهذا يفيد أن الصلاتية تقضى بعد السلام قبل أن يتكلم وإن لم يأت بمنافٍ لحرمتها فينبغي أن يقيد قولهم الصلاتية لا تقضى خارجها بهذا وأن يراد بالخارج الخارج عن حرمتها .

قوله (كمن كررها في مجلس لا في مجلسين) فإنه يكفيه واحدة في الأول دون الثاني والأصل فيه ما روي أن جبريل عليه السلام كان ينزل بالوحي فيقرأ آية السجدة على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورسول الله كان يسمع ويتلفن ثم يقرأ على أصحابه وكان لا يسجد إلا مرة واحدة، وهو مروي عن عدة من الصحابة ولأن المجلس جامع المتفرقات ولأن في إيجاب السجدة لكل تلاوة حرجاً خصوصاً للمعلمين والمتعلمين وهو منفي بالنص. قيد بسجدة التلاوة لأن الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بأن سمعه أو ذكره في مجلس واحد مراراً فيها اختلاف، فبعضهم قاسها عليها، وبعضهم منعه وأوجبها لكل مرة لأنه من حقوق العباد ولا تداخل فيها وهو جفاء له كما ورد في الحديث وقدمنا ترجيحه. وأما تشميت من عطس في مجلس واحد مراراً فأوجبه بعضهم كل مرة والصحيح أنه إن زاد على الثلاث لا يشمته لما روي عن عمر رضي الله عنه أنه قال للعاطس في مجلسه بعد الثلاث قم فانتثر فإنك مزكوم. وفي المجتبى ولا خلاف في وجوب تعظيم اسمه تعالى عند ذكره في كل مرة، وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا تلا مراراً ثم سجد وما إذا تلا وسجد ثم تلا بعده مراراً في مجلس واحد وهو تداخل في السبب دون الحكم ومعناه أن يجعل التلاوة المتعددة كتلاوة واحدة تكون الواحدة منها سبباً والباقي تبع لها وهو ألبق بالعبادات إذ السبب متى تحقق لا يجوز ترك حكمه، ولهذا يحكم بوجوبها في موضع الاحتياط حتى تبرأ ذمته بيقين والتداخل في الحكم أليق في العقوبات لأنها شرعت للزجر فهو ينزجر بواحدة فيحصل المقصود فلا حاجة إلى الثانية . والفرق بينهما أن التداخل في السبب ينوب فيه الواحدة عما قبلها وعما بعدها، وفي التداخل في الحكم لا تنوب إلا عما قبلها حتى لو زنا ثم زنا في المجلس يحد ثانياً بخلاف حد القذف إذا أقيم مرة ثم قذفه مراراً، قول البعض أن التداخل فيها في الحكم لا في السبب تلزمه أخرى ا.هـ. وفيه نظر بل الكلام فيما إذا سجد لها فيها كما يرشد إليه التعليل وعبارة الزيلعي والنهر صريحة في أنه سجد لها فيها قوله : (وهذا يفيد الخ) الإشارة إلى قوله فلو لم يسجدها في الصلاة (الخ) وقوله (وإن لم يأت بمناف) حق التعبير أن يقال ولم يأت بحذف «أن»، وقوله وإن يراد بالخارج من حرمتها» الظاهر عطفه بـ«أو»
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. He said: (And if he recited it outside prayer and prostrated, and repeated it in it) i.e., repeated its recitation in prayer (he prostrates another) because the prayer-prostration is stronger, so it cannot be subordinate to the weaker. He said: (And if he did not prostrate or not, one suffices him) and it is the prayer-prostration which takes the place of it and of the external one because the sitting is united and the prayer-prostration is stronger, so the first became subordinate to it. If he did not prostrate in prayer, both drop because the external takes the ruling of the prayer-prostration and thus drops as subordinate. He intended by 'one suffices' that it is conditioned on unity of the sitting; if the sitting of recitation changes from the sitting of prayer, then there is a prostration for each. And he singled it out for mention, although it is included under his statement 'like one who repeats it in one sitting not in two sittings', because it differs from it in that if he prostrates for the external, it does not suffice for the prayer-prostration, contrary to when there is no prayer-prostration and he prostrates for the first and then repeats it, the previous prostration suffices. The conclusion is that overlapping is necessary in this such that the second subsumes the first if he did not prostrate for the first, because unity of sitting necessitates overlapping, and the fact that the second is strong prevents making the first subsuming, since subsuming of the weak by the strong is against reason and violates principles, so overlapping is necessary in the mentioned manner. And he indicated that if the praying person recites it after hearing it from someone else once or multiple times, one prostration suffices him. And he restricted it to the first being recited outside prayer, because if he recited it in prayer first and then gave salam and repeated it in his place, it is mentioned in the Book of Prayer that another is required, because what is recited in prayer has no existence in reality or in legal consideration, and what exists is what subsumes, not the non-existent, contrary to when the first is external, for it remains after the recitation legally. And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir that it is not required. Al-Zahid al-Sarkhasi reconciled them by bearing the first upon when he repeated it after speech, and the second upon when it was before it. If he did not prostrate in prayer until he prostrated now, he said in al-Asl: it suffices him here, and it is borne upon when he repeated it after salam before speech because he has not left the sanctity of prayer, so it is as if he repeated it in prayer and prostrated, as this answer is not valid when he repeated it after speech because the prayer-prostration has dropped from him by speech. Thus in al-Bada'i' and al-Tawfiq in al-Muhit corrected this. And this indicates that the prayer-prostration is made up after salam before speaking, even if he did not do something contrary to its sanctity. Therefore, their statement 'the prayer-prostration is not made up outside it' should be restricted by this, and 'outside' should mean outside its sanctity. The follower knows that his imam intended it in ruku? I said: It is possible that the imam informs him before he speaks or leaves the mosque, so he performs it. He said: (Conditioned on unity of the sitting) It is mentioned in al-Nahr from al-Bada'i' that there is no condition; he said: whether the sitting is united or different, and likewise said in al-Durar even if differs. Al-Ramli said: and like what is in al-Bahr in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Nihaya, al-Zayla'i and others. So what is apparent from al-Nahr quoting al-Bada'i' and al-Durar contradicts what is in al-Bahr and others, and apparently there is a difference, and it is appropriate to prefer what is in al-Bahr; reflect. He said: It is mentioned in al-Nahr after what we quoted from him, and this upon its absoluteness is the apparent narration, and in the narration of al-Nawadir one does not suffice, and the source of the difference is whether prayer changes the sitting or not. i.e., whether it changes legally or does not change at all, as explained in Ghayat al-Bayan. Then he said: And he singled out this issue for mention, although it is included under his statement 'like one who repeats it in one sitting' to the end of what his brother mentioned here. Therefore, what is in al-Nahr is problematic because his generalization first contradicts what he mentioned as the source of the difference and what follows. And al-Zayla'i has mentioned the difference but after his reasoning that one suffices due to unity of sitting as the author, and there is no harm. And it is mentioned in al-Shurnublaliyya what benefits the answer, where he mentioned that the saying of al-Durar 'even if the sitting differs' is based on accepting the face of the narration of al-Nawadir, which is that the sitting changes by prayer legally, otherwise in the apparent it is united in reality and legally. And what is in al-Nahr can be borne upon this, and thus there is no contradiction between it and what is in al-Bahr and others, and no difference; reflect. He said: (Then he gave salam) Al-Ramli said: meaning he gave salam and did not prostrate in it, so if he prostrated in it and repeated it in his place, another does not become required, as is understood from the absoluteness of their statement 'like one who repeats it in one sitting' and upon... He prostrates another, and if he did not prostrate or not, one suffices him, like one who repeats it in one sitting not in two sittings, legally the recitation. And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir that it is not required. Al-Zahid al-Sarkhasi reconciled them... (then the text repeats similar content). He said: (Like one who repeats it in one sitting not in two sittings) then one suffices in the first but not in the second. The basis for this is what is narrated that Jibriel, peace be upon him, used to descend with revelation and recite the verse of prostration to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and the Messenger of Allah used to hear and [?] then recite to his companions, and he would not prostrate except once. This is narrated from several companions, and because the sitting gathers scattered things, and because requiring a prostration for each recitation would be hardship, especially for teachers and students, and hardship is negated by the text. It is restricted to the prostration of recitation, because sending blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, when hearing or mentioning it multiple times in one sitting has a difference: some analogize it to it, and some prevent it and require it each time because it is a right of the people and there is no overlapping in it, and it would be injustice to him as mentioned in the hadith, and we have presented its preference. As for saying 'Yarhamuk Allah' to one who sneezes multiple times in one sitting, some require it each time, but the correct view is that if it exceeds three, one should not say it, due to what is narrated from 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said to a sneezer in his gathering after the third: 'Get up and blow your nose, for you have a cold.' And in al-Mujtaba: There is no difference in the obligation of magnifying His name, Exalted is He, when mentioning Him each time. And he made it absolute, so it includes when he recites multiple times then prostrates, and when he recites and prostrates then recites afterwards multiple times in one sitting. And this is overlapping in the cause not in the ruling. Its meaning is to make the multiple recitations like a single recitation, one of them being the cause and the rest following it. And it is more suitable for acts of worship because once the cause is realized, it is not permissible to abandon its ruling. Therefore, it is ruled obligatory in a precautionary manner until one's obligation is definitively discharged. And overlapping in the ruling is more suitable for punishments because they are legislated for deterrence, and he is deterred by one, so the purpose is achieved, and there is no need for a second. The difference between them is that in overlapping in the cause, the one acts for what is before and after it, while in overlapping in the ruling, it only acts for what is before it, even if one commits zina then commits zina in the sitting, he is punished twice, unlike the punishment for slander if it is executed once and then he commits slander multiple times. Some say that overlapping in it is in the ruling not in the cause, so another is required. End quote. It is debatable; rather the talk is about when he prostrated in it as indicated by the reasoning, and the expressions of al-Zayla'i and al-Nahr are explicit that he prostrated in it. He said: (This indicates...) refers to his statement 'if he did not prostrate in prayer...' end. And his statement (and if he did not come with a contradiction) the correct expression is to say 'and he did not come' by dropping 'an'. And his statement 'and if 'outside' is meant from its sanctity' apparently is coordinated with 'or'.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the rulings of sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) when the same verse is recited multiple times in one sitting and across sittings, particularly in relation to prayer. The author begins by explaining the matn's ruling: if a person recites a sajdah verse outside prayer and prostrates, then recites it again inside prayer, a second prostration is required because the prayer prostration is stronger and cannot be subordinated to the weaker outside prostration. If they did not prostrate outside, or did not prostrate at all, then a single prostration (the one in prayer) suffices for both, provided the sitting (majlis) is the same. This establishes the principle of tadakhul (overlapping of prostrations) conditioned on unity of the sitting. The commentary then discusses the scenario where the first recitation was outside prayer and the second inside; here, even if the sitting is considered the same, the stronger (prayer) prostration subsumes the weaker. If the first recitation was inside prayer and the person gives salām, then recites it again in the same place, a new prostration is required because the first recitation in prayer has no legal existence after salām. A key point is that the prayer prostration can be made up after salām but before speaking, as long as one is still within the sanctity of the prayer (ḥurma al-ṣalāh). The text then delves into the condition of ittihad al-majlis (unity of the sitting), noting a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: the apparent narration (ẓāhir al-riwāya) requires unity of sitting, while a narration from al-Nawadir does not require it when the second recitation occurs after prayer, because prayer is considered to change the sitting legally. The commentator favors the view that the sitting is actually united in reality and legally, as stated in Al-Bahr, and the difference arises from whether prayer legally changes the sitting. The discussion then shifts to multiple recitations in one sitting: if one repeats the same sajdah verse multiple times in one sitting, one prostration suffices, based on the hadith of Jibrīl reciting to the Prophet (ṣallallāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam) who prostrated only once. The rationale includes hardship (ḥaraj) and the principle that the sitting gathers scattered recitations (al-majlis jāmiʿ al-mutafarriqāt). The commentary distinguishes between different types of overlapping: tadakhul in the cause (sabab) vs. tadakhul in the ruling (ḥukm). For acts of worship like sujud al-tilawah, overlapping is in the cause, meaning the multiple recitations are treated as a single cause, so one prostration suffices for all. For punishments (ʿuqūbāt), overlapping is in the ruling, meaning each offense incurs its own punishment unless a single punishment has already been executed (e.g., zinā requires a separate ḥadd for each occurrence, while qadhf after punishment does not). It also touches on related issues: sending ṣalāh on the Prophet (ṣallallāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam) multiple times in one sitting (some require repetition, the preferred view is one suffices if in one sitting), and replying to a sneeze (tasmit) – if a person sneezes repeatedly in one sitting, one should only respond up to three sneezes; beyond that, it is considered a cold. The passage concludes with a discussion on the correct interpretation of 'outside' in the phrase 'the prayer prostration is not performed outside prayer' – it means outside the sanctity (ḥurma) of prayer, not after salām before speaking.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a command for prostration.
اتحاد المجلس (ittihad al-majlis): Unity of the sitting; the condition that multiple recitations or events occur in the same physical and legal sitting for them to be treated as one.
تداخل (tadakhul): Overlapping or merging of rulings; in this context, treating multiple causes as one to avoid repeating the same obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a sajdah verse multiple times in one sitting without changing the sitting, how many prostrations are required according to the Hanafi school?
A) One prostration for each recitation.
B) One prostration for all recitations.
C) No prostration is required if recited multiple times.
D) It depends on whether the recitation is inside or outside prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one sujud al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations of a sajdah verse in the same sitting, due to tadakhul in the cause.
